<h1><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions Chapter 4 Work and Energy</span></strong></h2>
<p><span style="color: #00bdeb;">Page 145</span><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 1</span></strong><br />
Mass = m<br />
Height above the ground = h<br />
Work done = Potential energy acquired by the body = m x g x h<br />
where g is acceleration due to gravity<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 2</span></strong><br />
SI unit of work is Joule (J).<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 3</span></strong><br />
Work is a scalar quantity.<br />
Work, as a physical quantity, requires only magnitude to be represented. Hence, it is scalar quantity.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 4</span></strong><br />
When a force of 1 newton moves a body through a distance of 1 metre in its own direction, then the work done is known as 1 joule.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 5</span></strong><br />
The condition for a force to do work on a body is that it should produce motion in the body.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 6</span></strong><br />
Energy is a scalar quantity. It has only magnitude but no direction.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 7</span></strong><br />
a)Unit of work is joule.<br />
b) Unit of energy is joule.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 8</span></strong><br />
The work done against gravity is zero when a body is moved horizontally along a frictionless surface because force of gravity acts perpendicular to the direction of motion.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 9</span></strong><br />
Kinetic energy will become four times when the speed is doubled because kinetic<br />
energy is directly proportional to square of speed of the body<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8752/16745056427_92c3afa2f4_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-Q9" width="114" height="29" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 10</span></strong><br />
Mass = m<br />
Velocity = v<br />

energy will become one-fourth when the speed is halved because kinetic energy<br />

b) Square of the velocity of the body, v<sup>2</sup><br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 15</span></strong><br />
a) Both kinetic and potential energy<br />
b) Both kinetic and potential energy<br />
c) Only kinetic energy<br />
d) Only potential energy<br />
e) Only potential energy<br />
Note: In all the above cases we take ground as reference level where potential energy is zero.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 16</span></strong><br />

Height of body A = h<br />
Height of body B = 2h<br />
Potential energy for body A, PE<sub>A</sub> = m x g x h<br />
Potential energy for body B, PE<sub>B</sub> = m x g x 2h<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 18</span></strong><br />
Potential energy is a scalar quantity as it has magnitude only and it does not require any specification of direction.<br />

Height = 5 m<br />
g = 9.8 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />

Work done is equal to PE acquired by the body.<br />

= 1 x 9.8 x 1 = 9.8 J<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 24</span></strong><br />
The work done by a force on a body depends on two factors<br />
a) magnitude of force<br />
b) distance through which the body moves<br />
Work done is directly proportional to the force applied and the distance through which the body moves.<br />
W = F x s<br />
where W is work done, F is force applied and s is distance through which the body moves.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 25</span></strong><br />
Yes, it is possible that a force is acting on a body but still work done is zero. For example, in the case of a man pushing a wall, the work done is zero despite of non-zero force, sin ce there is no displacement of the wall.</p>
<p><span style="color: #00bdeb;">Page 146</span><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 26</span></strong><br />
a) Work done by force applied by the boy is positive because this force is in the direction of motion of the body.<br />
b) Work done by the gravitational force is negative because this force is against the direction of motion of the body.<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 29</span></strong><br />
(a) Positive work: Work done by the force applied by a person on a ball that is thrown upwards.<br />
(b) Negative work: Work done by gravitational force of earth on a ball thrown upwards.<br />
(c) Zero work: Work done by gravitational force of earth on a box that is sliding horizontally on the ground.<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 33</span></strong><br />
Mass of body = 2 kg<br />
Initial velocity u = 0<br />
Time taken = 2 s<br />
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 10 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Final velocity v<br />
Using first equation of motion<br />
v = u + gt = 0 + 10 x 2 = 20 m/s<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7604/16766202379_0ea099e778_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-Q33" width="257" height="177" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 34</span></strong><br />
Mass of scooter + scooterist = 150 kg<br />
Initial velocity u = 10 m/s<br />
Final velocity v = 5 m/s<br />
Retardation = a<br />
Distance covered= s<br />
Using third equation of motion<br />
v<sup>2</sup> &#8211; u<sup>2</sup> = 2as<br />
5<sup>2</sup> &#8211; 10<sup>2</sup> = 2as<br />
as = &#8211;<sub>75/2</sub> &#8212;&#8212;(i)<br />
Work done W = F x s<br />
But F = m x a<br />
So, W= m x a x s<br />
Put the value of &#8216;as&#8217; from eq(i)<br />
W = 150 x (-75/2) = -5625 J<br />
Neagtive sign implies that force of brakes acts opposite to the direction of motion.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 35</span></strong><br />
Mass of rock = 10 kg<br />
Height of ladder, h = 5 m<br />
Initial velocity of rock, u = 0<br />
Final velocity v<br />
g = 10 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
using third equation of motion<br />
v<sup>2</sup> &#8211; u<sup>2</sup> = 2gh<br />
v<sup>2</sup> &#8211; 0<sup>2</sup> = 2 x 10 x 5<br />
v = 10 m/s<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8689/16951461341_5fdb380507_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-Q35" width="259" height="187" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 36</span></strong><br />
Mass of car = 1000 kg<br />
Initial velocity u = 20 m/s<br />
Final velocity v = 10 m/s<br />
Retardation = a<br />
Distance covered = s<br />
Using third equation of motion<br />
v<sup>2</sup> -u<sup>2</sup> = 2as<br />
10<sup>2</sup>&#8211; 20<sup>2</sup> = 2as<br />
as = -150 &#8212;&#8212;(i)<br />
Work done W = F x s<br />
But F = m x a<br />
So, W= m x a x s<br />
Put the value of &#8216;as&#8217; from equation (i)<br />
W = 1000 x -150 = -150000 = -150 kJ Neagtive sign implies that force of brakes acts opposite to the direction of motion.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 37</span></strong><br />
Height , h= 10 m<br />
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 10 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
i) Work done, W = m x g x h = 100 x 10 x 10 = 10000 = 10 kJ<br />
ii) Potential energy of the body = work done = 10 kJ<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 38</span></strong><br />
Height, h = 100 m<br />
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 9.8m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Work done by the boy, W = m x g x h = 50 x 9.8 x 100 = 49000 J = 49 kJ<br />
Potential energy gained by the boy = work done by the boy = 49 kJ<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 39</span></strong><br />
Work done by a force applied on a body is<br />
i) positive when the force acts in the direction of motion of the body.<br />
ii) negative when the force acts in the direction opposite to the direction of motion of the body.<br />
iii) zero when the force acts at right angle to the direction of motion of the body.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 40</span></strong><br />
Mass of the box, m = 150 kg<br />
PE = 7350 J<br />
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 9.8m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
PE = m x g x h<br />
7350 = 150 x 9.8 x h<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 41</span></strong><br />
Mass of the body, m = 2 kg<br />
Initial velocity, u = 20 m/s<br />
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 10 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Height reached = h<br />
Time, t = 2 s<br />
Using second equation of motion<br />
PE after 2 s = m x g x h = 2 x 10 x 20 = 400 J<br />

Distance, s = 1 m<br />
Work done W = F x s = 1 x 1 = 1 J<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 43</span></strong><br />
Force, F = 2.5 x 10<sup>10</sup> N<br />
Velocity, v = 5 m/s<br />
Time, t = 2 minutes = 120 s<br />
Distance, s = v x t = 5 x 120 = 600 m<br />
Work done, W = F x s = 2.5 x 10<sup>10</sup> x 600 = 15 x 10<sup>12</sup> J<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 44</span></strong><br />
A stretched rubber band is an example of a body possessing energy while it is not in motion. The rubber band contains potential energy due to the change in its shape or configuration.<br />

ii)height to which the body is lifted, h<br />
iii)acceleration due to gravity, g<br />
b)<br />
i.A moving cricket ball has kinetic energy<br />
ii.A stretched rubber band has potential energy<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 46</span></strong><br />
Two examples where a body possesses both kinetic energy as well as potential energy are<br />
i)a man climbing up a hill<br />
ii)a flying aeroplane<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 51</span></strong><br />
Mass, m = 200 kg<br />
Height, h = 2 m<br />
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 9.8 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
i) Potential energy = m x g x h = 200 x 9.8 x 2 = 3920 J<br />
ii) Work done is against gravity = Potential energy gained by the weights, therefore<br />
Work done W = m x g x h = 200 x 9.8 x 2 = 3920 J<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 52</span></strong><br />
(a) Work is done when a force applied on a body produces motion in it.<br />
Formula for work done:<br />
W = F x s<br />
where W is the work done<br />
F is force applied<br />
S is the displacement of the body in the direction of force<br />
(b) Mass of the person, m = 50 kg<br />
Height of tower, h = 72 m<br />
Acceleration due to gravity = 9.8 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Work done W = m x g x h<br />
= 50 x 9.8 x 72 = 35280 J<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 53</span></strong><br />
(a) Work is said to be done when the force applied on a body produces motion in it.<br />
Work done by a body in moving up is given by<br />
W = m x g x h<br />
where W is the work done against the gravity<br />
m = mass of the body<br />
g = acceleration due to gravity<br />
h = height through which the body is lifted above the ground<br />
(b) Force, F = 2 N<br />
Distance, s = 10 cm = 0.1 m<br />
Work done W = F x s = 2 x 0.1 = 0.2 J<br />

(b) Force, F = 50 N<br />
Distance, s = 4 m<br />
Angle between direction of force and direction of motion,<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 55</span></strong><br />
(a) Energy is the ability to do work. SI unit of energy is Joule.<br />
(b) Various forms of energy are:<br />
1. Kinetic energy<br />
2. Potential energy<br />
3. Chemical energy<br />
4. Heat energy<br />
5. Light energy<br />
6. Sound energy<br />
7. Electrical energy<br />
8. Nuclear energy<br />
(c) Let masses of bodies be m<br />
Velocity of one body, v<sub>1</sub>= v<br />
Velocity of another body, v<sub>2</sub> = 2v<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7282/16766202229_5ab8aac870_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-Q55" width="404" height="500" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 56</span></strong><br />
(a) The energy of a body due to its motion is called kinetic energy<br />
(b) When the velocity becomes zero, the kinetic energy also becomes zero since kinetic energy is directly proportional to square of the velocity.<br />
(c)<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8701/16952422835_c6168f89f8_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-Q56" width="791" height="282" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 57</span></strong><br />
(a) The energy of a body due to its position or change in its shape is known as its potential energy. E.g. a stretched rubber has potential energy due to change in its shape and water in the overhead tank has potential energy due to its height above the ground.<br />
PE = m x g x h<br />
where, PE is the potential energy of the body,<br />
m is the mass of the body,<br />
g is the acceleration due to gravity,<br />
h is the height above the surface ofearth.<br />
(b) Kinetic energy of a body is due to motion of the body while potential energy is due to position or change in shape of the body.<br />
Kinetic energy is zero for a still body, while potential energy may or may not be zero for a still body.<br />
Kinetic energy of a body is directly proportional to its speed while potential energy is directly proportional to the height to which the body is above the ground.<br />
(c) Mass of ball, m = 0.5 kg<br />
Speed v<sub>1</sub> = 5 m/s<br />
Speed v<sub>2</sub> = 3 m/s<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7600/16330039854_d97158004d_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-Q57" width="368" height="147" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 58</span></strong><br />
(a) The potential energy due to the position of the body above the ground is gravitational potential energy and the potential energy due to change in shape and size of the body is elastic potential energy. E.g. a stretched rubber has elastic potential energy due to change in its shape while water in the overhead tank has gravitational potential energy due to its height above the ground.<br />
(b) Work done, W = 784 J<br />
Mass, m = 20 kg<br />
g = 9.8 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
W = m x g x h<br />
784 = 20 x 9.8 x h<br />

<p><span style="color: #00bdeb;">Page 148</span><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 71</span></strong><br />
Work done is more on the bicycle because the truck does not move at all and the bicycle moves through a certain distance. And work is said to be done only when applied force produces motion in the body.<br />
<span style="color: #00bdeb;">Page 149</span><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 72</span></strong><br />
The work done will decrease as the angle between the direction of force and direction of motion is increased gradually because<br />

Work done will be maximum when angle between the direction of force and direction of motion is 0<sup>o</sup> because<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 75</span></strong><br />
The work done is zero because the gravitational force acts along the radius of the circular path, at right angles i.e. 90<sup>o</sup> to the motion of satellite.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 76</span></strong><br />
Weight of man = Mg = 800 N<br />
Weight of package = mg = 200 N<br />
Total weight of man and package = Mg + mg = (M+m)g = 1000 N<br />
Height of the summit, h = 1200 m<br />
i) Work done = (M+m) x g x h = 1000 x 1200 = 12 x 10<sup>5</sup> J<br />
ii) Potential energy of the package = m x g x h = 200 x 1200 = 2.4 x 10<sup>5</sup> J<br />

the ball is thrown inside the moving bus.<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 30</span></strong><br />
Weight of the car = 20000 N= 20 kN<br />
Speed = 8 m/s<br />
Distance s= 120 m<br />
Time = 100 s<br />
a)Work done W = f x s = 20 x 120 = 2400 kJ<br />
b) Power<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7633/16951461751_c1776f69c4_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-A-Q30" width="273" height="127" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 31</span></strong><br />
a)The change of one form of energy into another form of energy is known as transformation of energy, e.g. in a cell chemical energy is transformed into<br />
electrical energy<br />
b) a. When a ball is thrown upwards its kinetic energy gradually converts into potential energy and potential energy<br />
becomes maximum at the maximum height attained by the ball<br />
b. When a stone is dropped from the roof of the building its potential energy gradually converts into kinetic energy and kinetic energy becomes maximum when the stone is just above the ground<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 32</span></strong><br />
a) Law of conservation of energy states that whenever energy changes from one form to another form, the total amount of energy remains constant. Energy can<br />
never be created nor destroyed, it transforms from one form to another. For example, when electrical energy is converted into light energy in an electric<br />
bulb, then some energy is wasted as heat during conversion but the total energy remains the same.<br />
b) Initially the pendulum is at rest. The bob is pulled to one side to position B to give it potential energy due to higher position of B and then released, the bob<br />
starts swinging<br />
i. When the bob is at position B, it has potential energy but no kinetic energy<br />
ii. As the bob starts moving down from position B to A, its potential energy starts decreasing and kinetic energy starts increasing<br />
iii. When the bob is at position A, it has maximum kinetic energy and zero potential energy<br />
iv. As the bob starts moving down from position A to C, its kinetic energy starts decreasing and potential energy starts increasing<br />
v. On reaching the extreme position C, the bob stops for a very small instant of time and bob maximum potential energy and zero kinetic energy.<br />
Therefore at extreme positions B and C bob has only potential energy and at A it has only kinetic energy and at other intermediate positions bob has both kinetic<br />
and potential energy. Thus the total energy of the pendulum is same for any instant of time (conserved)<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8732/16745056667_5d6f800122_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-A-Q32" width="340" height="278" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 33</span></strong><br />
a) The unit kWh stands for kilowatt-hour. One kilowatt-hour is the amount of electrical energy consumed when an electrical appliance having power of 1 kilowatt is used for 1 hour. It represents the amount of electrical energy consumed in 1 hour.<br />
b) Power = 1000 W = 1 kW<br />
Time = 60 minutes = 1 hour<br />
Energy(kWh) = 1 x 1 = 1 kWh<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 34</span></strong><br />
a) 1 kilowatt-hour = 1 kW for 1 hour = 1000 W for 1 hour<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8724/16330040434_2d01c1c5f7_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-A-Q34" width="284" height="220" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 35</span></strong><br />
a) Power is the rate of doing work.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8716/16951098642_a5be1e14f2_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter4-work-and-energy-A-Q35" width="270" height="226" /><br />
<span style="color: #00bdeb;">Page 164</span><br />

<h2><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 5 Why Do We Fall Ill ?</span></strong></h2>
<p><strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">Text Book Solutions &#8211; P.S.Verma and V.K.Agarwal &#8211; Biology</span></strong></p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">CBSE Class 9 Chapter 5 Why Do We Fall Ill ?</span></strong></p>
<p><a class="button-blue" title="LearnCBSE Forum - Post and Discuss your Queries" href="http://ask.learncbse.in/"> Share Queries and Discuss your Views and Ideas &#8211; <strong>LearnCBSE Forum</strong></a></p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page No &#8211; 300.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
Healthy:<br />
1. It is a state of complete physical, mental and social well being.<br />
2. A healthy person will be disease free.<br />
Disease Free:<br />
1. It is a state of absence of discomfort or derangement in any part of body.<br />
2. A disease free person can be healthy or unhealthy.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 2:</span><br />
There are many types of health problems that can possibly arise after disaster such as victims of disaster might suffer from lack of nourishment due to inadequate food.<br />
The immediate health problems after disaster includes suffering of trapped people, people may suffer from fractures, burns and asthma due to dust particles arising from buildings. Contaminated water can also cause other health issues.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 3</span><br />
The provisions made by local authorities was to allocate funds and guide investments, encourage research, develop human resources through training and other capacity-building efforts, promote water quality monitoring, provide guidelines for various programmes and ensure the implementation of the water supply programmes.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 4</span><br />
There are many provisions provided by local authorities for solid waste management. These are followings:<br />
(i) Sweeping<br />
(ii) Collection<br />
(iii) Vermi-composting<br />
(iv) Recycling system<br />
(v) Transportation system<br />
(vi) Power generation and<br />
(vii) Dumping<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 5:</span><br />
Symptoms:<br />
1. They indicate the presence of disease.<br />
2. Symptoms are a collective indication of a number of diseases in a particular part or organ.<br />
Signs:<br />
1. They provide information about the presence of particular disease.<br />
2. They are distinct for different diseases.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 6:</span><br />
Casual organisms of the following diseases:<br />
(i) Tuberculosis &#8211; Mycobacterium tuberculosis<br />
(ii) Kala-azar &#8211; Leishmania (protozoa)<br />
(iii) Malaria &#8211; Plasmodium<br />
(iv) Measles &#8211; Virus<br />
(v) Athlete&#8217;s foot &#8211; Fungi<br />
(vi) Cholera &#8211; Vibrio Cholerae<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 7:</span><br />
Two means of physical contacts by which AIDS does not spread are handshakes and hugs.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 8</span><br />
A vector is a carrier (mosquito, tick) that takes the disease from an infected individual to an uninfected individual. They do not have the disease themselves; they carry the infected agent such as blood. A reservoir is anything (person, animal, arthropod, plant, soil or substance) in which a disease lives and can multiply. The disease needs the reservoir in order to survive. A vector must be living but a reservoir can be a living or a non living thing such as soil or water. Vectors or carriers are not pathogenic but are simply transmitters.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 9</span><br />
Organ Specific Manifestation- These are the diseases caused in the same organ or organ system as the point of entry of the microbe. E.g. Tuberculosis which enters through the nose and affects the lungs. (Both are organs of the respiratory system)<br />
Tissue Specific Manifestation- These are the diseases caused in a different organ as the point of entry. E.g. Japanese Encephalitis which enters through the blood but affects the brain.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 10</span><br />
There are many possible areas, organs and tissues within our body where microbes may reside. However the severity of disease symptoms depends on the number of microbes in the body. For example, if the number of microbes is very small, then the symptoms of disease will be minor or unnoticed. However, if the numbers are large, the disease can be severe enough to be life-risking.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 11</span><br />
Infection of HIV is found to have multiple dimensional effects. In case of HIV infection, the virus goes to immune system and ultimately damages its function. Thus many symptoms of HIV &#8211; AIDS infection are due to the fact that patients body no longer fight off many minor infections that he/she faces everyday.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 12</span><br />
There are two ways to treat an infectious disease. One is to reduce the effects of the disease and the other way is to kill the cause of the disease.<br />
For example, we can take the medicines that bring down the fever, reduce pain or loose motions. We can take bed rest so that we can converse our energy. This exercise will enable us to focus on the healing. However it will not make the pathogen to go away, so the disease will not be cured. For that we have to kill the microbe.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 13</span><br />
Prevention is better than cure as a disease always cause some damage to the body, loss of working days, besides expenditure on medication. The important precautions for preventing occurrence of diseases include (i) hygienic environment; (ii) personal hygiene; (iii) proper nutrition; (iv) clean food; (v) clean water; (vi) regular exercise and (vii) adequate relaxation. Everybody should also be aware of diseases and their mode of spreading (epidemic). A regular medical checkup is also earnestly required to stay healthy.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 14</span><br />
Vaccines help a body&#8217;s immune system prepare in advance to fight infectious illnesses and potentially deadly diseases caused by infectious agents or their by-products. Vaccines work on the principle of immunization. During vaccination, when the immune system first encounters an infectious microbe, it responds against it and then remembers it specifically. So the next time that particular microbe, or its close relatives enter the body, the immune system responds with greater vigour. This eliminates the infection even more quickly than the first occurrence of the disease.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 15</span><br />
Three diseases caused by Bacteria are: Tuberculosis (T.B.), Cholera and Typhoid.<br />
Three diseases caused by Virus are: &#8211; Influenza, Jaundice and AIDS.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 16</span><br />
The diarrhoea spreads through infection by contaminated food, water, drinks, hands, clothes etc. During diarrhoea frequent loose motions and vomiting leads to dehydration.<br />
To control the dehydration during diarrhoea; Saline drip may be given intravenously to maintain fluid and electrolytes in the body. Alternatively oral rehydration Solution (ORS) may be given to the patient periodically.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 17</span><br />
Stagnant water (of pools, ponds) in the locality is the habitat of larvae of many types of mosquitoes and they are the vector of a disease, called malaria.<br />
Doctor confirms malaria if the patients have following symptoms: headache, nausea, muscular pain and high fever. Doctor also checks the presence of malarial parasite in the human body by blood test.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 18</span><br />
Methods of prevention of Malaria:<br />
(i) Wire-gauze should be used on doors and windows of houses to prevent entry of mosquitoes.<br />
(ii) One should sleep under mosquito nets.<br />
(iii) Insect-repellents should be used to prevent mosquito-bite.<br />
(iv) Mosquito larvae can be killed by sprinkling kerosene oil on large-sized water bodies.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 19</span><br />
The person having AIDS lose the power of fighting any infection. The disease of AIDS is caused by retrovirus (a RNA virus) known as Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV).<br />
AIDS disease spreads among human beings in the following ways:<br />
(i) The AIDS usually spreads through unprotected sexual contacts with an infected person carrying AIDS virus.<br />
(ii) It also spreads through the transfusion of blood contaminated with an AIDS virus.<br />
(iii) It also spreads through the use of infected needles for injections.<br />
(iv) An AIDS infected mother can transmit the virus to her child during pregnancy or during birth.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 20</span><br />
Diarrhoea is an abnormally frequent discharge of semisolid or fluid faeces. It spreads through infection by contaminated food, water, drinks, hands, clothes, bed sheets and utensils.<br />
Symptoms of Diarrhoea:<br />
(i) Decreased appetite, nausea, vomiting and abdominal cramps.<br />
(ii) There may be blood and mucus in the stools.<br />
Prevention:<br />
(i) Eatables should be covered to prevent their contamination.<br />
(ii) Fruits and vegetable should be properly washed before use.<br />
(iii) Stale food should not be consumed.<br />
Control:<br />
(i) Complete bed rest should be ensured till the illness is fully controlled.<br />
(ii) For treating diarrhoea anti-microbial drugs and anti-diarrhoea agents should be used.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 21</span><br />
In rabies, the patient feels restless, does excessive salivation, has a choking feeling and finds difficulty in the intake of even liquid food. Since patient develops fear of water, the disease is called hydrophobia.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 22</span><br />
Pulse Polio Programme &#8211; Pulse polio immunization programme forms the largest single day public health project. Pulse means a dose of a substance (here polio vaccine) especially when applied for a short period of time. It was conducted for the first time in 1995. The program uses oral polio vaccine or OPV. As per the National Immunization Schedule (NIS), a dose of 3 drops is given orally to the child, i.e. one dose each at 1.5, 2.5 and 3.5 month&#8217;s age. Finally a booster dose is given at the age of 1.5 years. After oral administration, virus particles in the vaccine begin to live in the intestine of the human body and multiply. It leads to production of protective molecules in the intestine and the blood.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 1</span><br />
Human beings live in societies. Our social environment therefore plays an important role in our individual health. In villages, towns or cities, our physical environment is decided by our social environment. For example &#8211; if there are heaps of garbage and trash littered here and there, or if there is open drain water lying stagnant around where we live, the possibility of poor health increases. So, public cleanliness is an important contribution to an individual&#8217;s health.<br />
Some other community issues that influence health are:<br />
Community issues like child marriage can affect the health of the girl the baby born to an underage girl.<br />
Lack of education of the community to sex related issues can also cause sexually transmitted diseases.<br />
Bad treatment with the underprivileged sections of the society can also cause mental problems.<br />
Social equality and harmonious relationships among our population are necessary for the individual health. Thus, we see that there is an overlap of personal and community issues for health.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 2</span><br />
Infectious diseases spread from one infected person to other normal person by various methods.<br />
(a) Air-borne diseases &#8211; For example: common cold, pneumonia and tuberculosis. Such disease causing microbes are spread throughout the air. The transmission of these microbes occurs through the little droplets coughed out by an infected person who sneezes or coughs. A person in the vicinity of such a person can inhale these disease causing microbes and may become infected.<br />
(b)Water-borne diseases &#8211; For example: Cholera, Infectious diseases can also spread through water. These occur when a stool from someone suffering from an infectious gut disease, such as cholera or amoebiasis, gets mixed with the drinking water used by people living nearby. The cholera-infested bacteria can enter new hosts through the water they drink and can cause disease in them.<br />
(c) Sexually-transmitted diseases &#8211; For example: Syphilis and AIDS. Both of these pathogens are transmitted by sexual contact from one partner to the other. However, such sexually transmitted diseases are not spread by casual physical contact.<br />
(e) Formite borne diseases &#8211; Articles coming in contact with the patients act as sources of infection. For example: door handles, taps, garments, utensils, crockery, etc.<br />
(f) Spread of disease through vectors &#8211; Many animals which live with us may carry diseases. These animals can transfer infecting agents from a sick person to another potential host. Thus, these animals act as intermediaries or vectors. For example &#8211; female Anopheles mosquitos are vectors of disease, malaria.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 3</span><br />
General ways of preventing infection are:<br />
Public hygiene is one basic key to the prevention of infectious diseases.<br />
In the method of prevention of diseases, following practices are adopted:<br />
(i) To avoid exposure to air-borne microbes, adopt living conditions that are not overcrowded.<br />
(ii) To prevent exposure to water-borne microbes, safe drinking water should be provided.<br />
(iii) To avoid vector-borne infections, we can provide clean environment as it would not allow mosquito breeding.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 4</span><br />
Principle of Treatment:<br />
There are two ways to treat an infectious disease. One is to reduce the effects of the disease and the other way is to kill the cause of the disease. For the first requirement, we can provide treatments that will reduce the symptoms. The symptoms are usually a result of inflammation. For example, we can take medicines that bring down fever, reduce pain or loose motions. We can take bed rest so that we can converse our energy.<br />
However such a kind of symptom-directed treatment by itself is inadequate. Since it will not make the pathogen go away, so the disease will not be cured. For that we have to kill the microbe itself.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 5</span><br />
(a) AIDS &#8211; AIDS stands for Acquired Immuno Deficiency Syndrome. It is a fatal disease. The disease of AIDS is caused by retrovirus (a RNA virus) known as Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV). AIDS virus attacks white blood cells (WBCs) or lymphocytes of human beings and weakens the human body&#8217;s immunity or self-defence mechanism.<br />
Some important symptoms of AIDS are: Swollen lymph nodes, regular fever, sweating at night and weight loss. Its virus also cause severe damage to brain and may lead to loss of memory, ability to speak and of clear thinking.<br />
(b) Malaria &#8211; Malaria is caused by a protozoan parasite Plasmodium. This disease spreads through the bite of an insect vector &#8211; the female Anopheles mosquito which feeds on human blood. Male Anopheles mosquito feeds upon plant juice. Main symptoms of malaria include headache, nausea, muscular pain and high fever. Malarial attack consists of three stages:<br />
(i) Cold stage, feeling of extreme cold and shivers.<br />
(ii) Hot stage, high fever, faster respiration and heart beat.<br />
(iii) Sweating stage, due to profuse sweating, temperature of the body goes down to normal.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 6</span><br />
Few diseases caused by bacteria are:<br />
(i) Tuberculosis (T.B.) &#8211; T.B. is an infectious disease which is communicated from one person to another directly or indirectly. It is caused by the bacterium called Mycobacterium tuberculosis. T.B. can affect all parts of the body such as lungs, lymph glands, bones, intestine etc.<br />
(ii) Cholera &#8211; Cholera is an acutely infectious, fatal disease and is more common during overcrowded fairs, festivals and after floods. Cholera is caused by the bacterium Vibrio Cholerae. It is transmitted by flies, contaminated water and food.<br />
(iii) Typhoid &#8211; Typhoid is most common communicable disease in India. Typhoid fever is common in humans of the age 1to 15 years age group. Typhoid is caused by a rod-shaped and motile bacterium, called Salmonella typhi which is commonly found in the intestine of human beings. Human infection is direct.<br />
(iv) Diarrhoea &#8211; Diarrhoea is an abnormally frequent discharge of semisolid or fluid faeces. The diarrhoea spreads through infection by contaminated food, water, drinks, hands, clothes, etc. The causative agents of diarrhoea are mainly bacteria such as Escherichia coli, Clostridium botulinum, Shigella dysentiriae, Campylobacter jejuri and Salmonella.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 7</span><br />
Important viral diseases of human beings are:<br />
(i) Influenza &#8211; Influenza is commonly called flu. It is caused by an influenza virus (Myxovirus influenza). There exist three types of influenza viruses &#8211; A, B and C. A and B types of influenza viruses are important because these are responsible for causing of disease epidemics throughout the world. The inhaled virus attacks the epithelial cells in the mucous membrane of nose, throat and upper respiratory tract. Influenza is spread mainly from person to person contact and by droplet infection via sneezing, coughing and talking.<br />
(ii) Jaundice &#8211; Jaundice or hepatitis is the disease of liver. Since liver is a very important organ in the body, so its inflammation due to jaundice affects digestion adversely. Jaundice is caused by viral infection. The types of hepatitis are: Hepatitis A, Hepatitis B, Hepatitis C, Hepatitis D, Hepatitis E or Hepatitis G. Except for type B which is a DNA virus, all the other are RNA viruses. Hepatitis is spread mostly by food and water contaminated with hepatitis virus.<br />
(iii) AIDS &#8211; AIDS stands for Acquired Immuno Deficiency Syndrome. It is a fatal disease. The disease of AIDS is caused by retrovirus (a RNA virus) known as Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV). AIDS virus attacks white blood cells (WBCs) or lymphocytes of human beings and weakens the human body&#8217;s immunity or self-defence mechanism. AIDS becomes prone to many other infections or diseases.<br />
(iv) Polio &#8211; Poliomyelitis or polio is a disease of the nervous system caused by one of the smallest known virus, called polio virus. The virus enters the body through the food and water and reaches the intestine and from there it enters the CNS or central nervous system via blood stream and lymphatic systems. Children between the age of 6 months to 3 years are most prone to polio infection. Polio is transmitted among children by the faeco-oral route and through the direct contact, dirty hands, contaminated food or milk and flies.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 8</span><br />
(a) Tuberculosis &#8211; T.B. is an infectious disease which is communicated from one person to another directly or indirectly. It is caused by the bacterium called Mycobacterium tuberculosis. T.B. can affect all parts of the body such as lungs, lymph glands, bones, intestine etc. The incubation period of T.B. includes a few weeks to a few years.<br />
The patient of tuberculosis feels sick and weak. There is a loss of appetite and weight. Typical fever pattern and night sweats are also common.<br />
(b) Polio &#8211; Poliomyelitis or polio is a disease of the nervous system caused by one of the smallest known virus, called polio virus. The virus enters the body through the food and water and reaches the intestine and from there it enters the CNS or central nervous system via blood stream and lymphatic systems. Children between the age of 6 months to 3 years are most prone to polio infection. Polio is transmitted among children by the faeco-oral route and through the direct contact, dirty hands, contaminated food or milk and flies.<br />
The early symptoms of the polio disease are sore throat and headache.</p>

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 41</span></strong><br />
Vacuum means empty space, region with no matter particles. Sound cannot travel through vacuum because vacuum has no molecules which can vibrate and carry sound waves.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 42</span></strong><br />
The maximum displacement of the particles of the medium from their original undisturbed positions, when a wave passes through the medium, is called amplitude (A) of the wave.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8714/16766454979_b14e3f585d_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q42" width="514" height="146" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 43</span></strong><br />
(a) A wave in which the particles of the medium vibrate back and forth in the &#8216;same direction&#8217;, in which the wave is moving, is called a longitudinal wave. These<br />
waves can be produced in all the three media: solids, liquids and gases. A wave in which the particles of the medium vibrate up and down, &#8216;at right angles&#8217;<br />
to the direction in which the wave is moving, is called a transverse wave. It can be produced in solids and liquids but not in gases.<br />
(b) Sound is a longitudinal wave.<br />

The time required to produce one complete wave (or cycle) is called time-period of the wave.<br />
The time taken to complete one vibration is called time-period.<br />
Relation between time-period and frequency of a wave is:<br />

<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8718/16765193320_49c39ab729_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q58" width="288" height="177" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 59</span></strong><br />
A compression is that part of a longitudinal wave in which the particles of the medium are closer to one another than they normally are, and there is a momentary reduction in volume of the medium. It is a region of high pressure.<br />
A rarefaction is that part of a longitudinal wave in which the particles of the medium are farther apart than normal, and there is a momentary increase in the volume of the medium. It is a region of low pressure.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8708/16951719541_619c69860c_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q59" width="371" height="179" /></p>
<p><span style="color: #3366ff;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Class 10 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:187</strong></span></p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 60</span></strong><br />
(a) Sound is that form of energy which makes us hear. Sound waves are longitudinal waves in air.<br />
(b) Sound cannot travel through vacuum. This can be shown by the following experiment:<br />
(i) A ringing electric bell is placed inside an air tight glass jar containing air. We can hear the sound of ringing bell clearly. Thus, when air is present as medium in the bell jar, sound can travel through it and reach our ears.<br />
(ii) The bell jar containing ringing bell is placed over the plate of a vacuum pump. Air is gradually removed from the bell jar by switching on the vacuum pump. As more and more air is removed from the bell jar, the sound of ringing bell becomes fainter and fainter. And when all the air is removed from the bell jar, no sound can be heard at all. Thus, when vacuum is created in the bell jar, then the sound of ringing bell placed inside it cannot be heard.<br />
This shows that sound cannot travel through vacuum.<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7603/16745309977_b1eee0651e_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q60" width="366" height="246" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 61</span></strong><br />
(a) Sound is produced when an object vibrates. For example, the sound of our voice is produced by the vibrations of two vocal cords in our throat caused by air coming from the lungs.<br />
(b) When an object vibrates (and makes sound), then the air layers around it also start vibrating in exactly the same way and carry sound waves from the sound producing object to our ears.<br />
Suppose a tuning fork is vibrating and producing sound waves in air. Since the prongs of the tuning fork are vibrating, the individual layers of air are also vibrating. Sound travels in the form of longitudinal waves in which the back and forth vibrations of the air layers are in the same direction as the movement of sound wave.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8748/16332589873_b12313f0e6_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q61" width="493" height="169" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 62</span></strong><br />
(a) If the air is gradually pumped out of the glass vessel, no sound of the electric bell can be heard because vacuum is created in the vessel and there are no air molecules to carry sound vibrations.<br />
(b) Sound cannot be heard on the surface of moon because there is no air on the moon to carry the sound waves.<br />
Astronauts talk to one another on the surface of moon through wireless sets using radio waves. This is because radio waves can travel even through vacuum though sound waves cannot travel through vacuum.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 63</span></strong><br />
(a) The number of vibrations per second is called frequency.<br />
The minimum distance in which a sound wave repeats itself is called its wavelength.<br />
The distance travelled by a wave in one second is called velocity of wave.<br />
Relation between velocity, frequency and wavelength of a wave:<br />
Velocity of wave= frequency x wavelength<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7646/16926731046_0aecbcdb80_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q63" width="306" height="201" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 64</span></strong><br />
(a) A wave in which the particles of the medium vibrate back and forth in the &#8216;same direction&#8217;, in which the wave is moving, is called a longitudinal wave. These waves can be produced in all the three media: solids, liquids and gases.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8728/16951719391_67b9e6c5cc_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q64" width="761" height="312" /><br />
(b) Longitudinal waves:<br />
(i) The waves which travel along a spring when it is pushed and pulled at one end.<br />
(ii) Sound waves in air Transverse waves:<br />
(i) The waves produced by moving one end of a long spring up and down rapidly, while other end is fixed.<br />
(ii) The water waves or ripples formed on the surface of water in a pond.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 65</span></strong><br />
(a) A compression is that part of a longitudinal wave in which the particles of the medium are closer to one another than they normally are, and there is a momentary reduction in volume of the medium.<br />
A rarefaction is that part of a longitudinal wave in which the particles of the medium are farther apart than normal, and there is a momentary increase in the volume of the medium.<br />
Longitudinal waves consist of compressions and rarefactions.<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7594/16745309747_d888e88c4b_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q65" width="240" height="121" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 66</span></strong><br />
(a) The &#8216;elevation&#8217; or &#8216;hump&#8217; in a transverse wave is called crest. It is that part of the transverse wave which is above the line of zero disturbance of the medium. The &#8216;depression&#8217; or &#8216;hollow&#8217; in a transverse wave is called trough. It is that part of the transverse wave which is below the line of zero disturbance of medium. A ransverse wave consists of crests and troughs.<br />
(b) Speed of sound= 332m/s<br />
Time =3 sec<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7589/16766454509_cd627b5755_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-Q66" width="288" height="125" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 67</span></strong><br />
(a) When we put our ear to a railway line, we can hear the sound of an approaching train even when the train is far off but its sound cannot be heard through the air. This is due to the fact that sound travels much more fast through the railway line made of steel than through air.<br />
(b) There is no actual movement of air from the sound-producing body to our ear. The air layers only vibrate back and forth, and transfer the sound energy from one layer to the next layer till it reaches our ear.<br />
This will be clear from an example: If we turn on a gas tap for a few seconds, a person standing a few metres away will hear the sound of escaping gas first and the smell of gas reaches him afterwards. The sound of gas travels through the vibrations of air layers so it reaches first, but the smell of gas reaches the person through the actual movement of the air layers, which takes more time. So, it is clear that the sound is not being transmitted by the actual movement of air from the gas tap to person, otherwise he would hear and smell the gas at the same time.</p>

(b) Frequency = vibrations per sec x number of complete waves<br />
= 30 x 4 =120 Hz<br />
(c ) Speed = frequency x wavelength<br />
= 120 x 0.05= 6m/s<br />

<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 40</span></strong><br />
The persistence of sound in a big hall due to repeated reflections from the walls, ceiling and floor of the hall is called reverberation. If the reverberation time in a big hall is too long, then the sound becomes blurred, distorted and confusing due to overlapping.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 41</span></strong><br />
Reverberations in a big hall or auditorium can be reduced by the following methods :<br />
i) Panels made of sound absorbing materials are put on the walls and ceilings of hall and auditorium.<br />
ii) Carpets are put on the floor to absorb sound and reduce reverberations<br />
iii) Heavy curtains are put on doors and windows to absorb sound and reduce reverberations<br />
iv) The seats in the hall are made from materials having sound absorbing properties<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 42</span></strong><br />
We hear more clearly in a room with curtains than in a room without curtains because curtains are bad reflectors of sound. They absorb most of the sound falling on them, and hence do not produce echoes. On the other hand, in rooms without curtains, there is a greater reflection of sound due to which some echoes are produced.<br />
These echoes cause a hindrance to hearing.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 43</span></strong><br />
A megaphone is a large, cone-shaped (or funnel-shaped) device for amplifying and directing the voice of a person who speaks into it. A megaphone works on the principle of multiple reflections of sound.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 44</span></strong><br />
A bulb horn is a cone shaped wind instrument which used for signaling in bicycles, cars, buses, trucks and boats, etc. A bulb horn works on the principle of multiple<br />
reflections of sound.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 45</span></strong><br />
Stethoscope is a medical instrument used by the doctors for listening to the sounds produced within the human body, mainly in the heart and lungs. It works on the<br />
principle of multiple reflections of sound.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 46</span></strong><br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7624/16952678255_4de1443c47_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-A-Q46" width="341" height="250" /><br />
The soundboard is a concave board (curved board) which is placed behind the speaker in large halls or auditoriums so that his speech can be easily heard even by the persons sitting at a considerable distance. The sound board works as follows: the speaker is made to stand at the focus of the concave soundboard. The concave surface of the soundboard reflects the sound waves of the speaker towards the audience (and hence prevents the spreading of sound in various directions). Due to this, sound is distributed uniformly throughout the hall and even the persons sitting at the back of the hall can hear the speech easily.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 47</span></strong><br />
a) The loudness of sound is a measure of the sound energy reaching the ear per second. It depends on the amplitude of the sound waves.<br />
b) <img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7600/16332590653_cf301b7a6e_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-A-Q47" width="368" height="381" /><br />

<p><strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 49</span></strong><br />
Quality (or timbre) is that characteristic of the sound by which we can distinguish between sounds of same pitch and loudness produced by different musical instruments (and different singers). The quality (or timbre) depends on the shape of the sound wave (or waveform) produced by it.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 50</span></strong><br />
When we strike a table lightly, then due to less energy supplied, the table top vibrates with a small amplitude and hence a soft sound is produced. However if we hit the table hard, due to greater energy supplied, the table top vibrates with a large amplitude and hence a loud sound is produced.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 51</span></strong><br />
Ultrasound is used in industry for detecting flaws in metal blocks without damaging them. In hospitals, ultrasound is used to investigate the internal organs of the human body such as liver, kidneys, uterus, etc.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 52</span></strong><br />
Bats are able to fly at night without colliding with other objects because they emit high frequency ultrasonic squeaks while flying and listen to the echoes produced by the reflection of their squeaks from the objects or obstacles in their path. From the time taken by the echo to be heard, bats can judge the distance of the object in their path and avoid it by changing the direction.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 53</span></strong><br />
Bats emit high frequency ultrasonic squeaks while flying and listen to the echoes produced by the reflection of their squeaks from their prey. From the time taken by the echo to be heard, bats can judge the distance of the prey in their path and catch it.<br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 54</span></strong><br />
Ultrasound waves are made to pass through one face of the metal block and ultrasound detectors are placed on the opposite face of the block to detect the transmitted ultrasound waves.<br />
(i) If the ultrasound waves pass uninterrupted through all parts of the metal block, then the block is flawless.<br />
(ii) However, if the ultrasound waves are not able to pass through a part of the metal block and get reflected back, then there is a flaw in the metal block.<br />

The ceilings of concert halls are made curved so that sound, after reflection from the ceiling, reaches all part of the hall.<br />

<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7584/16952677995_1ed19b7a64_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-A-Q67" width="798" height="161" /><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 68</span></strong><br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8690/16765193630_112fe83621_o.png" alt="s-chand-class-9-physics-solutions-chapter-5-Sound-A-Q68" width="532" height="285" /><br />
Construction of human ear:<br />
The ear consists of three compartments: outer ear, middle ear and inner ear. The outer ear consists of broad part called pinna and about 2 to 3 centimeters long passage called ear canal. At the end of ear canal is a thin, elastic, circular membrane called tympanum or ear-drum. The middle ear contains three small delicate bones called hammer, anvil and stirrup. These bones are linked to one another. The one end of hammer is touching the ear drum and its other end is connected to the second bone called anvil. The other end of anvil is connected to the third bone called stirrup. And the free end of stirrup is held against the membrane over the oval window of the inner ear. The lower part of middle ear has Eustachian tube going to the throat. The inner ear has a coiled structure called cochlea. The cochlea is filled with liquid containing sound sensitive nerve cells. The other side of cochlea is connected to the auditory nerve which goes to the brain.<br />
Working of human ear:<br />
The sound waves are collected by the pinna. These sound waves pass through ear canal and fall on the ear-drum. Sound waves consist of compressions and rarefactions. When the compression strikes the ear drum, the pressure on the outside of ear drum increases and pushes the ear drum inwards. And when rarefaction strikes the ear drum, the pressure on the outside of ear drum decreases and it moves outwards. Thus, when sound waves fall on the ear drum, it vibrates back and forth rapidly. These vibrations are passed onto the three bones in the middle ear and finally to the liquid in the cochlea. Due to this, liquid in the cochlea starts to vibrate, setting up electrical impulses in the nerve cells present in it. These impulses are carried to the brain by auditory nerve. The brain interprets the impulses and we get the sensation of hearing.</p>

solution 90<br />
(a) The person would hear a lot of noise of heavy traffic in a city.<br />
(b) The person would hear very little noise of traffic in a village.<br />
(c) The person would hear echoes of persons talking in a bare room.<br />
(d) The person will find furnished room less echoic.</p>

<h2><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 6 Natural Resources</span></strong></h2>
<p><strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">Text Book Solutions &#8211; P.S.Verma and V.K.Agarwal &#8211; Biology</span></strong></p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">CBSE Class 9 Chapter 6 Natural Resources</span></strong></p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page No &#8211; 356.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 1</span><br />
Air is composed of a mixture of gases such as nitrogen, oxygen and carbon dioxide. It also contains water vapours and suspended dust particles.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 2</span><br />
Oxygen is required by all living beings for respiration and for burning materials. This is balanced by green plants. Green plants take in carbon dioxide and release oxygen during the process of photosynthesis.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 3</span><br />
The atmosphere keeps the average temperature of the earth fairly steady during the day as the atmosphere prevents the sudden increase in temperature during the daylight hours and at night atmosphere slows down the escape of heat into the outer space.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 4</span><br />
The movement of air from one region to another creates winds. When the solar radiations fall on the earth, some are absorbed and majority of these are reflected back by the land and water bodies. These reflected solar radiations heat up the atmosphere from below. As a result convection currents are set up in the air but since land gets heated faster than the water, the air above the land gets heated faster than the air over water bodies. During the day the air above the land gets heated and starts rising, creating a region of low pressure below. As a result the air over the sea moves into this region of low pressure and forms the wind.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 5</span><br />
(i) Take a beaker full of water, a beaker full of soil and a closed bottle containing a thermometer.<br />
(ii) Keep them in bright sunlight for three hours.<br />
(iii) Now, measure the temperature of all three vessels and also take the temperature reading in shade at the same time.<br />
(iv) You will observe that the temperature of the soil and sand is more than that of water in bright sunlight because sand and soil gets heated by solar radiations faster than the water.<br />
(v) Therefore, land would become hot faster than the sea.<br />
(vi) You will also observe that the temperature of air in shade is different from the temperature of soil, sand and water in bright sunlight because of the direct effect of radiations.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 6</span><br />
When the solar radiations fall on the earth, some are absorbed and majority of these are reflected back or re-radiated by the land and water bodies. These reflected or re-radiated solar radiations heat the atmosphere from below. As a result convection currents are set up in the air.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 7</span><br />
The factors that influence the movement of air are:<br />
(i) Uneven heating of land at different parts of the earth.<br />
(ii) Differences in heating and cooling of land and water bodies.<br />
(iii) Vapourisation and condensation of water vapours.<br />
(iv) Rotation of earth.<br />
(v) Presence of high mountain ranges in the paths of wind.<br />
(vi) Difference in topography over which the wind passes.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 8</span><br />
When the water bodies get heated by solar radiations during the day, a large amount of water evaporates and goes in the air. The air carrying water vapours also gets heated. This hot air rises up carrying water vapours with it. As the air rises, it expands and cools. This cooling causes the water vapour in the air to condense as tiny droplets which slowly grow bigger by the condensation of more water droplets and forms clouds. When the droplets have grown big and heavy, they fall down in the form of rain.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 9</span><br />
(i) Take an empty plastic bottle.<br />
(ii) Pour 5-10 ml water into it and close the bottle tightly with a cap.<br />
(iii) Shake the bottle well and then place it in the sun for 10 minutes.<br />
(iv) Now, open the cap of the bottle and allow some smoke from the lighted incense stick to enter the bottle.<br />
(v) Quickly close the bottle tightly with the cap.<br />
(vi) Press the bottle hard between your hands as much as possible.<br />
(vii) After few seconds release the bottle. Press the bottle again as hard as you can.<br />
This simple experiment replicates, on a very small scale, the happenings when air with a very high content of water vapour goes from a region of high pressure to a region of low pressure. When bottle containing water is kept in the sun, the water evaporates and air inside the bottle gets saturated with water vapour. When the bottle is pressed between your hands, the pressure inside becomes high and air inside the bottle moves in a region of low pressure. It expands and cools. The smoke particles act as &#8216;nuclei&#8217; on which water vapours condense in the form of tiny droplets. When you release the pressure, the air inside the bottle becomes foggy. When bottle is again pressed, the fog will disappear. It is so because due to high pressure condensed water vapours will fall down and collect as water at the bottom of the bottle. When the experiment is repeated without smoke inside the bottle, one will not observe foggy air inside the bottle as smoke particles are absent and nothing is available in air to act as &#8216;nucleus&#8217; for water vapours to condense as tiny droplets.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 10</span><br />
The major components of air pollution are soot, fly ash, dust particles, smoke and some gases like sulphur dioxide, carbon monoxide, nitrogen oxide, ammonia etc.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 11</span><br />
When fossil fuels such as coal and petroleum products are burnt, they produce oxides of nitrogen and sulphur. On dissolving in rain these oxides form nitric acid and sulphuric acid respectively. This causes acid rain. These acids wash down into the soil and make it highly acidic, thus, affecting the growth of plants and ultimately the forest growth. It also affects the surface of buildings by eroding the stone and brick works.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 12</span><br />
Smog is a photochemical haze caused by the action of solar ultra violet radiation on atmosphere polluted with primary pollutants such as hydrocarbons and oxides of nitrogen from automobile exhaust. It reduces visibility and is highly suffocating and toxic to humans, animals and plants.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 13</span><br />
Effects of air pollution on human beings:<br />
(i) Suspended particulate matter causes asthma, bronchitis and allergic cold.<br />
(ii) Pollutant gases cause irritation in eyes, throat and lungs. Heart related diseases tend to increase.<br />
(iii) Hydrocarbon vapours not only damage the internal organs but also cause cancer.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 14</span><br />
In coastal areas, during daytime, there is a regular flow of cool air from the sea towards the land. At night, there is a reverse flow of air from land to sea. This happens because during the daytime, land gets heated faster than water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 15</span><br />
The atmosphere keeps the average temperature of the earth fairly steady during the day as the atmosphere prevents the sudden increase in temperature during the daylight hours and at night atmosphere slows down the escape of heat into the outer space.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 16</span><br />
Atmosphere is divided into five distinct layers: Troposphere, stratosphere, mesosphere, thermosphere and exosphere.<br />
i. Troposphere is the lowest region of atmosphere which contains air and is subject of differential heating. It extends from the surface of the earth upto 8-20 kms. Many important climatic events such as cloud formation, lightning, thundering etc all takes place in the troposphere.<br />
ii. The Stratosphere extends from the top of the troposphere up to around 31 miles (50 km) above the Earth&#8217;s surface. In this region the temperature increases with height. Heat is produced due to the formation of ozone.<br />
iii. The mesosphere extends from the top of the stratosphere to about 53 miles (85 km) above the earth. The gases, including the oxygen molecules, continue to become thinner and thinner with height.<br />
iv. Above the mesosphere the thermosphere extends up to near 375 miles (600 km) above the earth. This layer is known as the upper atmosphere. As such, incoming high energy ultraviolet and x-ray radiation from the sun, absorbed by the molecules in this layer, causes a large temperature increase.<br />
v. Exosphere exists above the thermosphere.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 17</span><br />
Air pollution is of two main types:<br />
Natural: It is the pollution caused by nature. It includes forest fires, dust storms, pollen etc.<br />
Human made: It is the pollution caused by human activities. It includes burning of fossil fuels in industries, vehicles and thermoelectric plants, gaseous emission from industries, mining, processing and stone crushing.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 18</span><br />
When the water bodies get heated by solar radiations during the day, a large amount of water evaporates and goes in the air. The air carrying water vapours also gets heated. This hot air rises up carrying water vapours with it. As the air rises it expands and cools. This cooling causes the water vapours in the air to condense as tiny droplets which slowly grow bigger by the condensation of more water droplets and forms clouds.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 19</span><br />
Global warming: An increase in the carbon dioxide content in the atmosphere leads to global warming. The global warming is quite dangerous as it tends to melt polar ice and glaciers existing on mountains, rise in the water level of the oceans and submerge several coastal areas and islands. This could further lead to floods.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 20</span><br />
Ozone depletion is caused by certain chemicals called ozone depleting substances. They include chlorofluoro carbons, methyl bromide, nitrogen oxides and chlorine.<br />
Effects of ozone depletion:<br />
(i) Skin cancer.<br />
(ii) Damage of eyes.<br />
(iii) Damage of immune system.<br />
(iv) Decreased crop yields.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 21</span><br />
When fossil fuels such as coal and petroleum products are burnt, they produce oxides of nitrogen and sulphur. On dissolving in rain these oxides form nitric acid and sulphuric acid respectively. This causes acid rain. These acids wash down into the soil and make it highly acidic, thus, affecting the growth of plants and ultimately the forest growth. It also affects the surface of buildings by eroding the stone and brick works.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 22</span><br />
Rainwater harvesting is a technique used to capture and store rain water by making special water harvesting structures so that there is an increase in the recharge of underground water resources.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 23</span><br />
Climate is the average weather of an area. It represents the general pattern of atmospheric or weather conditions, seasonal variations and weather extremes, in a region over an extended period, say 50 years or 100 years. For example, desert areas have a hot climate whereas snowbound mountains have a cold climate.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 24</span><br />
The short term changes in the properties of the troposphere forms the weather. The weather changes take place everyday. It tells us about the temperature, rain, cloud and sunshine of an area.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 25</span><br />
CFC&#8217;s are chlorofluoro carbons which deplete the ozone layer. They are rich in chlorine, fluorine and carbon.<br />
Effects of chlorofluoro carbons:<br />
(i) Skin cancer.<br />
(ii) Damage of eyes.<br />
(iii) Damage of immune system.<br />
(iv) Decreased crop yields.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 26</span><br />
Break down of bigger rocks into smaller mineral particles is called weathering. It is of 3 types:<br />
(i) Physical weathering: Various climatic factors such as temperature, wind, rain water, ice, snow, glaciers and running water contribute to physical weathering. Water and high temperature cause corrosive humidity and bring about unequal expansion and contraction of rocks, facilitating their break down.<br />
(ii) Chemical weathering: It involves a variety of chemical processes, such as hydrolysis, hydration, oxidation and reduction. The breakdown of complex compounds by the carbonic acids present in water and acidic substances derived from the decomposition of organic matter in soil, are examples of chemical weathering.<br />
(iii) Biological weathering: Is done by living organisms such as lichens and bryophytes. They create small crevices which deepen to form cracks in the rocks. Cracks gradually widen and cause slow fragmentation and eventually pulverisation of rocks.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 27</span><br />
The removal and transportation of the top layer of soil from its original position to another place, under the effect of strong winds and fast running rainwater is called soil erosion. Soil erosion can be prevented by :<br />
(i) Intensive cropping<br />
(ii) Sowing grasses and planting xerophytes.<br />
(iii) Terrace farming.<br />
(iv) Contour bunding.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 28</span><br />
Biological weathering: Is done by living organisms such as lichens and bryophytes. Lichens growing on rock surface extract minerals from the rocks. This creates small crevices at places where a thin layer of soil builds up. Mosses grow over these crevices causing deepening of crevices and results in the buildup of more soil inside them. The roots of short lived herbs also passes into them and the cracks gradually widen and cause slow fragmentation and eventually pulverisation of rocks.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 29</span><br />
Water is replenished in the seas by the means of water or hydrological cycle. We know that the oceans or seas are the largest global reservoir of water. Water evaporates from these reservoirs in large quantities and helps in the formation of clouds. The winds blows the clouds over to the lands where after getting cooled enough, the water in clouds falls on the earth or directly over the seas as rain and hail. Some water from rain and melting snow soaks into the ground, but most of it flows in rivers and returns directly to the seas.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 30</span><br />
Nitrogen fixation is the process of fixing free nitrogen into compounds. This takes place by the following means:<br />
(a) Certain blue-green algae and bacteria can fix atmospheric nitrogen.<br />
(b) Nitrogen fixing bacteria found in the nodules of roots of legumes such as gram, bean, pulses etc. fix atmospheric nitrogen into nitrogen containing compounds.<br />
(c) Lightning also helps in the formation of nitrogen containing compounds.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 31</span><br />
Nitrogen exists as free nitrogen in the atmosphere. This free nitrogen is fixed into compounds of ammonia and nitrates. Most of the organisms cannot utilise nitrogen as molecular nitrogen. Plants take compounds containing nitrogen from the soil. From plants nitrogen passes into the food web. Decay of dead plants, animals and excreta causes return of nitrogen compounds to the soil. Denitrifying bacteria cause liberation of free nitrogen in the atmosphere.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 32</span><br />
Carbon is an important constituent of organic compounds found in all living beings in the form of carbohydrates, fats, proteins and nucleic acids. Carbon is trapped in the surrounding air and water in the form of carbon dioxide. The consumers devour the organic carbon compounds that producers manufacture. Through respiration, both consumers and producers return carbon to the non-living environment in the form of carbon dioxide. Some carbon accumulates in wood for many years and is eventually returned to the atmosphere by fires or through consumption and respiration by fungi, bacteria and other detrivores. Volcanic eruption also releases carbon dioxide to the atmosphere.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 33</span><br />
The dangers of global warming are:<br />
(i) It leads to the melting of polar ice caps and rise in sea level.<br />
(ii) Increase in the temperature of the earth due to green house effect will cause a change in weather and precipitation patterns on the earth.<br />
(iii) It leads to methane burp which is caused by the melting of methane hydrates in permafrost and on sea floor.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 34</span><br />
Carbon dioxide concentration in atmosphere is rising primarily because of two reasons: (i) Deforestation and (ii) Increased combustion of fossil fuels.<br />
As trees take in carbon dioxide from air and release oxygen back into the air, it helps in maintaining the desired levels of oxygen and carbon dioxide in the atmosphere. But due to deforestation, trees are being cut down and this is leading to the increase in carbon dioxide levels.<br />
The increased combustion of fossil fuels also leads to the release of enormous amounts of carbon dioxide in the atmosphere.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 35</span><br />
Ozone layer is called ozone umbrella/shield because it filters out the harmful, high energy ultra violet radiations coming from the sun.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 36</span><br />
In 1985, Farmen found that ozone layer had thinned out over Antarctica. It was called an ozone hole.<br />
Effects of widening of ozone hole are:<br />
(i) Skin cancer.<br />
(ii) Damage of eyes.<br />
(iii) Damage of immune system.<br />
(iv) Decreased crop yields.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 37</span><br />
Water is one of the most important physical components which is essential for the survival of live on earth. Ocean is the biggest storehouse of water. Water on evaporation forms clouds and which after condensation falls down as rain. After rain, it passes through rivers and gets collected again in the ocean. The circulation of water in this manner is called water cycle. The cycle is also performed through living beings in the processes like absorption and transpiration of water by plants and drinking by animals. Animals lose water during respiration and evaporation, perspiration and excretion.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 38</span><br />
(i) Nitrogen cycle<br />

(ii) Carbon cycle<br />
