<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 39</span><br />
The bacteria which help in nitrogen fixation are Azotobactor and Rhizobium. Some bacteria help to convert ammonia into nitrates. These are Nitrosomonas and Nitrobactor.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 40:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-6-40.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 4" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 41:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-6-41.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 4" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 42</span><br />
The three aspects of nutrient cycling are:<br />
(i) Input of nutrients &#8211; An ecosystem receives the nutrients from an external source. It stores them for further use through biological processes.<br />
(ii) Output of nutrients &#8211; Nutrients move out of an ecosystem and many of them become input to another ecosystem.<br />
(iii) Internal nutrient cycling &#8211; Nutrients are continuously regenerated and stored in soil in forms available to plants. This is done by decomposers by the process of decomposition of detritus.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 43</span><br />
The organisms get water from and return it to the global water cycle. Plants absorb water from the soil or water reservoir and add it to the air in vapour form by a process called transpiration. Water transpired by trees cools the surrounding air. Animals take water from the water reservoir or with food and return it to the air and vapours by respiration or to the soil by excretion. Mammals also excrete water as sweat which evaporates from the water bodies. Water is added to the environment by the death and decay of organisms. Water vapour formed by transpiration and respiration form clouds and enters global water cycle. Rain adds water to the soil and reservoir for reuse by plants and animals. This completes the water cycle.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-6-laq-01.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 4" width="750" height="450" /><br />
Natural resources are living and non-living components of nature which are used by humans to meet their requirements. Since natural resources are available only from the Earth, they are called Earth resources.<br />
Based on their abundance, natural resources are of two main types, inexhaustible and exhaustible.<br />
(a) Inexhaustible natural resources: They are natural resources which occur in such abundance that they are not likely to get exhausted despite continuous use, e.g., air, water, solar energy.<br />
(b) Exhaustible natural resources: They are natural resources which are available in limited quantity. They may to get depleted by continuous and indiscriminate human consumption. Exhaustible resources are of two kinds, renewable and non-renewable.<br />
(i) Renewable resources: They are exhaustible resources which get replenished regularly. These are both living and non-living resources which can replenish themselves by quick recycling, e.g., forests, wildlife, soil and underground water. Renewable resources can last for ever if they are used responsibly.<br />
(ii) Non-renewable resources: They are exhaustible resources which once used cannot be replenished. Thus, these resources are non-living and cannot replenish themselves by recycling and replacement. If not used carefully they will ultimately get exhausted. Their increased consumption results in quicker exhaustion, e.g., minerals, fossil fuels such as coal and petroleum.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 2</span><br />
Air contains oxygen. The latter is needed by most organisms and plants for all respiration to go on. It is therefore rightly called the breath of life. Air is an inexhaustible natural resource. In a world without air, there would be no plant or animal life, no winds, clouds or rain, no fires and no protection against harmful solar radiations. This is because the atmosphere covers the Earth, like a blanket. Air is a bad conductor of heat. The atmosphere keeps the average temperature of the Earth fairly steady during the day and even during the course of whole year. The atmosphere prevents the sudden increase in temperature during the daylight hours. And at night, atmosphere slows down the escape of heat into outer space.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 3</span><br />
The introduction of chemicals, particulate matter, or biological materials into the atmosphere that cause harm or irritate living organisms or damage the natural environment is known as air pollution.<br />
The major causes of air pollution can be in the form of solid particles, liquid droplets, or gas. There are many different chemical substances that contribute to air pollution. These chemicals come from a variety of sources. Among the many types of air pollutants are nitrogen oxides, carbon monoxides, and organic compounds that can evaporate and enter the atmosphere.<br />
Air pollutants have sources that are both natural and human. Humans contribute substantially more to the air pollution problem. Forest fires, volcanic eruptions, wind erosion, pollen dispersal, evaporation of organic compounds, and natural radioactivity are all among the natural causes of air pollution. Though some pollution comes from these natural sources, most pollution is the result of human activity. The biggest causes are the operation of fossil fuel-burning, power plants and automobiles that combust fuel.<br />
Effects of air pollution on human beings:<br />
(i) SPM (suspeneded particulate matter) causes asthma, bronchitis and allergic cold.<br />
(ii) Pollutant gases cause irritation in eyes, throat and lungs. Heart related diseases tend to increase.<br />
(iii) Hydrocarbon vapours not only damage the internal organs but also cause cancer.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 4</span><br />
The ozone layer is a deep layer in the stratosphere, encircling the Earth, which has large amounts of ozone in it. This layer shields the entire Earth from much of the harmful ultraviolet radiation that comes from the sun. Ozone is a special form of oxygen, made up of three oxygen atoms rather than the usual two oxygen atoms.<br />
It is formed when some type of radiation or electrical discharge separates the two atoms in an oxygen molecule (O2), which can then individually recombine with other oxygen molecules to form ozone (O3).<br />
Reduction in the concentration of ozone layer is called ozone depletion. Ozone depletion is caused by certain chemicals called ozone depleting substances. They include chlorofluoro carbons, methyl bromide, nitrogen oxides and chlorine.<br />
Effects of ozone depletion: Depleting ozone layer allows more ultraviolet (UV) radiations to pass through it, which reach the earth&#8217;s surface. These UV rays cause various harmful effects on human beings, animals, plants and environment such as:<br />
(i) Skin cancer.<br />
(ii) Damage of eyes.<br />
(iii) Damage of immune system.<br />
(iv) Decreased crop yields.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 5</span><br />
Sources of water pollution:<br />
(i) Sewage &#8211; Organic wastes are contributed as domestic and commercial sewage by food processing plants, dairy farms, piggeries, poultry farms, slaughter houses, breweries, tanneries, etc. Animal excreta is discharged into fields or dumped into pits reaches water bodies through run off and leaching, particularly during the rainy season.<br />
(ii) Industrial wastes &#8211; Effluents of mills and industries such as paper mills, petroleum refineries, etc., contain large quantities of harmful chemicals including acids, alkalis and heavy metals (e.g., mercury salts from paper industries) that are discharged into water bodies (rivers and lakes).<br />
(iii) Synthetic soaps and detergents &#8211; Water containing soaps and detergents is discharged from houses and certain factories.<br />
(iv) Fertilizers and pesticides &#8211; Fertilizers and pesticides are being used excessively in the fields to increase crop production. These are washed by rainwater into water bodies and pollute them.<br />
(v) Petroleum oil &#8211; Drilling and shipping operations are common in the oceans. Leakage of petroleum oil during such operations or due to accidents results in water pollution.<br />
(vi) Solid particles &#8211; Rain erodes soil and carries silt to water. Tiny suspended particles of clay and dust also settle in water from air. These soil particles cause turbidity.<br />
(vii) Thermal pollution &#8211; Discharge of hot water from industries and thermal plants into water body changes the normal temperature of the water. The content of oxygen decreases. Reduced oxygen content kills aquatic animals and reduces the rate of decomposition of organic matter which, therefore, accumulates.<br />
Harmful effects of Water pollution:<br />
(i) Human diseases &#8211; Diseases such as typhoid, cholera, dysentery, jaundice and hepatitis are caused due to water pollution.<br />
(ii) Disturbance in ecological balance &#8211; All types of water pollutants affect the life forms living in the water. These pollutants can encourage the growth of some life forms and harm some other life forms hence affecting the balance between various organisms.<br />
(iii) Removal of desirable substances from water bodies &#8211; With increase in the amount of organic wastes in water, bacteria multiply rapidly and use up the available oxygen. Lack of oxygen kills the fish and other animals.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 6</span><br />
(i) Eutrophication is nutrient enrichment (i.e., addition of nitrates and phosphates) of water body that results in the growth of aquatic plants, especially algae causing colouration of water known as algal bloom. It leads to depletion of dissolved oxygen in water resulting in killing of aquatic organisms (e.g., fish).<br />
(ii) The phenomenon of increase in the concentration of harmful non-biodegradable substances in the body of living organisms at each trophic level of the food chain is called biomagnification. Two heavy metals which are biomagnified are mercury and cadmium. Due to biomagnification fish-eating predatory birds such as kingfishers and loon become poisoned.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 7</span><br />
Living organisms need water because it plays a vital role in the reactions taking place within organism&#8217;s cells and body. Water acts as a universal solvent, providing a medium for the chemical reactions to occur. Substances are also transported from one part of body to the other in the dissolved state. Therefore, it is necessary for the organisms to maintain a distinct level of water within their bodies in order to stay alive. Terrestrial life forms require fresh water because their bodies cannot tolerate or get rid of the high amounts of the dissolved salts in saline water. So, water sources need to be easily accessible to animals and plants to survive on land.<br />
Thus, availability of water decides not only the number of individuals of each species that are able to survive in a particular area, but it also decides the diversity of life there.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 8</span><br />
Soil is a mixture of small particles of rocks and humus (i.e., organic matter obtained from decaying of living organisms or their wastes). Temperature variations due to radiations of the sun, rain water, winds and living organisms influence the formation of soil from the rocks involving two processes: weathering and paedogenesis.<br />
Breakdown of bigger rocks into small, fine soil particles is called weathering. It may occur due to physical, chemical or biological means. Under the influence of solar radiations, rocks heat up and expand. At night, these rocks cool down and contract. Since all the parts of rocks do not expand and contract at the same rate, cracks appear in the rocks and ultimately the large rocks breakdown into smaller pieces. Flow of water through or over the rocks makes the cracks bigger. Flowing/falling water also has an erasing effect on the rocks. On freezing the water expands in rock crevices and breaks the rocks. Similarly, strong winds continue to rub against hard rocks and erode them. Growth of lichens, mosses and other plants also influence the formation of soil by eroding the rocks over which they are growing.<br />
Paedogenesis: This process concludes the decomposition by bacteria and fungi, during which organic materials are broken down, leading to humification and mineralization. Detritivores such as nematods, earthworms, etc., consume organic matter and add excretory nitrogen to it. Thus, addition of organic matter (humus) from dead and decomposed plants and animals, is the final stage in soil formation.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 9</span><br />
Soil pollution is caused by solid wastes and chemicals. The slag heaps from mines spoil the beauty of sites of mines. Pulp and paper mills, sugar mills, oil refineries, power plants, chemicals fertilizer manufacturing units, iron and steel plants, plastic and rubber producing complexes are some major contributions to soil pollution. Most industrial furnaces and thermal power stations produce fly ash, which is a grey, powdery residue of unburnt material, and causes pollution. This fly ash hampers the growth of crop plants and also decreases crops of orchards. Domestic waste also adds a large amount of solid wastes. Modern farming practices involve the use of large amounts of fertilizers and pesticides. Use of these substances over long period of time can destroy the soil structure by killing the soil microorganisms that recycle nutrients in the soil. It also kills the earthworms which are helpful in making the rich humus. Fertile soils can quickly become barren if sustainable practices are not followed.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 10</span><br />
The removal and transportation of top soil from its original position to another place with the help of certain agents such as strong winds and fast running waters, is called soil erosion.<br />
Causes of Soil Erosion:<br />
1. Strong winds: The soil which is uncovered and loose, is eroded, when it is exposed to strong winds. The winds carry away the fine soil particles to other places.<br />
2. Heavy rains: When rain falls on the unprotected top soil, rain water washes it down into the streams and rivers, etc.<br />
3. Human actions: Human activities such as expansion of urban areas has led to removal of vegetation from certain regions. The bare land is thus exposed to agencies (winds, rains) of soil erosion.<br />
Effects of Soil Erosion:<br />
1. Loss of fertility and desertification: Soil erosion results in the displacement of the top soil from one region to another, thus, reducing its fertility. When the top fertile soil is constantly removed from a region, only infertile sub-soil is left behind. In such a soil, only sparse vegetation can grow. This way, soil erosion gradually turns lush green areas into deserts.<br />
2. Landslides in hilly areas: Barren hills or hills with sparse vegetation are constantly exposed to heavy rain fall that makes the top soils of hills loose. Due to soil erosion, rock pieces of various sizes and loose soil from hills, suddenly slide down the steep slopes of mountains/hills. This phenomenon is called landslides. When these rock pieces and soil block the narrow river bed they result in floods. Sometimes, landslides block the roads and disrupt hill-life.<br />
3. Flash floods: Vegetation in the hilly regions absorb a lot of rain water and keep the top soil intact. Barren hills or hills with sparse vegetation cannot absorb much rain water and thus can not keep the soil intact. So, heavy rains result in rapid movement of water in the areas resulting in flash floods in lower areas causing enormous loss to life and property.<br />
Prevention of soil erosion:<br />
1. Intensive cropping: If the fields remain covered with crops throughout the year, their top soil will not be exposed to winds or rains. In such a condition, no soil erosion will occur.<br />
2. Sowing grasses and planting xerophytes: Soil should not be left uncovered. Sowing grasses on barren soil or planting of xerophytes will bind the loose soil. The roots of grasses and xerophytes hold the soil in place. Vegetative cover on the ground also helps in percolating water into deeper layers of soil.<br />
3. Terrace farming (terracing): In terracing the slopes are divided into a number of flat fields to slow down the flow of water. In hilly regions, small crop fields are thus formed in the form of steps on terraces for cultivation of crops. Such terrace farms reduced the flow of rain water down the slopes of hills. Moreover, eroded soil from upper regions of hills gets deposited in lower terraces.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 11</span><br />
The continuous process by which nitrogen is exchanged between organisms and the environment is called nitrogen cycle. Nitrogen is an essential nutrient, needed to make amino acids and other important organic compounds, but most organisms cannot use free nitrogen, which is abundant as a gas in the atmosphere.<br />
Nitrogen cycle involves the following steps:<br />
(i) Nitrogen fixation: This process involves the conversion of atmospheric nitrogen into nitrates, which are soluble in water. This is done by various nitrogen fixing bacteria. Example &#8211; Rhizobium, blue green algae and bacterium Azotobacter.<br />
(ii) Ammonification: It is the process of decomposing complex, dead organic matter into ammonia. This is done by microorganisms living in the soil.<br />
(iii) Nitrification: It is the process of conversion of ammonia into nitrites and then into nitrates. This is done by nitrifying bacteria. Example &#8211; Nitrosomonas and Nitrobacter.<br />
(iv) Denitrification: It is the process of reducing nitrates present in the soil to release nitrogen back into the atmosphere. Example &#8211; Pseudomonas.<br />
The decomposers help in decomposing the dead bodies of plants and animals, and hence act as cleansing agents of environment. The decomposers also help in putting back the various elements of which the dead plants and animals were made, back into the soil, air and water for reuse by the producers like crop-plants, e.g. the decomposers like purifying bacteria and fungi decompose the dead plants and animal bodies into ammonia. This ammonia is converted into nitrates by nitrifying bacteria present in soil. These nitrates act as fertilizer in the soil and are again absorbed by the plants for their growth. Thus, the nitrates act as fertilizer in the biosphere so that the process of life may go on and on like an unending chain.</p>

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 06:</span><br />
Advantages of manures are:<br />
(i) Manures are natural fertilizers.<br />
(ii) Manures are bulky sources of organic matter which supply nutrients in small quantity and organic matter in large quantities.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 07:</span><br />
Limitations of using manures are:<br />
(i) Manures are not nutrient specific.<br />
(ii) Manures are not able to fulfill the high and rapid demand of nutrients required by improved high-yielding hybrid varieties of crops.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 08;</span><br />
Manure contains many organic substances of biological origin which can be easily degraded and absorbed by plants. It helps in recycling of biological waste. Manures increase the fertility of soil for long duration without causing any harm. However, the chemical fertilizers (e.g. urea) improve soil fertility for short duration but cause environmental hazard. Continuous use of fertilizers in a particular area / crop field causes destruction of soil fertility.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 09:</span><br />
Advantages of fertilizer over manure:<br />
(i) Fertilizers are very rich in plant nutrient whereas manure contains small amounts of essential plant nutrients.<br />
(ii) Fertilizers are soluble in water whereas manure is not soluble in water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 10:</span><br />
As a result of this, the pond water would acquire a high concentration of nitrates and phosphates which would result in the excessive growth of algae and phytoplankton in the pond.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 11:</span><br />
Eutrophication is a process whereby water bodies, such as lakes or slow-moving streams receive excess nutrients that stimulate excessive plant growth (algae, phytoplankton&#8217;s and nuisance plants weeds). This enhanced plant growth is also termed as an algal bloom.<br />
Example: During rains the nutrients from the fields are washed away and get accumulated in nearby water bodies.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 12:</span><br />
The continuous use of chemical fertilizers in a particular area or crop field leads to loss of soil fertility.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 13:</span><br />
There are three methods of fertilizer applications in practice:<br />
(i) Broadcasting: Uniform distribution over the whole cropped field.<br />
(ii) Placement: Application in bands or in pockets near the plants or plant rows.<br />
(iii) Foliar application: Using low or high volume sprayers, the fertilizers are sprayed covering the plants.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 14:</span><br />
Farmyard Manure<br />
It is the decomposed mixture of cattle excreta, dung, urine, litter and left over organism matter such as roughage and Fodder.<br />
Compost Manure<br />
It is prepared from farm and town refuge such as vegetable and animal refuse.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 15:</span><br />
Manure &#8211; Manures are natural fertilizers. They are bulky sources of organic matter which supply nutrients in small quantities, and organic matter in large quantities. There are different types of manures: Farmyard manure (FYM), Compost, Green manures and Vermicompost.<br />
Manures affect the soil in following three ways:<br />
(i) Manures enrich the soil with nutrients. They replenish the general deficiency of nutrients in the soil. Since manure contains fewer nutrients they need to be used in large quantities.<br />
(ii) Manures add organic matter (called humus) to the soil which restores the soil texture, for better retention of water and aeration of soil.<br />
(iii) The organic matter in manures provides food for the soil organisms, (decomposers such as bacteria, fungi, etc. which help in providing nutrients to plants.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 16:</span><br />
Green manuring is the practice which includes growing, mulching by ploughing and mixing of green crops with soil, to improve physical structure and soil fertility.<br />
Example &#8211; Sunn hemp (Crotalaria juncea).<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 17:</span><br />
Fertilizers &#8211; Fertilizers are one of the major components for obtaining higher yields especially in expensive farming practices. Fertilizers are divided into following four groups:<br />
(i) Nitrogenous fertilizers &#8211; These fertilizers supply the macronutrient nitrogen.<br />
Example &#8211; Urea, CO(NH2)2<br />
(ii) Potassic fertilizers &#8211; These fertilizers supply potassium which is one of the essential macronutrient of the plants.<br />
Example &#8211; Potassium sulphate, K2SO4.<br />
(iii) Complex fertilizers &#8211; These fertilizers contains two or more nutrients.<br />
Example &#8211; Nitrophosphate<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 18:</span><br />
Biofertilisers &#8211; Organisms which enrich the soil with nutrients are called biofertilisers. Biofertilisers are used for the specific crop plants such as pulses, legumes, oil seeds and rice. They are renewable and non-pollutant sources of plant nutrient such as nitrogen.<br />
Nitrogen fixing microorganisms, i.e., non-symbiotic and symbiotic cyanobacteria and phosphate-solubilising microorganism are the main type of biofertilisers.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 19:</span><br />
A legume crop does not require nitrogenous fertilizers because its roots have root nodules which have nitrogenous bacteria called Rhizobium. This bacteria fixes atmospheric nitrogen and the plants converts nitrogen into various nitrogenous compounds.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 20:</span><br />
Irrigation is essential for the absorption of nutrient elements by the crop plants from the soil. The irrigation water tends to dissolve the nutrients present in the soil of a crop field to form a Solution. This Solution of nutrients is then absorbed by the roots of crops for the development of the plants.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 21:</span><br />
Excessive irrigation causes water logging and increases surface salinity which leads to soil salinity.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 22:</span><br />
Effects of excessive irrigation:<br />
(i) It causes water logging.<br />
(ii) It increases salinity in the soil.<br />
(iii) The roots do not get proper aeration due to which they die.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 23:</span><br />
Water should be used judiciously because:<br />
(i) It helps in the cultivation of crops.<br />
(ii) In desert areas where there is scarcity of water, it is supplied through irrigation practices to prevent drought.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 24:</span><br />
Advantages of irrigation:<br />
(i) It is necessary to provide sufficient moisture for the germination of seeds.<br />
(ii) Irrigation of crop plants is essential for the growth and elongation of roots of the crop plants.<br />
(iii) It is necessary to increase the number of aerial branches in crop plants.<br />
(iv)It is essential for the absorption of nutrient elements by the crop plants from the soil.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 25:</span><br />
The efficiency of irrigation can be increased by:<br />
(i) Drip and sprinkler system &#8211; It increases the efficiency of irrigation as it sprays water through pipes and a sprinkler.<br />
(ii) River lift system &#8211; It is useful in those areas where canal flow is insufficient or irregular due to inadequate water release. The water is directly drawn from the rivers for supplement irrigation.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 26:</span><br />
There are two main factors responsible for loss of grains during storage:<br />
(i) Biotic factors &#8211; Insects, rodents, birds, mites and bacteria.<br />
(ii) Abiotic factors &#8211; They include moisture, temperature and other non-living environmental factors.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 27:</span><br />
Biotic and abiotic factors which cause destruction of grains during storage can be prevented by the following methods:<br />
(i) Drying &#8211; The harvested food grains should be dried by spreading them over plastic sheets or cemented floors. All the sun dried food grains are allowed to cool to room temperature before storing them.<br />
(ii) Cleaning &#8211; The grains should be properly cleaned before storage. They should be filled in new gunny bags before keeping in godowns, warehouses or stores.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 28:</span><br />
Drying &#8211; The harvested food grains is dried by spreading them over plastic sheets or cemented floors. All the sun dried food grains are then allowed to cool to room temperature before storing them.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 29:</span><br />
For the storage of grains, grain silos are used. The silos are big and tall cylindrical structures. They are provided with outlets at different levels to withdraw the desired stock of grains. They have built in arrangement for aeration, temperature control, protection from insects, rats, birds etc.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 30:</span><br />
Field crops are infested with a variety of pests. There are various methods by which insects and diseases can be controlled. One of the most common and effective methods is the use of pesticides or biocides which include insecticides (for killing the insects), weedicides (for killing the weeds) and fungicides (for killing the fungi). Thus chemicals used to kill the pests, e.g. weeds; insects, mites, rodents and fungi are called pesticides. These chemicals are sprayed on crop plants or used for treating seeds and soil.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 31:</span><br />
During the grain storage, if the loss is due to the biotic factors which includes insects, rodents, birds, mites, fungi and bacteria, then it shows the presence of pests in the grain stores.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 32:</span><br />
Spraying:<br />
(i) Spraying requires mechanical devices such as manual sprayer or mechanical sprayer.<br />
(ii) It is less effective than fumigation.<br />
Fumigation:<br />
(i) It does not require any mechanical device.<br />
(ii) It is more effective than spraying.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 33;</span><br />
Milk is rich in fat, tocopherol, proteins, calcium, and phosphorus and contains low sodium, potassium and cholesterol. It is ideal for making milk products like ghee, curd etc. Milk in comparison to other food products such as egg and meat contain all the major food constituents such as carbohydrates, proteins, fats, minerals, water and vitamins such as A and D.<br />

(ii) It is high in fibre.<br />
Concentrates:<br />
(i) Concentrates are a mixture of substances which are rich in one or more nutrients.<br />
(ii) It is low in fibre.<br />

The daily average feed of a cow is given below:<br />

(ii) Grain mixture (Concentrates) = 4 to 5 Kg.<br />
(iii) Water = 30 to 35 litres.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 40:</span><br />
Artificial insemination; It generally gives improved breeds. This method is widely used to improve the qualities of cow, buffaloes, poultry, horse, sheep, goats and pigs. This method is economical, reliable and hygienic.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 41:</span><br />
(a) Cows are classified as draught, diary and dual purpose breeds.<br />
(i) Draught breeds &#8211; Their meat is tough and gives little milk. They are used in agricultural practices.<br />
(ii) Diary breeds &#8211; They have large digestive systems and gives large amount of milk.<br />
(iii) Dual breeds &#8211; These breeds provide milk as well as help in agricultural tasks.<br />
(b) Breeds of buffaloes &#8211; There are ten breeds of buffalo in our country. The important breeds of buffalo with high yield of milk are &#8211; Murrah, Mehsana and Surti.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 42:</span><br />
Steps involved in artificial insemination are:<br />
(i) The semen of healthy and tough animal of high milk yielding breed is collected.<br />
(ii) It is preserved by freezing or chemical methods.<br />
(iii) The preserved semen is then injected into the genital tract of the female animal.<br />
(iv) The preserved semen is injected during fertility period.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 43:</span><br />
Artificial insemination is the process of injecting the semen obtained from a desired male bull of high milk yielding breed into the genital or reproductive tract of female animal during heat period.<br />
Advantages:<br />
(i) It is economical because semen from a single bull can be used to impregnate several thousand cows.<br />
(ii) It gives high rate of successful fertilization.<br />

Poultry diseases can be prevented by giving good management practices. The growers require enough space as overcrowding tends to suppress their growth. Adequate lighting should be there. They should be provided with proper feed. Clean and hygienic conditions are must to keep them in good health and prevent them from diseases.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 50 :</span><br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
Plants as food are gift of nature to humans and most animals. Different parts of plants, such as root, stem, leaf, flower and fruit are consumed by humans in the form of cereals, vegetables, spices and fruits. Animals produce milk, egg, meat, etc. which also supplement our food requirements.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 2:</span><br />
Green revolution is the high production of food grains. The objectives of crop improvement are:<br />
(i) Crop production management.<br />
(ii) Crop variety improvement.<br />
(iii) Crop protection management.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 3:</span><br />
The cereals provide us with carbohydrates. The pulses provide us with proteins. Fruits and vegetables give us carbohydrates, protein, fat, vitamins, minerals and lots of fibers.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 4:</span><br />
The basic objective of mixed cropping is to minimize the risk and insure against the crop failure due to abnormal conditions.<br />
Criteria for the selection of crops for mixed cropping:<br />
(i) The different crops to be grown together are so selected that the products and waste materials from one crop stimulates the growth of the other crop.<br />
(ii) Care is taken to select crops that do not compete with each other for light, nutrients and water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 5 :</span><br />
Mixed Cropping:<br />
(i) It aims to minimize the risk of crop failure.<br />
(ii) Seeds of two crops are mixed before sowing.<br />
(iii) It involves no set pattern of rows of crops.<br />
Intercropping:<br />
(i) It aims to increase the productivity per unit area.<br />
(ii) Seeds of two crops are not mixed.<br />
(iii) It involves set pattern of rows of crops.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 6:</span><br />
Advantages of mixed cropping:<br />
(i) The risk of total crop failure due to uncertain monsoon is reduced.<br />
(ii) Chances of pest infestation are greatly reduced.<br />
(iii) Fertility of the soil is improved by growing two crops simultaneously.<br />
Disadvantages of mixed cropping:<br />
(i) Seeds of two crops are mixed before sowing and there is no definite pattern for sowing the seeds.<br />
(ii) Products of different crops are harvested, threshed, marketed and consumed in mixed form.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 7:</span><br />
Intercropping is the practice of growing two or more crops simultaneously in a same field in definite row patterns with the objective of increasing productivity per unit area.<br />
Mixed Cropping:<br />
(i) It aims to minimize the risk of crop failure.<br />
(ii) Seeds of two crops are mixed before sowing.<br />
(iii) It involves no set pattern of rows of crops.<br />
Intercropping:<br />
(i) It aims to increase the productivity per unit area.<br />
(ii) Seeds of two crops are not mixed.<br />
(iii) It involves set pattern of rows of crops.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 8:</span><br />
Disadvantages of crop rotation: Crops of the same family should not be repeatedly grown in the same field. This practice will promote build up of diseases and insect pests and decrease the similar nutrients from the soil.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 9: </span><br />
Criteria for the selection of crops for crop rotation:<br />
(i) Availability of moisture through rain or irrigation.<br />
(ii) Status of nutrients in the soil.<br />
(iii) Duration of crop &#8211; short or long.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 10:</span><br />
Leguminous crops are required in crop rotation as they are used to increase the soil fertility. Those crops which require high fertility level may be grown after growing legumes. They also replenish the soil with nitrogen content.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 11:</span><br />
The three steps involved in hybridization are:<br />
(i) Introduction &#8211; This refers to the transportation of crop plants from the place of cultivation to the place where they were grown earlier.<br />
(ii) Selection &#8211; This process involves the selection of most desirable offspring of a variety of plant for controlled propagation.<br />
(iii) Hybridisation &#8211; It involves the crossing between genetically dissimilar plants to produce a new kind. Crossing may be between two different varieties (intervarietal cross &#8211; breeding) or between the two different species of the same genus (inter specific cross &#8211; breeding) and between different genera (intergeneric cross &#8211; breeding).<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 12:</span><br />
Plant breeding means production of new varieties or strains by a programme of artificial selection spanning several generations of the organism concerned.<br />
It involves hybridization and mutation breeding.<br />
(i) Hybridisation &#8211; It involves the crossing between genetically dissimilar plants to produce a new kind. Crossing may be between two different varieties (intervarietal cross &#8211; breeding) or between the two different species of the same genus (inter specific cross &#8211; breeding) and between different genera (intergeneric cross &#8211; breeding).<br />
(ii) Mutation breeding &#8211; The breeding that takes place through various mutagens.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 13:</span><br />
Biological method of weed control involves the deliberate use of insects or some other organisms which consume and specifically destroy the weed plants.<br />
Example &#8211; Opuntia can be controlled by using cochineal insects in Maharashtra.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 14:</span><br />
Plant disease Occurrence Transmission<br />
(i) Blast Rice Air-borne<br />
(ii) Rust Wheat Air-borne<br />
(iii) Wilt Chick pea Soil-borne<br />
(iv) Stem rot Pigeon pea Water-borne<br />
(v) White rust Rice Mustard Air-borne<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 15:</span><br />
The ways by which the insects attack the crop plants are:<br />
(i) The chewing insects destroy all sorts of crop plants. They cut the root, stem and leaf of the crop plants by the help of their chewing mouth parts.<br />
(ii) Sucking insects suck the cell sap from various parts of the plant. They make fine punctures in the skin of plants with their needle &#8211; like, hollow beaks and suck the sap.<br />
(iii) The internal feeders live inside the plant parts. They make holes in the developing grains.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 16:</span><br />
Controlling insect pests:<br />
(i) Root cutting type of insects is controlled by mixing insecticides in the soil.<br />
Example &#8211; Chloropyriphos.<br />
(ii) Stem and leaf cutting type of insects can be controlled by dusting or spraying the contact insecticides.<br />
Example &#8211; Malathion, lindane and thiodan.<br />
(iii) All sap sucking insects can be controlled by spraying systematic insecticides.<br />
Example &#8211; Dimethoate and metasystox.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 17:</span><br />
(a) Example of narrow leaved rabi season weeds are &#8211; Cyperus rotundas and Wild sorghum.<br />
(b) Example of broad leaved kharif season weeds are &#8211; Amaranthus viridis and Trianthema.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 18:</span><br />
The various methods of weed control are:<br />
(i) Mechanical methods &#8211; These include uprooting, weeding with trowel or khurpi, hand hoeing, interculture, ploughing, burning and flooding.<br />
(ii) Cultural methods &#8211; This includes the proper bed preparation, timely sowing of crops, intercropping and crop rotation.<br />
(iii) Chemical methods &#8211; Herbicides and weedicides are sprayed on weeds to destroy weeds like &#8211; 2, 4 &#8211; D.<br />
(iv) Biological methods &#8211; Biological method of weed control involves the deliberate use of insects or some other organisms which consume and specifically destroy the weed plants. Example &#8211; Opuntia can be controlled by using cochineal insects in Maharashtra.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 19:</span><br />
Effect of weeds on crop plants:<br />
(i) The growth of weeds in the crop fields is harmful because they compete with the crops for nutrients, water, space and light.<br />
(ii) The weeds spread crop pests and diseases by acting as alternate host to insects and microorganisms.<br />
(iii) Some weeds may produce toxic substances which may interfere with the growth of crop plants.<br />
(iv) During harvesting weeds get mixed with crop&#8217;s produce to downgrade its quality.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 20:</span><br />
Crop&#8217;s pest is any destructive organism which causes great economic loss by destroying crop plants or products obtained from them.<br />
These can be controlled by the use of pesticides or biocides which includes insecticides, weedicides and fungicides. These chemicals are sprayed on crop plants or used for treating seeds and soil.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 21:</span><br />
Insect resistant varieties are advantageous as they do not get infested with pests. Their genes are modified so pests cannot harm them. Therefore, pesticides are not used to protect them diseases which are toxic in nature and cause environmental pollution.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
Manures:<br />
(i) They are organic in nature.<br />
(ii) They are generally insoluble in water.<br />
(iii) They are not nutrient specific.<br />
(iv) They are biodegradable.<br />
(v) They are voluminous and bulky, so difficult to store and carry.<br />
(vi) They provide humus to the soil.<br />
Examples &#8211; compost and green manure.<br />
Fertilizers:<br />
(i) They are inorganic in nature.<br />
(ii) They are generally soluble in water.<br />
(iii) They are nutrient specific.<br />
(iv) They are non-biodegradable.<br />
(v) They can be easily stored and are easy to carry.<br />
(vi) They do not provide humus to the soil.<br />
Examples &#8211; urea and ammonium sulphate.<br />
Advantages of Fertilizers:<br />
(i) They are easy to store, transport and apply to crops.<br />
(ii) Being soluble in water, they are readily absorbed by the crop plants.<br />
(iii) They are nutrient specific and can be selected according to the specific nature of the soil.<br />
Disadvantages of Fertilizers:<br />
(i) They are costly.<br />
(ii) These are the chemicals, which when washed away with rain water, pollute the water bodies.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 2:</span><br />
Mechanism of compost formation:<br />
(i) A trench of dimension of 4 to 5 m long, 1.5 to 1.8 m broad and 1.0 to 1.8 m deep is dug.<br />
(ii) A layer of well mixed refuse of about 30 cm thickness is spread in the trench.<br />
(iii) The refuse layer is well moistened by slurry of cow dung, earth and water.<br />
(iv) Now, a second layer of well mixed refuse is spread in trench till the heap rises to a height of 45 to 60 cm above the ground level.<br />
(v) The top of the heap is covered with a thin layer of moist earth.<br />
(vi) After three months, the material is taken out of the trench and placed in the form of conical heap. The conical heap, if required, be suitably moistened and should be covered with earth.<br />
(vii) Conical heap is left undisturbed for about one to two months. After this period, compost can be used in crop fields.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 3:</span><br />
Manures are rich in organic matter but are poor supplier of nutrients. So, the cultivated field which is not supplied with fertilizers may suffer from the deficiency of nutrients and not give very good yield.<br />
The cultivated field which is supplied with fertilizers only may face drainage problem and water logging due to lack of organic matter in the soil. This may harm the crop and the yield. Use of fertilizers over long periods of time can destroy the soil texture by killing the microorganisms that recycle nutrients in the soil.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 4:</span><br />
Irrigation is the process of supplying water to crop plants by means of canals, wells, reservoirs, tube-wells, etc.<br />
Irrigation is necessary in the areas where there is scarcity and irregular distribution of rain that can cause drought. It provides sufficient moisture for the germination of seeds, as seeds do not germinate in dry soil. It is also necessary for the growth and development of crop plants. The irrigation water tends to dissolve the nutrients present in the soil and forms a Solution which is easily absorbed by the roots of the plants.<br />
Excessive irrigation causes water logging and increases surface salinity. In water logged soil, plants do not get proper aeration.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 5:</span><br />
The various types of irrigation systems are &#8211;<br />
(i) Canal system: In this system, the human-made canals receive water from one or two reservoirs or from rivers. The main canal is distributed into branch canals which have further distributaries or field channels.<br />
(ii) Tanks: These are small storage reservoirs which catch and store the runoff of smaller catchment areas.<br />
(iii) Wells: These are of two types &#8211; dug wells and tube wells. In dug wells, water is collected from water bearing strata. The water from the shallow strata slowly accumulates in the pit and water is lifted by mechanical means. A tube well can tap water from the deeper strata.<br />
(iv) River lift system: It is more useful in the areas where canal flow is insufficient or irregular due to inadequate water release. In this system, water is directly drawn from the rivers for supplement irrigation.<br />
(v) River valley system: Certain parts of the country such as Karnataka and Kerala which lie along the Western Ghats use water that is discharged into the steep and narrow riverine valleys, during the rainy season. The bottom flat lands of the valleys are used for growing crops.<br />
(vi) Drip and sprinkler system: It employs the overhead pipes for spraying water.<br />
Efficiency of applied water can be increased by rain water harvesting and water shed management.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 6:</span><br />
Mixed Cropping:<br />
(i) It aims to minimize the risk of crop failure.<br />
(ii) Seeds of two crops are mixed before sowing.<br />
(iii) It involves no set pattern of rows of crops.<br />
(iv) Spraying for pest control to individual crop is difficult.<br />
Intercropping:<br />
(i) It aims to increase the productivity per unit area.<br />
(ii) Seeds of two crops are not mixed.<br />
(iii) It involves set pattern of rows of crops.<br />
(iv) Pesticides can be easily applied to individual crop.<br />
Advantages of mixed cropping:<br />
(i) The risk of total crop failure due to uncertain monsoon is reduced.<br />
(ii) Chances of pest infestation are greatly reduced.<br />
(iii) Fertility of the soil is improved by growing two crops simultaneously.<br />
Advantages of intercropping:<br />
(i) It makes better use of the natural resources of sunlight, land and water.<br />
(ii) Soil erosion is effectively arrested.<br />
(iii) The produce of each crop can be marketed and consumed separately.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 7 :</span><br />
Crop variety improvement is the manipulation of crop plants for increasing their yield and improving quality. Various approaches which are used for genetic improvement of crop plants are referred as plant breeding methods. These involve three processes:<br />
(i) Introduction &#8211; This refers to the transportation of crop plants from the place of cultivation to the place where grown earlier.<br />
(ii) Selection &#8211; This process involves the selection of most desirable offspring of a variety of plant for controlled propagation.<br />
(iii) Hybridisation &#8211; It involves the crossing between genetically dissimilar plants to produce a new kind. Crossing may be between two different varieties (intervarietal cross &#8211; breeding) or between the two different species of the same genus (inter specific cross &#8211; breeding) and between different genera (intergeneric cross &#8211; breeding).<br />
Crop:<br />
Rice<br />
Maize<br />
Soyabean<br />
Sunflower<br />
Mustard<br />
Improved Variety<br />
IR8<br />
Ganga 5<br />
PK 262<br />
BSH 1<br />
Pusa Bold</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ -08:</span><br />
Methods to control plant diseases:<br />
(i) Seed treatment with Thiram 2.5 g/kg to prevent blast of rice.<br />
(ii) Spraying Bavistin at 10 days interval to prevent wheat rust.<br />
(iii) Spraying Dithane M45 at 2 g/l water at 10 days interval to prevent wheat rust.<br />
(iv) Avoid water logging for fungus diseases.<br />
(v) Growing sorghum and pigeon pea mixed cropping to avoid stem rot.<br />
(vi) Spraying the crop with 0.2% Ziram and Maneb.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ -09:</span><br />
Preventive measures against insect pests:<br />
(i) Root cutting type of insects is controlled by mixing insecticides in the soil.<br />
Example &#8211; chloropyriphos.<br />
(ii) Stem and leaf cutting type of insects can be controlled by dusting or spraying the contact insecticides.<br />
Example &#8211; malathion, lindane and thiodan.<br />
(iii) All sap sucking insects can be controlled by spraying systematic insecticides.<br />
Example &#8211; dimethoate and metasystox.</p>
<p><span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ -10:</span><br />
The food eaten by animals is called feed.<br />
The animal feed is of two types:<br />
(i) Roughage &#8211; It largely contains fibres such as green fodder, silage, hay and legumes.<br />
(ii) Concentrates &#8211; It includes the mixture of substances which are rich in one or more nutrients. Concentrates are low in fibres and contains relatively high proteins and other nutrients. Example &#8211; oil seeds, cotton seeds, oats, barley, jowar, gram etc.<br />
Feed according to age and functions are:<br />
(i) Maintenance requirements &#8211; The food is required by the animal to support it to perform the basic functions of life.<br />
(ii) Milk producing requirements &#8211; It includes the type of food during lactation period. Maintenance part of the ration depends upon the body weight and age while milk production part is dependent upon the level and composition of milk.</p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page N0: 65</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 11:</span><br />
Artificial insemination is the process of injecting the semen obtained from a desired male bull of high milk yielding breed into the genital or reproductive tract of female animal during heat period.<br />
Steps involved in artificial insemination are:<br />
(i) The semen of healthy and tough animal of high milk yielding breed is collected.<br />
(ii) It is preserved by freezing or chemical methods.<br />
(iii) The preserved semen is then injected into the genital tract of the female animal.<br />
(iv) The preserved semen is injected during fertility period.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 12:</span><br />
Prevention of animal diseases:<br />
(i) The shelters should have roofed sheds which protects them from rain, heat, direct sunlight and cold.<br />
(ii) The shelters should be provided with cross ventilation.<br />
(iii) The floor of the cattle shed is made brick lined for facilitating cleaning and dry floor.<br />
(iv) Animals must be protected from diseases caused by virus, bacteria and fungi by giving them proper treatment and vaccinating them on time.<br />
(v) Proper nutritional requirements should be given to them so that they do not suffer from nutritional deficiency diseases.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 13:</span><br />
Honey bee lives in a colony and different tasks are done by different groups of bees in the same colony. According to their roles, there are three types of castes in the colony of bee:<br />
(i) Queen &#8211; The body size of queen is much larger than other castes of bees of the colony. Queen is responsible for laying eggs and lays upto 200 eggs everyday of each season.<br />
(ii) Drone &#8211; It is haploid, fertile male. These are larger in size than workers. They are stingless and their main role is to mate with queen and remain in colony to sleep and eat honey.<br />
(iii) Worker &#8211; Worker is diploid, sterile female. Its size is smallest among the caste of bees. They are the active members of the colony. For various outdoor and indoor chores, the workers are provided with a variety of organs such as hypopharyngeal glands (for secretion of bee milk), wax glands (for building cells of comb), pollen baskets on their hind legs (for collection of pollen), sucking type mouth parts (for collecting the nectar), high level secretion of invertase enzyme (in the honey sac for honey formation), a sting at the tip of the abdomen (for defence of the colony.<br />
Honey bees provide a good example of team work and division of labour.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 14:</span><br />
Italian bee is commonly domesticated in India to increase the yield of honey. It is preferred because:<br />
(i) It is gentle in nature.<br />
(ii) It has good honey collection capacity.<br />
(iii) It has the ability to protect itself from enemies.<br />
(iv) It has prolific queen with less swarming.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 15:</span><br />
The pasturage means the flowers available to the bees for nectar and pollen collection. In addition to adequate quantity of pasturage, the kinds of flowers available will determine the taste of the honey.<br />
Pasturage of honey bee includes a variety of flowering plants such as Mango, Cotton, Litchi, Shishame, Apple, Cashew, Coffee, Rubber plant, Sunflower, Neem, etc.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 16:</span><br />
For increasing production, the common feature in poultry, fisheries and bee keeping are:<br />
(i) Quality and quantity of x.<br />
(ii) Low maintenance requirement.<br />
(iii) Tolerance to high temperature.<br />
(iv) Care to prevent mortality.<br />
(v) To increase their productivity, cross breading should be done.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 17:</span><br />
Capture Fishery:<br />
(i) It is method of obtaining fish from natural resources.<br />
(ii) There is no seeding and raising of fish.<br />
(iii) It is undertaken in both inland and marine waters.<br />
Culture Fishery:<br />
(i) It is a method of obtaining fish from fish farming.<br />
(ii) The fish is seeded and reared.<br />
(iii) It is undertaken mostly inland and near sea shore.<br />
Inland Fishery:<br />
(i)It is a method of obtaining fish from fresh water resources such as canals, rivers, etc and brackish water resources where sea water and fresh water mix together.<br />
(ii) The fish is seeded and reared.<br />
(iii) Most fish production is through aquaculture.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 18:</span><br />
Worker &#8211; Worker is diploid, sterile female. Its size is smallest among the caste of bees. They are the active members of the colony. For various outdoor and indoor chores, the workers are provided with a variety of organs such as hypo pharyngeal glands (for secretion of bee milk), wax glands (for building cells of comb), pollen baskets on their hind legs (for collection of pollen), sucking type mouth parts (for collecting the nectar), high level secretion of invertase enzyme (in the honey sac for honey formation), a sting at the tip of the abdomen (for defence of the colony.<br />
The worker bees of a hive fall under 3 groups. These are:<br />
(i) Scavenger Bees &#8211; For the first three days each worker bees act as a scavenger.<br />
(ii) Nurse Bees &#8211; From the fourth day onwards each worker bee feeds the entire brood, like a foster mother, with a mixture of honey and pollen. By seventh day, its starts producing royal jelly, which is fed to the queen and future queen bees. They also perform guard duties.<br />
(iii) Foraging or Field bees &#8211; They explore new sources of nectar. They collect nectar, pollen and propolis. Nectar is changed into honey in the crops.</p>

<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 25</span><br />
(a) Diffusion:<br />
(i) Matter is made up of tiny particles<br />
(ii) The particles of matter are constantly moving.<br />
(b) Brownian motion:<br />
(i) The particles of matter are very, very small.<br />
(ii) The particles of matter are constantly moving.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 26</span><br />
Robert Brown suspended extremely small pollen grains in water and observed it through a microscope. It was found that pollen grains were moving very rapidly throughout the water in a very irregular way. He also observed that warmer the water, faster the pollen grains move on the surface of water. This phenomenon is known as the &#8216;Brownian Motion&#8217;.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 27</span><br />
It shows that each potassium permanganate crystal is made up of millions of small particles and particles of water have spaces between them.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 28</span><br />
Both bromine gas and air is made up of tiny moving particles. When a gas jar containing air is inverted over gas jar containing bromine vapour, both bromine and air molecules move and collide with one another and bounce about in all directions due to which we see a uniform red brown colour in both the jars.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 29</span><br />
When salt is added to water and stirred, the tiny salt particles break off from each solid salt granule and fill up the spaces available between the particles of water and mix with them.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 30</span><br />
Air is a gas whose particles are very far apart and there are very weak forces of attraction between them. Extremely weak forces between particles of air can be overcome easily due to which we can move our hand in air. On the other hand, the particles of a solid plank of wood are very closely packed and there are very strong forces of attraction between the particles of wood. Hence, it needs a huge outside force to overcome the strong inter particle attractions which only a karate expert can apply.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 31</span><br />
If two metal blocks are bound together tightly and kept undistributed for a few years, then the particles of one metal are found to have diffused into the other metal.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 32</span><br />
The diffusion between solids is a very, very slow process because the particles in solids do not move from their fixed positions.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 33</span><br />
Solids diffuse the slowest as the particles in solids do not move from their fixed positions.<br />
Gases diffuse the fastest as the particles in gases move very quickly in all directions.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 34</span><br />
The particles of gases produced by the burning of incense sticks move rapidly in all directions. They collide with the particles of air present in the room, mix with air and reach every part of the room quickly.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 35</span><br />
Three states of matter are:<br />
(i) The solid state &#8211; Ice.<br />
(ii) The liquid state &#8211; Water.<br />
(iii) The gas state &#8211; Air.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 36</span><br />
(a) Characteristics of a solid:<br />
(i) Solids have a fixed shape and fixed volume.<br />
(ii) Solids do not flow.<br />
(b) Characteristics of a liquid:<br />
(i) Liquids have a fixed volume but no fixed shape, they take the shape of the vessel in which they are placed.<br />
(ii) They generally flow easily.<br />
(c) Characteristics of a gas:<br />
(i) Gases can be compressed easily.<br />
(ii) Gases fill their container completely.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 37</span><br />
A gas does not have a fixed shape or fixed volume because the particles of gases do not have fixed positions or fixed spaces between them.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 38</span><br />
(i) Solids &#8211; They have a fixed shape and a fixed volume.<br />
(ii) Liquids &#8211; They have a fixed volume but no fixed shape.<br />
(iii) Gases &#8211; They neither have a fixed shape nor a fixed volume.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 39</span><br />
Oxygen&lt;Water&lt;Sugar.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 40</span><br />
(a) Water is a liquid at room temperature because:<br />
(i) Water has a fixed volume (which does not change on changing its container).<br />
(ii) Water has no fixed shape (it takes the shape of the container in which it is kept).<br />
(b) An iron almirah is a solid because:<br />
(i) It has a fixed shape (which cannot be changed by pressing it with hands).<br />
(ii) It has a fixed volume (which depends on the dimensions according to which it is made).<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 41</span><br />
(a) Diffusion.<br />
(b) The smell of food being cooked reaches the other room by the diffusion of gases released into the air during the cooking of food.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 42</span><br />
(a) Diffusion in gases shows that their particles move very quickly in all directions and the rate of diffusion of a gas depends on its density. Light gases diffuse faster than heavy gases.<br />
(b) Gases like carbon dioxide and oxygen present in the atmosphere diffuse into water (of ponds, lakes etc) and dissolves in it.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 43</span><br />
The smell of hot sizzling food reaches us quickly as compared to cold food because the rate of diffusion of hot gases (released by hot sizzling food) into air is faster than that of cold gases released by cold food.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 44</span><br />
The smell of food being cooked reaches us even from a considerable distance is because of the process of diffusion.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 45</span><br />
The smell of perfume spreads due to the diffusion of perfume vapours into the air.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 46</span><br />
The spreading of blue colour of copper sulphate into water, on its own, is due to the diffusion of copper sulphate particles into water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 47</span><br />
The force of attraction between the particles of honey is much more than the force of attraction between the particles of water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 48</span><br />
(a) Air is used to inflate tyres because when we blow air into a tyre the air particles push the tyre walls from inside and exerts pressure on them.<br />
(b) Steel is used to make railway lines because steel is a rigid object having a definite shape and definite volume.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 49</span><br />
Diffusion occurs more quickly in gases than in a liquid because the particles in gases move very quickly in all directions whereas the particles in liquids move slowly as compared to the gas particles.<br />
<strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Class 9 solutions Page No: 20</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 50</span><br />
(a) The spreading out and mixing of a substance due to the motion of its particles is called diffusion. For example: Smell of food being cooked in the kitchen reaches us even from a considerable distance.<br />
(b) Gases diffuse very fast because the particles in gases move very quickly in all directions.<br />
(c) Carbon dioxide and Oxygen gas dissolve in water by diffusion. This process is important as these gases are essential for the survival of aquatic plants and animals. The aquatic plants use the dissolved carbon dioxide for preparing food by photosynthesis and aquatic animals use the dissolved oxygen in water for breathing.<br />

(b) (i) Wood is a rigid object which has a tendency to maintain its shape when subjected to outside force.<br />
(ii) It has a definite shape and definite volume.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 52</span><br />
(a) Because of high energy and negligible forces of attraction, the particles of a gas move with high speed in all directions. Thus, the pressure exerted by a gas is due to the constant collisions of the fast moving gas particles against the walls of the container.<br />
(b) The particles of a gas have high kinetic energy and negligible forces of attraction amongst them. Due to this, the particles of a gas are constantly moving with high speeds in all the directions and the gas completely fills the vessel in which it is kept.<br />
(c) Gases can be compressed easily because its particles are far apart and there are large spaces between them (which can be reduced by compression).<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 53</span><br />
(a) Anything which occupies space and has mass is called matter.<br />
Examples: Air, water, sugar, iron.<br />
(b) The characteristics of matter are:<br />
(i) The particles of matter are very, very small.<br />
(ii) The particles of matter have spaces between them.<br />
(iii) The particles of matter are constantly moving.<br />
(iv) The particles of matter attract each other.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 54</span><br />

(b) These dust particles move in a haphazard way because they are constantly hit by the fast moving particles of air.<br />

Bromine diffuses slowly into air because the motion of bromine molecules is obstructed due to the collisions with the moving molecules of air. Bromine diffuses very rapidly into vacuum because there is &#8216;nothing&#8217; in the vacuum to oppose the motion of bromine molecules.<br />

Chlorine will diffuse faster than bromine vapour. This is because light gases diffuse faster than heavy gases.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 24</span><br />
The heat energy that has to applied to change the state of a substance is called &#8216;latent heat&#8217;. They are of two types:<br />
(i) Latent heat of fusion and (ii) Latent heat of vaporization.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 25</span><br />
When a solid is heated, the heat energy makes its particles vibrate more vigorously. At the melting point, the particles of solid have sufficient energy to overcome the strong forces of attraction holding them in fixed positions and break to form small groups of particles. This heat energy is kinetic energy.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 26</span><br />
When a change of state of a substance has to take place the heat given would not raise the temperature.<br />
<strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Class 9 solutions Page No: 37</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 27</span><br />
The heat energy supplied to ice during the change of state (at its melting point) is all used up in overcoming (or breaking) the force of attraction between its particles without increasing its kinetic energy. Since the heat (or latent heat) supplied during the change of state does not increase the kinetic energy of the ice cubes, therefore no rise in temperature takes place. The temperature remains constant.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 28</span><br />
The heat energy supplied to water during the change of state (at its boiling point) is all used up in overcoming (or breaking) the force of attraction between its particles without increasing its kinetic energy. Since the heat (or latent heat) supplied during the change of state does not increase the kinetic energy of the water, therefore no rise in temperature takes place. The temperature remains constant.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 29</span><br />
This is due to the fact that for melting, each kilogram of ice takes its latent heat of 3.34 x 105 joules from the substance and hence cools the substance more effectively. On the other hand, water at 0o cannot take any such latent heat from the substance.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 30</span><br />
We would place ice in the water to cool it more quickly because the ice takes its latent heat from the water and hence cools it more effectively. On the other hand, if we keep the water on ice then the latent heat would be taken from the surrounding air hence releasing its coolness to the surrounding and not the water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 31</span><br />
Steam causes more severe burns than boiling water because the steam contains more heat, in the form of latent heat, than boiling water. Hence, when steam falls on our skin and condenses to produce water, it gives out 22.5 x 105 Joules per kilogram more heat than boiling water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 32</span><br />
The latent heat of fusion of ice is 3.34 x 105 J/Kg. It means that 3.34x 105 joules of heat is required to change 1 Kg of ice at its melting point of 0oC into water at the same temperature (of 0oC). This means that 1 Kg of ice at 0oC has 3.34 x 105 joules of less heat than 1 kg of water at the same temperature of 0oC.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 33</span><br />
1 Kg of steam at 100oC has more heat than water at the same temperature because when water changes into steam, it absorbs latent heat, but when steam condenses to form water, an equal amount of latent heat is given out.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 34</span><br />
It is because of the fact that steam at 100oC contains more heat, in the form of latent heat, than boiling water at 100oC. Hence, steam would give out 22.5 x 105 joules per kilogram more heat than boiling water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 35</span><br />
Steam causes more severe burns than boiling water because the steam contains more heat, in the form of latent heat, than boiling water. Hence, when steam falls on our skin and condenses to produce water it gives out 22.5 x 105 joules per kilogram more heat than boiling water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 36</span><br />
The temperature of a substance remains constant during the change of state because the heat gets used up in changing the state by overcoming the forces of attraction between the particles.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 37</span><br />
(a) Either solid (as ice) or liquid as 0oC is the melting point of ice as well as the freezing point of water.<br />

The temperature of a substance remains constant during the change of state though heat is supplied continuously because the heat gets used up in changing the state by overcoming the forces of attraction between the particles.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 39</span><br />
The temperature, at which a solid substance melts and changes into a liquid at atmospheric pressure, is called melting point of the substance. The melting point of ice is 0oC.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 40</span><br />
The temperature, at which a liquid boils and changes rapidly into a gas at atmospheric pressure, is called boiling point of the liquid. The boiling point of water is 100oC.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 41</span><br />
(a) Melting &#8211; The process in which a solid substance changes into a liquid on heating is called melting.<br />
(b) Boiling &#8211; The process in which a liquid substance changes into a gas rapidly on heating is called boiling.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 42</span><br />
(a) Condensation &#8211; The process of changing a gas (or vapour) to a liquid by cooling is called condensation.<br />
(b) Freezing &#8211; The process of changing a liquid into a solid by cooling, is called freezing.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 43</span><br />
This happens because naphthalene balls undergo sublimation. The naphthalene balls keep on forming naphthalene vapours slowly which disappear into the air.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 44</span><br />
Gases can be liquefied by applying pressure and lowering temperature. The temperature needs to be lowered because when the gas is compressed too much, then heat is produced due to compression. Cooling lowers the temperature of the compressed gas and helps in liquefying it.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 45</span><br />
Ammonia gas is liquefied by applying high pressure and lowering the temperature of the gas. Lowering the temperature is done by continuously pouring water over the coils carrying the compressed gas.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 46</span><br />
There is a lot of space between the particles of a gas. If enough pressure is applied to the gas, it gets highly compressed. The particles of gas get so close together that they start attracting each other sufficiently to form a liquid. And we say that the gas has liquefied.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 47</span><br />
On a hot day, when our body temperature tends to rise too much, our sweat glands give out moisture (sweat) on our skin. When this sweat evaporates, it takes the latent heat of vaporization from our body hence making our body cool.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 48</span><br />
All water on earth does not get evaporated on hot summer days because of the high value of latent heat of vaporization of water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 49</span><br />
Liquids like alcohol, petrol and perfume are volatile (which can change into vapours easily). When we apply alcohol to the back of our hand, we find that it dries up quickly and while it is drying, the hands feel cold. This happens due to the fact that to change from liquid to the vapour state, alcohol requires latent heat of vaporization. The alcohol takes this latent heat of vaporization from the hand due to which the hand loses heat and we feel cold.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 50</span><br />
The cooling in a desert room cooler is caused by the evaporation of water. The higher temperature on a hot day increases the rate of evaporation of water, and the dryness of air also increases the rate of evaporation of water. And due to this increased rate of evaporation of water, a desert room cooler works better on a hot and dry day.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 51</span><br />
The earthen pot (or matka) has a large number of extremely small pores on its walls. Some of the water kept in the earthen pot continuously keeps seeping through these pores to the outside of the pot. This water evaporates continuously by taking the latent heat of vaporization from the earthen pot and the remaining water. In this way, the earthen pot and remaining water loses heat and gets cooled.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 52</span><br />
We should wear cotton clothes in hot summer days because we perspire more through the pores of the skin during such days. Since, sweat is mainly water and cotton clothes are good absorber of water, they absorb the sweat quickly and expose it to the atmosphere for evaporation. The evaporation of sweat from the cotton clothes takes the latent heat of vaporization from our skin hence the skin loses heat and makes us feel cool and comfortable.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 53</span><br />
If the hot tea or milk is taken in a cup, then due to the narrow shape of the cup, the surface area of hot tea in the cup is comparatively small. Due to this, the evaporation of hot tea is slow; cooling caused by evaporation is less and hence the hot tea remains appreciably hot for a much longer time. On the other hand, the saucer has a large surface area due to which the tea taken in the saucer evaporates much faster, thus cooling it quickly and making it convenient to sip or drink.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 54</span><br />
Acetone (or perfume) is volatile in nature. When we apply it to our palm, we feel cold. This happens due to the fact that to change from liquid to the vapour state, acetone requires latent heat of vaporization. Acetone takes this latent heat of vaporization from the hand due to which the palm loses heat and feels cold.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 55</span><br />
The presence of water vapour in air can be demonstrated by the following experiment: We take a steel tumbler and put some well crushed ice in it. Allow the steel tumbler to stand undisturbed for about 5 minutes with the ice in it. We would observe that a large number of tiny drops of water appear on the outer surface of the steel tumbler. This happens because the air around the steel tumbler contains water vapour in it. When these water vapour come in contact with the cold, outside surface of steel tumbler, they condense to form tiny drops of liquid.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">solution 56</span><br />
(a) The latent heat of fusion of a solid is the quantity of heat in joules required to convert 1 Kg of the solid (at its melting point) to liquid, without any change in temperature. The latent heat of fusion of ice is 3.34 x 105 J/Kg.<br />
