<h1>
<font color="white">
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 1:</strong></span><br />
Is displacement a scalar quantity ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
No, displacement is a vector quantity.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 2:</strong></span><br />
State whether distance is a scalar or a vector quantity.<br \/>
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Distance is a scalar quantity.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 3:</strong></span><br />
Change the speed of 6 m/s into km/h.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
6 m/s<br />
= 6 x (3600/1000) km/hr = 21.6km/hr</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 4:</strong></span><br />
What name is given to the speed in a specified direction ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Speed of a body in a specified direction is called velocity.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 5:</strong></span><br />
Give two examples of bodies having non-uniform motion.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Motion of a bus on a road<br />
(b) Motion of a racing horse</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 6:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity obtained by dividing &#8216;Distance travelled&#8217; by &#8216;Time taken&#8217; to travel that distance.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Speed is defined as the distance travelled per unit time.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 7:</strong></span><br />
What do the following measure in a car ?<br />
(a) Speedometer (b) Odometer<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a)The speedometer of a car measures instantaneous speed of the car.<br />
(b)Odometer is a device used to record the distance travelled by the car.</p>
<p><span style="color: brown;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:20</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 8:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity which gives us an idea of how slow or fast a body is moving.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Speed gives an idea of how slow or fast a body is moving.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 9:</strong></span><br />
Under what conditions can a body travel a certain distance and yet its resultant displacement be zero ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When the body comes back to its starting point, it has zero resultant displacement but covers a certain non-zero distance.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 10:</strong></span><br />
In addition to speed, what else should we know to predict the position of a moving body ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
In addition to speed, we should know the direction in which the body is moving.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 11:</strong></span><br />
When is a body said to have uniform velocity ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a body covers equal distances in equal intervals of time in a particular direction however small or big the time interval may be, the object is said to have uniform velocity.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 12:</strong></span><br />
Under which condition is the magnitude of average velocity equal to average speed ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When the object moves in a single straight line, t he magnitude of average velocity equal to average speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 13:</strong></span><br />
Which of the two can be :zero under certain conditions : average speed of a moving body or average velocity of a moving body ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Average velocity of a moving body can be zero.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 14:</strong></span><br />
Give one example of a situation in which a body has a certain average speed but its average velocity is zero.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Motion of a boy from his home to shop (in one direction) and back to home (in its reverse direction) is an example of a situation in which a body has a certain average speed but its average velocity is zero.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 15:</strong></span><br />
What is the acceleration of a body moving with uniform velocity ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a body is moving with uniform velocity, its acceleration is zero.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 16:</strong></span><br />
What is the other name of negative acceleration ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Negative acceleration is also called retardation.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 17:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity whose SI unit is :<br />
(a) m/s (b) m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Speed (or Velocity)<br />
(b) Acceleration</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 18:</strong></span><br />
What <a>type of motion</a> is exhibited by a freely falling body ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Uniformly accelerated motion</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 19:</strong></span><br />
What is the SI unit of retardation ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
S.I. unit of retardation is m/s<sup>2</sup>.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 20:</strong></span><br />
Fill in the following blanks with suitable words :<br />
(a) Displacement is a&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230; quantity whereas distance is a&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;.<br />
(b) The physical quantity which gives both, the speed and direction of motion of a body is called its&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;..<br />
(c) A motorcycle has a steady&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;. of 3 m/s<sup>2</sup>. This means that every&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;. its&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;.. increases by&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;.<br />
(d) Velocity is the rate of change of&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230; It is measured in .<br />
(e) Acceleration is the rate of change of&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;&#8230;. It is measured in<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) vector, scalar<br />
(b) velocity<br />
(c) acceleration, second, velocity, 3m/s<br />
(d) displacement, m/s<br />
(e) velocity, m/s<sup>2</sup></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 21:</strong></span><br />
What type of motion, uniform or non-uniform, is exhibited by a freely falling body ? Give reason for your solution.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
A freely falling body has non-uniform motion because it covers smaller distances in the initial &#8216;1 second&#8217; intervals and larger distances in the later &#8216;1 second&#8217; intervals, i.e., it covers unequal distances in equal intervals of time.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 22:</strong></span><br />
State whether speed is a scalar or a vector quantity. Give reason for your choice.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Speed is a scalar quantity as it has magnitude only, it has no specified direction.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 23:</strong></span><br />
Bus X travels a distance of 360 km in 5 hours whereas bus Y travels a distance of 476 km in 7 hours. Which<br />
bus travels faster ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
For bus X,<br />
Speed= Distance/Time<br />
Speed=360/5=72km/h<br />
For bus Y,<br />
Speed= Distance/Time<br />
Speed=476/7=68 km/h<br />
Speed of bus X is more than that of bus Y. Hence, bus X travels faster.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 24:</strong></span><br />
Arrange the following speeds in increasing order (keeping the least speed first):</p>
<ol>
<li>An athlete running with a speed of 10 m/s.</li>
<li>A bicycle moving with a speed of 200 m/min.</li>
<li>A scooter moving with a speed of 30 km/h.</li>
</ol>
<p><span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Speed of athelete = 10 m/s<br />
Speed of bicycle = 200 m/min = 200/60 m/s = 3.33 m/s<br />
Speed of scooter = 30 km/h = 30000/3600 m/s = 8.33 m/s<br />
3.33 m/s &lt; 8.33 m/s &lt; 10 m/s<br />
i.e. 200 m/min &lt; 30 km/h &lt; 10 m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 25:</strong></span><br />
(a) Write the formula for acceleration. Give the meaning of each symbol which occurs in it.<br />
(b) A train starting from Railway Station attains a speed of 21 m/s in one minute. Find its acceleration.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7632/16920132496_80b42910fb_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q25" width="322" height="237" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 26:</strong></span><br />
(a) What term is used to denote the change of velocity with time ?<br />
(b) Give one word which means the same as &#8216;moving with a negative acceleration&#8217;.<br />
(c) The displacement of a moving object in a given interval of time is zero. Would the distance travelled by the object also be zero ? Give reason for your solution.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Acceleration<br />
(b) Retardation<br />
(c) No, because if a body takes a round trip such that its final position is same as the starting position, then the displacement of the body is zero but the distance travelled is non-zero.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 27:</strong></span><br />
A snail covers a distance of 100 metres in 50 hours. Calculate the average speed of snail in km/h.<br />
<img class="" src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4305/35412746483_29ba611c25_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-1" width="699" height="220" /><br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Average speed = Total distance travelled/ Total time taken<br />
Total distance travelled = 100m = 0.1 km; Total time taken = 50 hr<br />
Average speed= 0.1/50=0.002km/h</p>
<p><span style="color: brown;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:21</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 28:</strong></span><br />
A tortoise moves a distance of 100 metres in 15 minutes. What is the average speed of tortoise in km/h ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Total distance=100m =0.1 km<br />
Total time taken=15 minutes= 15/60=0.25 hour<br />
Average speed = Total distance travelled/ Total time taken<br />
=0.1/0.25= 0.4km/h</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 29:</strong></span><br />
If a sprinter runs a distance of 100 metres in 9.83 seconds, calculate his average speed in km/h.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Total distance travelled =100m<br />
Total time taken = 9.83 sec<br />
Average speed = Total distance travelled/ Total time taken<br />
=100/9.83 =10.172m/s<br />
Averge speed in km/h:<br />
10.172 x(3600/1000)=36.62 km/h</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 30:</strong></span><br />
A motorcyclist drives from place A to B with a uniform speed of 30 km h<sup>-1</sup> and returns from place B to A with a uniform speed of 20 km h<sup>-1</sup>. Find his average speed.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8728/16323692294_e143646723_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q30" width="449" height="298" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 31:</strong></span><br />
A motorcyclist starts from rest and reaches a speed of 6 m/s after travelling with uniform acceleration for 3 s. What is his acceleration ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Initial velocity= 0m/s<br />
Final velocity=6m/s<br />
Time=3 sec<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7635/16920132416_543f85edf2_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q31" width="300" height="128" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 32:</strong></span><br />
An aircraft travelling at 600 km/h accelerates steadily at 10 km/h per second. Taking the speed of sound as 1100 km/h at the aircraft&#8217;s altitude, how long will it take to reach the &#8216;sound barrier&#8217; ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Initial velocity, u = 600 km/h<br />
Final velocity, v = 1100 km/h<br />
Acceleration = 10 km/h/s = 600 km/h<sup>2</sup><br />
From relation, a = (v-u)/t<br />
t = (v-u)/a<br />
t = (1100-600)/600 = 500/600 = 5/6 hr = 50 sec</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 33:</strong></span><br />
If a bus travelling at 20 m/s is subjected to a steady deceleration of 5 m/s<sup>2</sup>, how long will it take to come to rest ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Deceleration, a=-5m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Initial velocity, u=20m/s<br />
Final velocity, v=0m/s<br />
t=?<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8742/16326021053_80cf51de05_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q33" width="230" height="193" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 34:</strong></span><br />
(a) What is the difference between &#8216;distance travelled&#8217; by a body and its &#8216;displacement&#8217; ? Explain with the<br />
help of a diagram.<br />
(b) An ant travels a distance of 8 cm from P to Q and then moves a distance of 6 cm at right angles to PQ. Find its resultant displacement.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Distance travelled is the actual length of the indirect path covered by the body whereas displacement refers to the straight line path between the initial and final positions. For e.g. In the figure given below, a body moves from point A to point B and then from point B to point C. Here, the distance travelled by the body is AB + BC and displacement is AC.<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7592/16946086475_7ea6da1a49_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q34" width="386" height="366" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 35:</strong></span><br />
Define motion. What do you understand by the terms &#8216;uniform motion&#8217; and &#8216;non-uniform motion&#8217; ? Explain with examples.<br />
(a) Define speed. What is the SI unit of speed ?<br />
(b) What is meant by (i) average speed, and (ii) uniform speed ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
A body is said to be in motion when its position changes continuously with respect to a stationary object taken as reference point.<br />
A body has uniform motion if it travels equal distances in equal intervals of time, no matter how small these time intervals may be. For example: a car running at a constant speed of 10m/s, will cover equal distance of 10m every second, so its motion will be uniform.<br />
Non-uniform motion: A body has a non-uniform motion if it travels unequal distances in equal intervals of time. For example: dropping a ball from the roof of a tall building .</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 36:</strong></span><br />
(a) Define velocity. What is the SI unit of velocity ?<br />
(b) What is the difference between speed and velocity ?<br />
(c) Convert a speed of 54 km/h into m/s.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Speed of a body is the distance travelled by it per unit time. The SI unit of speed is m/s.<br />
(b) (i) Average speed of a body is the total distance travelled divided by the total time taken to cover this distance.<br />
(ii) Uniform speed refers to the constant speed of a moving body. A body has a uniform speed if it travels equal distance in equal intervals of time, no matter how small these time intervals may be.<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7623/16758634390_2630404b2d_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q36" width="806" height="105" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 37:</strong></span><br />
(a) What is meant by the term &#8216;acceleration&#8217; ? State the SI unit of acceleration.<br />
(b) Define the term &#8216;uniform acceleration&#8217;. Give one example of a uniformly accelerated motion.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Velocity of a body is the distance travelled by it per unit time in a given direction. SI unit of velocity is m/s.<br />
( b)(i)Speed is a scalar quantity whereas velocity is a vector quantity.<br />
(ii) Speed of a body is distance travelled by it per unit time whereas velocity of a body is the distance travelled by it per unit time in a given direction.<br />
(iii)Speed is always positive whereas velocity can be both positive as well as negative.<br />
(c) Speed = 54km/h = 54 x (1000/3600) = 15m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 38:</strong></span><br />
The distance between Delhi and Agra is 200 km. A train travels the first 100 km at a speed of 50 km/h. How fast must the train travel the next 100 km, so as to average 70 km/h for the whole journey ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Acceleration of a body is defined as the rate of change of its velocity with time. SI unit of acceleration is m/s<sup>2</sup>.<br />
(b) A body has uniform acceleration if it travels in a straight line and its velocity increases by equal amounts in equal intervals of time. For example: Motion of a freely falling body.</p>

A train travels the first 15 km at a uniform speed of 30 km/h; the next 75 km at a uniform speed of 50 km/h; and the last 10 km at a uniform speed of 20 km/h. Calculate the average speed for the entire train journey.<br />

(ii) What is the resultant displacement ?<br />

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 58:</strong></span><br />
A boy walks from his classroom to the bookshop along a straight corridor towards North. He covers a distance of 20 m in 25 seconds to reach the bookshop. After buying a book, he travels the same distance in the same time to reach back in the classroom. Find (a) average speed, and (b) average velocity, of the boy.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) Total distance covered in going to the bookshop and coming back to the classroom = 20 + 20 = 40m<br />
Total time taken= 25 + 25 = 50 sec<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7635/16945109641_d032e424d6_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q58" width="581" height="182" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 59:</strong></span><br />
A car travels 100 km at a speed of 60 km/h and returns with a speed of 40 km/h. Calculate the average speed for the whole journey.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
In the first case, car travels at a speed of 60 km/h for a distance of 100 km<br />
In the second case, car travels at a speed of 40 km/h for a distance of 100 km<br />
Total distance travelled = 200 km<br />

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 60:</strong></span><br />
A ball hits a wall horizontally at 6.0 m s<sup>-1</sup>. It rebounds horizontally at 4.4 m s<sup>-1</sup>. The ball is in contact with the wall for 0.040 s. What is the acceleration of the ball ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Initial velocity, u=6m/s<br />
Final velocity ,v=-4.4m/s(the ball rebounds in opposite direction)<br />
Time, t = 0.040 s<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7627/16758634010_048c40a465_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-Q60" width="380" height="88" /><br />

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 1:</strong></span><br />
(a) What remains constant in uniform circular motion ?<br />
(b) What changes continuously in uniform circular motion ? &#8216;<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a)Speed<br />
(b)Direction of motion</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 2:</strong></span><br />
State whether the following statement is true or false :<br />
Earth moves round the sun with uniform velocity.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
No, earth moves round the sun with uniform speed, but its velocity changes continuously.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 3:</strong></span><br />
A body goes round the sun with constant speed in a circular orbit. Is the motion uniform or accelerated ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The motion is accelerated.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 4:</strong></span><br />
What conclusion can you draw about the velocity of a body from the displacement-time graph shown below :<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4297/36176711356_dc5c477655_m.jpg" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-2" width="189" height="177" /><br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
It represents uniform velocity.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 5:</strong></span><br />
Name the quantity which is measured by the area occupied under the velocity-time graph.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Distance travelled by the moving body .</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 6:</strong></span><br />
What does the slope of a speed-time graph indicate ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The slope of a speed-time graph indicates acceleration.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 7:</strong></span><br />
What does the slope of a distance-time graph indicate ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The slope of a distance-time graph indicates speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 8:</strong></span><br />
Give one example of a motion where an object does not change its speed but its direction of motion changes continuously.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Motion of moon around the earth.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 9:</strong></span><br />
Name the type of motion in which a body has a constant speed but not constant velocity.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Uniform circular motion.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 10:</strong></span><br />
What can you say about the motion of a body if its speed-time graph is a straight line parallel to the time axis ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The Speed of the body is constant or uniform.</p>
<p><span style="color: brown;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:40</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 11:<br />
</strong></span>What conclusion can you draw about the speed of a body from the following distance-time graph ?<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4295/35383358944_1785ce016d_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-3" width="198" height="172" /><br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The body has uniform speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 12:<br />
</strong></span>What can you say about the motion of a body whose distance-time graph is a straight line parallel to the time axis ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The body is not moving. It is stationary.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 13:<br />

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 14:<br />
</strong></span>A satellite goes round the earth in a circular orbit with constant speed. Is the motion uniform or accelerated ?<br />
<img class="" src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4316/36052176932_fb9861dc57_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-5" width="704" height="407" /><br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
It is accelerated motion as the velocity is changing continuously.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 15:<br />
</strong></span>What type of motion is represented by the tip of the &#8216;seconds&#8217; hand&#8217; of a watch ? Is it uniform or accelerated ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The tip of the &#8216;seconds&#8217; hand&#8217; of a watch represents uniform circular motion. It is an accelerated motion.</p>

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 17:<br />
</strong></span>Is the uniform circular motion accelerated ? Give reasons for your solution<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Yes, uniform circular motion is accelerated because the velocity changes due to continuous change in the direction of motion.</p>

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 19:<br />
</strong></span>Explain why, the motion of a body which is moving with constant speed in a circular path is said to be accelerated.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The motion of a body which is moving with constant speed in a circular path is said to be accelerated because its velocity changes continuously due to the continuous change in the direction of motion.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 20:<br />
d2</strong></span>What is the difference between uniform linear motion and uniform circular motion ? Explain with examples.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Uniform linear motion is uniform motion along a linear path or a straight line. T he direction of motion is fixed. So, it is not accelerated. For e.g.: a car running with uniform speed of 10km/hr on a straight road.<br />
Uniform circular motion is uniform motion along a circular path. T he direction of motion changes continuously. So, it is accelerated. For e.g.: motion of earth around the sun.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 21:<br />
</strong></span>State an important characteristic of uniform circular motion. Name the force which brings about uniform circular motion.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
An important characteristic of uniform circular motion is that the direction of motion in it changes continuously with time, so it is accelerated.<br />
Centripetal force brings about uniform circular motion.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 22:<br />
</strong></span>Find the initial velocity of a car which is stopped in 10 seconds by applying brakes. The retardation due to brakes is 2.5 m/s<sup>2</sup>.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Initial velocity, u=?<br />
Final velocity, v=0m/s (car is stopped)<br />
Retardation, a=-2.5 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Time, t=10s<br />
v=u + at<br />
0=u +(-2.5)x 10<br />
u=25m/s</p>

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 38:<br />
</strong></span>Show by means of graphical method that: v = u + at, where the symbols have their usual meanings.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Consider the velocity-time graph of a body shown in figure.<br />
The body has an initial velocity u at a point A and then its velocity changes at a uniform rate from A to B in time t. In other words, there is a uniform acceleration a from A to B, and after time t its final velocity becomes v which is equal to BC in the graph. The time t is represented by OC. To complete the figure, we draw the perpendicular CB from point C, and draw AD parallel to OC. BE is the perpendicular from point B to OE.<br />
Now, Initial velocity of the body, u= OA &#8212;&#8211;(1)<br />
And,Final velocity of the body, v=BC &#8212;&#8212;(2)<br />
But from the graph BC =BD + DC<br />
Therefore, v=BD + DC &#8212;&#8212;(3)<br />
Again DC = OA<br />
So,v =BD + OA<br />
Now, from equation (1), OA =u<br />
So, v=BD + u &#8212;&#8212;(4)<br />
We should find out the value of BD now. We know the slope of a velocity-time graph is equal to the acceleration, a.<br />
Thus,Acceleration, a= slope of line AB<br />
<sub>or a = BD/AD</sub><br />
But AD =OC= t, so putting t in place of AD in the above relation, we get:<br />
or BD=at<br />
Now, putting this value of BD in equation(4), we get:<br />
v= u+ at<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7621/16758635210_e85ef51535_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q38" width="810" height="529" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 39:<br />
</strong></span>Show by using the graphical method that:\(s=ut+\frac { 1 }{ 2 } { at }^{ 2 }\) where the symbols have their usual meanings.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Consider the velocity-time graph of a body shown in figure. The body has an initial velocity u at a point A and then its velocity changes at a uniform rate from A to B in time t. In other words, there is a uniform acceleration a from A to B, and after time t its final velocity becomes v which is equal to BC in the graph. The time t is represented by OC.<br />
Suppose the body travels a distance s in time t. In the figure, the distance travelled by the body is given by the area of the space between the velocity-time graph AB and the time axis OC, which is equal to the area of the figure OABC. Thus:<br />
Distance travelled = Area of figure OABC<br />
= Area of rectangle OADC + area of triangle ABD<br />
Now, we will find out the area of rectangle OADC and area of triangle ABD.<br />
(i) Area of rectangle OADC =OA x OC<br />
= u x t<br />
=ut<br />
(ii) Area of triangle ABD= <sub>(1/2)</sub>x Area of rectangle AEBD<br />
= <sub>(1/2) </sub> x AD x BD<br />
= <sub>(1/2)</sub> x t x at<br />
= <sub>(1/2)</sub> at<sup>2</sup><br />
Distance travelled, s = Area of rectangle OADC + area of triangle ABD<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8749/16738731977_9b9dc0501b_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q39" width="810" height="499" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 40:<br />
</strong></span>Derive the following equation of motion by the graphical method : v<sup>2</sup> = u<sup>2</sup> + 2as, where the symbols have their usual meanings.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Consider the velocity-time graph of a body shown in figure. The body has an initial velocity u at a point A and then its velocity changes at a uniform rate from A to B in time t. In other words, there is a uniform acceleration a from A to B, and after time t its final velocity becomes v which is equal to BC in the graph. The time t is represented by OC. To complete the figure, we draw the perpendicular CB from point C, and draw AD parallel to OC. BE is the perpendicular from point B to OE.<br />
The distance travelled s by a body in time t is given by the area of the figure OABC which is a trapezium.<br />
Distance travelled, s= Area of trapezium OABC<br />
Now, OA + CB = u + v and OC =t Putting these values in the above relation, we get:<br />
Eliminate t from the above equation. This can be done by obtaining the value of t from the first equation of motion.<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7616/16326021743_6916941174_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q40" width="808" height="468" /></p>

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 53:<br />
</strong></span>The graph given alongside shows the positions of a body at different times. Calculate the speed of the body as it moves from :<br />
(i) A to B,<br />
(ii) B to C, and<br />
(iii) C to D.<br />
<img class="alignnone" src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4322/35384087584_671f97cbda_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-6" width="221" height="216" /><br />

(ii) The speed of the body as it moves from B to C is zero.<br />
(iii) The distance covered from C to D is (7-3)=4 cm<br />

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 54:<br />
</strong></span>What can you say about the motion of a body if:<br />
(a) its displacement-time graph is a straight line ?<br />
(b) its velocity-time graph is a straight line ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) The body has a uniform velocity if its displacement-time graph is a straight line.<br />
(b) The body has a uniform acceleration if its velocity-time graph is a straight line.</p>

<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 56:<br />
</strong></span>Given alongside is the velocity-time graph for a moving body :<br />
Find :<br />
(i) Velocity of the body at point C.<br />
(ii) Acceleration acting on the body between A and<br />
(iii) Acceleration acting on the body between B and C.<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4318/36083942831_cb2990fa5a_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-7" width="332" height="213" /><br />

(iii) BC represents uniform velocity, so acceleration acting on the body between B and C is zero.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8753/16738731757_95b97af7fe_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q56" width="585" height="98" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 57:<br />
</strong></span>A body is moving uniformly in a straight line with a velocity of 5 m/s. Find graphically the distance covered by it in 5 seconds.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Distance travelled = Area of rectangle OABC<br />
= OA x OC<br />
= 5 x 5 =25 m<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7626/16944763432_e8b2139ae8_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q57" width="323" height="267" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 58:<br />
</strong></span>The speed-time graph of an ascending passenger lift is given alongside.<br />
What is the acceleration of the lift:<br />
(i) during the first two seconds ?<br />
(ii) between second and tenth second ?<br />
(iii) during the last two seconds ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7617/16944763382_54776f1eb9_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q58" width="468" height="127" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 59:<br />
</strong></span>A car is moving on a straight road with uniform acceleration. The speed of the car varies with time as follows :<br />
Time (s)              :     0          2         4          6       8         10<br />
Speed (m/s)       :     4          8       12        16     20         24<br />
Draw the speed-time graph by choosing a convenient scale. From this graph :<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4311/36177561466_8561bc4fc0_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-8" width="388" height="204" /><br />
(i) Calculate the acceleration of the car.<br />
(ii) Calculate the distance travelled by the car in 10 seconds.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :<br />
</strong></span><img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7591/16945110451_8c8181874d_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q59" width="510" height="532" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 60:<br />
</strong></span>The graph given alongside shows how the speed of a car changes with time:<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4323/36218874515_825354b749_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-9" width="301" height="207" /><br />
(i) What is the initial speed of the car ?<br />
(ii) What is the maximum speed attained by the car ?<br />
(iii) Which part of the graph shows zero acceleration ?<br />
(iv) Which part of the graph shows varying retardation ?<br />
(v) Find the distance travelled in first 8 hours.<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(i) Initial speed of the car=10km/h<br />
(ii) Maximum speed attained by the car= 35km/h<br />
(iii) BC represents zero acceleration.<br />
(iv) CD represents varying retardation.<br />
(v)<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7606/16758381998_0ffa867e7e_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q60" width="395" height="482" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 61:<br />
</strong></span>Three speed-time graphs are given below :<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4316/35384087434_8fdaffd07b_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-10" width="547" height="135" /><br />
Which graph represents the case of:<br />
(i) a cricket ball thrown vertically upwards and returning to the hands of the thrower ?<br />
(ii) a trolley decelerating to a constant speed and then accelerating uniformly ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(i) Graph (c): The speedof the ball goes on decreasing uniformly as it moves upward, reaches zero at the highest point, and then increases uniformly as it moves downward.<br />
(ii) Grap(a): The speed of the trolley decreases uniformly, then it moves at a constant speed, and then the speed increases uniformly.</p>
<p><span style="color: brown;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:44</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 62:<br />
</strong></span>Study the speed-time graph of a car given alongside and solution the following questions:<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4294/36177561366_f6ff3e71b8_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-11" width="305" height="206" /><br />
(i) What type of motion is represented by OA ?<br />
(ii) What type of motion is represented by AB ?<br />
(iii) What type of motion is represented by BC ?<br />
(iv) What is the acceleration of car from O to A ?<br />
(v)What is the acceleration of car from A to B ?<br />
(vi) What is the retardation of car from B to C ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(i) OA represents uniform acceleration<br />
(ii) AB represents constant speed.<br />
(iii) BC represents uniform retardation.<br />
(iv) Acceleration of car from O to A = slope of line OA<br />
(v) Acceleration of car from A to B is zero as it has uniform speed during this time.<br />
(vi) Retardation of car from B to C = slope of line BC<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8734/16758634560_6fa15a3d8e_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q62" width="459" height="188" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 63:<br />
</strong></span>What type of motion is represented by each one of the following graphs ?<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4291/36177561596_1fc90050d1_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-motion-12" width="542" height="135" /><br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(i) Graph (a) represents uniform acceleration.<br />
(ii) Graph (b) represents constant speed.<br />
(iii) Graph (c) represents uniform retardation.<br />
(iv) Graph (d) represents non-uniform retardation.</p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 64:<br />
</strong></span>A car is travelling along the road at 8 ms<sup>-1</sup>. It accelerates at 1 ms<sup>-2</sup> for a distance of 18 m. How fast is it then travelling ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Initial velocity, u=8m/s<br />
Acceleration, a=1m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Distance, s=18m<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8749/16326021233_c68810e88b_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q64" width="347" height="155" /></p>
<p><span style="color: yellow;"><strong>Question 65:<br />
</strong></span>A car is travelling at 20 m/s along a road. A child runs out into the road 50 m ahead and the car driver steps on the brake pedal. What must the car&#8217;s deceleration be if the car is to stop just before it reaches the child ?<br />
<span style="color: #yellow;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Initial velocity, u=20m/s<br />
Final velocity, v=0m/s<br />
Distance, s=50m<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7650/16759859709_16ae01fa85_o.png" alt="Lakhmir-Singh-Class-9-Physics-solutions-Motion-A-Q65" width="294" height="203" /><br />
The car&#8217;s deceleration must be 4 m/s<sup>2</sup>.</p>

	<h1 class="entry-title">PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2 &#8211; The Fundamental Unit Of Life &#8211; Cell</h1>
</header><div class="entry-content"><p><a class="button-red" title="Buy Now Formulae Handbook for CBSE Class 9 Maths and Science" href="https://goo.gl/L2Txmv">Formulae Handbook for Class 9 Maths and Science</a></p>
<h2><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2 &#8211; The Fundamental Unit Of Life &#8211; Cell</span></strong></h2>
<p><strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">Text Book Solutions &#8211; P.S.Verma and V.K.Agarwal &#8211; Biology</span></strong></p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">CBSE Class 9 Chapter 2 &#8211; The Fundamental Unit Of Life &#8211; Cell</span></strong></p>
<p><a class="button-blue" title="LearnCBSE Forum - Post and Discuss your Queries" href="http://ask.learncbse.in/"> Share Queries and Discuss your Views and Ideas &#8211; <strong>LearnCBSE Forum</strong></a></p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page No &#8211; 116.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
Prokaryotic Cell:<br />
1. Cell size is generally small.<br />
2. Only a single chromosome is present.<br />
3. Nucleolus is absent.<br />
4. Cell division takes place by fission or budding.<br />
Eukaryotic Cell:<br />
1. Cell is generally large.<br />
2. More than one chromosome is present.<br />
3. Nucleolus is present.<br />
4. Cell division takes place by mitotic or meiotic.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 2:</span><br />
Organs:<br />
1. They are found in multicellular organisms.<br />
2. They are large sized.<br />
3. They may be external or internal to the body of organisms.<br />
4. Organs coordinate to form organ systems, while organ systems form the body of an organism.<br />
Organelles:<br />
1. They are found in all eukaryotic cells.<br />
2. They are very small sized.<br />
3. They are mostly internal.<br />
4. Organelles coordinate to produce the cell.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 4:</span><br />
Light microscope:<br />
1. It uses glass lenses.<br />
2. It uses a beam of light to illuminate the object.<br />
3. Internal vacuum is not required.<br />
Electron microscope:<br />
1. It uses electromagnets.<br />
2. It uses a beam of electrons instead of light.<br />
3. Internal vacuum is essential.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 5:</span><br />
Robert Hooke examined a thin slice of cork under a self-designed crude microscope and observed that the cork resembled the structure of a honey comb. The latter consisted of many tiny compartments. Hooke called them cellulae (Singular cellula), now termed cells. Cellula is a Latin name which means a &#8216;little room&#8217;. Such rooms were also present in monasteries.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 6:</span><br />
There are two types of protein molecules: Intrinsic proteins, which completely covers the lipid bilayer and extrinsic proteins, which occur either on the outer surface or on the inner surface of the lipid membrane.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 7:</span><br />
Its major function is to hold cellular contents and control passage of materials in and out of the cell.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 8:</span><br />
In amoeba, oxygen (O2) enters the cell by the process of diffusion when the level or concentration of O2 inside the cell decreases.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 9:</span><br />
Put dried raisins and apricots in pure water and leave them for some time. Then place them into a concentrated Solution of sugar or salt. Each one of them gains water and swells when placed in pure water due to endosmosis. When such swollen raisins/apricots are placed in the concentrated Solution, each of them loses, water, and consequently shrinks again (due to exosmosis).<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 10:</span><br />
Diffusion:<br />
1. Diffusion can occur in any medium.<br />
2. The diffusing molecules may be solids, liquids or gases.<br />
3. Semipermeable membrane is not required.<br />
4. An equilibrium in the free energy of diffusion molecules is achieved in the system.<br />
Osmosis:<br />
1. It occurs only in liquid medium.<br />
2. It involves movement of solvent molecules only.<br />
3. Semipermeable membrane is required.<br />
4. Equilibrium in the free energy of solvent molecules is never achieved.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 11:</span><br />
Endocytosis is the ingestion of material by the cells through the plasma membrane. It is a collective term that describes three similar processes: phagocytosis (cell eating), potocytosis (cell drinking) and receptor-mediated endocytosis. These processes are pathways to specifically internalize solid particles, small molecules ion, and macromolecules, respectively. All of them require energy, so they may be regarded as different forms of active transport.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 12:</span><br />
(i) When eukaryotic cells are placed in hypotonic Solution, the water molecules will enter into the cell and the cell will swell up.<br />
(ii) If eukaryotic cells are placed in hypertonic Solution, the water molecules will come out of the cell and the cell with shrink.<br />
(iii) If the eukaryotic cell is placed in isotonic Solution, the amount of water molecule will remain the same; it will neither move out nor will go inside. The cell will remain same sized.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 13:</span><br />
(a) Ribosome.<br />
(b) Plastid in plants and Mitochondria in animals.<br />
(c) Rough endoplasmic reticulum.<br />
(d) Genes.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 14:</span><br />
(a)<br />
Chloroplasts:<br />
1. They are green plastids.<br />
2. They contain chlorophylls and carotenoids.<br />
3. Lamellae are present.<br />
4. Chloroplasts are sites of photosynthesis.<br />
Chromoplasts<br />
1. They are non-green coloured plastids.<br />
2. Chlorophylls are absent. Only carotenoids are present.<br />
3. Lamellae are absent.<br />
4. They add colour to the organs for attracting animals to perform pollination and fruit dispersal.<br />
(b)<br />
Ribosome:<br />
1. It is found in both animal cell and plant cell.<br />
2. These are dense, spherical and granular particles which occur freely in the matrix or remain attached to the endoplasmic reticulum.<br />
Centrosome:<br />
1. Centrosome is found only in animal cells.<br />
2. It consists of two granules like centrioles.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 15:</span><br />
Animal Cell:<br />
1. Animal cells are generally small in size.<br />
2. Cell wall is absent.<br />
3. Animal cells have a single highly complex and prominent Golgi apparatus.<br />
4. Animals cells have centrosome and centrioles.<br />
Plant Cell:<br />
1. Plant cells are larger than animal cells.<br />
2. The plasma membrane of plant cell is surrounded by a rigid cell wall made up of cellulose.<br />
3. Plant cells have many simpler units of Golgi apparatus, called dictyosomes.<br />
4. Plant cells lack centrosome and centrioles.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 16:</span><br />
If nucleus is removed from a cell, the protoplasm will ultimately dry up and the cell will die because the nucleus controls all the metabolic activities of a cell.</p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page No &#8211; 117.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 17:</span><br />
Spinach looks green due to the presence of chloroplasts, papaya is yellow and edible part of watermelon is red due to the presence chromoplasts.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 18:</span><br />
(a) Functions of endoplasmic reticulum:<br />
(i) It forms supporting skeletal framework of the cell.<br />
(ii) ER provides a pathway for the distribution of nuclear material from one cell to the other.<br />
(b) Functions of lysosomes:<br />
(i) Lysosomes serve as intracellular digestive system. They destroy any foreign material which enters the cells such as bacteria and virus.<br />
(ii) Lysosomes also remove the worn out and poorly working cellular organelles by digesting them to make way for their new replacements.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 19:</span><br />
(a) Ribosome.<br />
(b) Leucoplasts.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 20:</span><br />
Lysosomes contain digestive enzymes for almost all types of organic materials. If their covering membrane breaks as it happens during injury to cell, the digestive enzymes will spill over the cell contents and digest the same. As Lysosomes are organelles which on bursting can kill cells possessing them, they are called suicide bags.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 21:</span><br />
(a) Cell Inclusions &#8211; Cell inclusions are non-living materials present in the cytoplasm.<br />
(b) Cytosol &#8211; It is the soluble part of cytoplasm and is located between cell organelles.<br />
(c) Protoplasm &#8211; Nucleus and cytoplasm together are called protoplasm.<br />
(d) Nucleoplasm &#8211; It is the liquid ground substance present in the nucleus.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 22:</span><br />
Ribosomes get synthesized in the nucleolus.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 23:</span><br />
(a) The mitochondria are tiny bodies of varying shapes and size. Each mitochondria is bounded by a double membrane envelope. Outer membrane is porous. The inner membrane is thrown into folds. These folds are called cristae and are studded with small rounded bodies known as F1 particles or oxysomes. The interior cavity of the mitochondria is filled with a proteinaceous matrix which contains a few small-sized ribosomes, a circular DNA molecule and phosphate granules. Mitochondria are sites of cellular respiration.<br />
(b) Plastids occur in most plant cells and are absent in animal cells. They have their own genome and ribosomes. There are three types of plastids: chromoplasts, chloroplasts and leucoplasts.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 24:</span><br />
The cell organelles are &#8211; Endoplasmic Reticulum, Ribosomes, Golgi apparatus, Lysosomes, Mitochondria, Plastids, Vacuoles, Peroxisomes and Centrosome.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 25:</span><br />
The three main functional regions of the cell are: Plasma membrane, Nucleus and the cytoplasm.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 26:</span><br />
(a) Nucleus.<br />
(b) Nucleus.<br />
(c) Vacuoles.<br />
(d) Nucleus.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 27:</span><br />
Genes are the functional units of chromosomes which transmit the heredity information from parents to offsprings. These are located on chromosomes.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 28:</span><br />
Lysosomes are called digestive bags because they digest any foreign material which enters the cell such as bacteria and virus.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 29:</span><br />
Mitochondria is called the power plant of eukaryotic cell because it contains enzymes that are needed for the step wise oxidation of food stuffs present in the cells to carbon dioxide and water and energy is released.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 30:</span><br />
Centrioles &#8211; Centrioles are hollow and cylindrical structures which are made up of microtubules.<br />
Functions: (i) It migrates to the poles of animal cells and is involved in the formation of the spindle.<br />
(ii) In plant cells, cell division involves polar caps for the spindle formation.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 31:</span><br />
Lipids gets synthesised in the smooth endoplasmic reticulum and proteins gets synthesised in the ribosomes and rough endoplasmic reticulum.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 32:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-2-32.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 33:</span><br />
Plasmolysed cell means the cell in which the water crosses the plasma membrane in both directions but more water leaves the cell than enters it and the cell will shrinks.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
According to fluid mosaic model, plasma membrane is made up of a bilayer of phospholipids. There are two types of protein molecules: Intrinsic Proteins, which completely covers the lipid bilayer and Extrinsic Proteins, which occur either on the outer surface or on the inner surface of the lipid membrane.<br />
The fluid mosaic membrane has been described as &#8220;a number of protein icebergs floating in the sea of lipids&#8221;.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-2-laq-01.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 2:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-2-laq-02.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2" width="750" height="450" /><br />
Functions of cell organelles:<br />
(i) Endoplasmic Reticulum &#8211; It forms the supporting skeletal framework of the cell.<br />
(ii) Ribosomes &#8211; It synthesises proteins.<br />
(iii) Golgi Apparatus &#8211; It produces vacuoles which contain cellular secretion.<br />
(iv) Lysosomes &#8211; It serves as intracellular digestive system as it digest the foreign materials which enter the cell.<br />
(v) Mitochondria &#8211; These are the sites of cellular respirations<br />
(vi) Plastids &#8211; These are present only in plants and trap solar energy to manufacture food for plants.<br />
(vii) Vacuoles &#8211; They help to maintain the osmotic pressure in a cell.<br />
(viii) Peroxisomes &#8211; They carry out some oxidative reactions.<br />
(ix) Centrosome &#8211; It helps in cell division in the animal cell.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 3:</span><br />
Nucleus &#8211; The nucleus is a large, centrally located spherical cellular component. It is bounded by two nuclear membranes, both forming a nuclear envelope. The nuclear envelope separates the nucleus from the cytoplasm. Within nucleoplasm two types of nuclear structures are embedded &#8211; the nucleolus and chromatin material. The nucleolus may be one or more in number and is not bounded by any membrane. It is rich in protein and RNA molecules and acts as the site for ribosome formation.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-2-laq-03.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 4:</span><br />
(a) Golgi apparatus consists of a set of membrane-bounded, fluid filled vesicles, vacuoles and flattened cisternae. Cisternae are usually stacked together (placed one above the other) in parallel rows. Golgi apparatus exists as an extensive network near the nucleus in the animal cells. However, the plant cells contain many freely distributed subunits of Golgi apparatus, called dictyosomes.<br />
The Golgi apparatus arises from the membrane of the smooth endoplasmic reticulum, which in turn originates from the rough endoplasmic reticulum.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-2-laq-04.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2" width="750" height="450" /><br />
(b) The mitochondria are tiny bodies of varying shapes and size. Each mitochondria is bounded by a double membrane envelope. Outer membrane is porous. The inner membrane is thrown into folds. These folds are called cristae and are studded with small rounded bodies known as F1 particles or oxysomes. The interior cavity of the mitochondria is filled with a proteinaceous matrix which contains a few small-sized ribosomes, a circular DNA molecule and phosphate granules. Mitochondria are sites of cellular respiration.<br />





































































<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-2-laq-05.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 2" width="750" height="450" /><br />



<h1>class 9th solution of chemistry chapter 2</h1>



<h2><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Class 9 Solutions Is Matter Around Us Pure ?</span></strong></h2>
<p><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">Text Book Solutions &#8211; Lakhmir Singh and Manjit Kaur &#8211; Chemistry</span></strong><br />
<strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">CBSE Class 9 &#8211; Chemistry</span></strong><br />
<strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Text Book Page No &#8211; 56</strong><br />
<h1>
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 01</span><br />
False<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 02</span><br />
Milk, Paint, Glass<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 03</span><br />
Air is a mixture.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 04</span><br />
Mercury is a liquid metal and bromine is a liquid non-metal.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 05</span><br />
Sodium metal is soft and diamond is an extremely hard non-metal.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 06</span><br />
Diamond is a non-metal which is good conductor of electricity.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 07</span><br />
Mercury<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 08</span><br />
Carbon is a solid non-metal, bromine is a liquid non-metal and chlorine is a gaseous non-metal.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 09</span><br />
(a). Malleability<br />
(b). Ductility<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 10</span><br />
Non-metals show brittleness.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 11</span><br />
This means that metals can be drawn into thin sheets and can also be drawn into wires.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 12</span><br />
This means that non-metals break into pieces when they are hammered.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 13</span><br />
This means that metals make a ringing sound when we strike them.<br />

Solutions are homogeneous mixtures in which no separation is visible between different materials.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 29</span><br />
Air is a mixture because-<br />
(i). Air can be separated into its constituents like oxygen, nitrogen, etc. by physical process of fractional distillation.<br />
(ii). Air shows the properties of all the gases present in it.<br />
(iii). Liquid air does not have a fixed boiling point.<br />
Water is compound because &#8211;<br />
(i). Water cannot be separated into its constituents, hydrogen and oxygen by physical methods.<br />
(ii). Heat and light are given out when water is prepared by burning hydrogen in oxygen.<br />
(iii). Water has standard b.p. of 100oC under standard atmospheric pressure.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 30</span><br />
Two solid elements at room temp. &#8211; Iron and copper<br />
Two liquid elements at room temp. &#8211; Mercury and bromine<br />
Two gaseous elements at room temp. &#8211; Hydrogen and oxygen<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 31</span><br />
Hydrogen and oxygen cannot be split up into two or more simpler substances by applying heat, light or electric energy.<br />
Whereas, water can be split up into hydrogen and oxygen by applying electric energy, so it is not an element.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 32</span><br />
All the elements can be divided into following three groups-<br />
(i). Metals ; Iron and copper<br />
(ii).Non-metals ; Carbon and sulphur<br />
(iii).Metalloids ; Boron and silicon<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 33</span><br />
Metals are malleable and ductile whereas non-metals are not.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 34</span><br />
(i). Malleability &#8211; Metals show this property but non-metals don&#8217;t.<br />
(ii). Ductility &#8211; Metals show this property but non-metals don&#8217;t.<br />
(iii). Electrical conductivity &#8211; Metals are good conductors of electricity whereas non-metals are bad conductors except graphite.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 35</span><br />
Aluminium is malleable, ductile and sonorous, so it is a metal.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 36</span><br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 37</span><br />

If nothing is left behind then the colourless liquid is pure water.<br />

Sea-water and Soda-water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 39</span><br />
Air is a mixture because-<br />
(i). Air can be separated into its constituents like oxygen, nitrogen, etc. by physical process of fractional distillation.<br />
(ii). Air shows the properties of all the gases present in it.<br />
(iii). Liquid air does not have a fixed boiling point.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 40</span><br />
Water is a compound because &#8211;<br />
(i). Water cannot be separated into its constituents, hydrogen and oxygen by physical methods.<br />
(ii). Heat and light are given out when water is prepared by burning hydrogen in oxygen.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 41</span><br />
A compound is a substance made up of two or more elements chemically combined in a fixed proportion by mass.<br />
NaCl cannot be separated into its constituents by physical process and the properties of NaCl is completely different from that of Na and Cl, so NaCl is a compound and not a mixture.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 42</span><br />
A mixture is a substance which consists of two or more elements or compounds not chemically combined together.<br />
As energy is neither evolved nor absorbed during the formation of sugar solution and a sugar solution shows properties of both sugar and water so sugar solution is a mixture not a compound.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 43</span><br />
Brass is a mixture because-<br />
(i). It shows the properties of its constituents, copper and zinc.<br />
(ii). It has a variable composition.<br />

As energy is neither evolved nor absorbed during the formation of salt solution and a salt solution shows properties of both salt and water so salt solution is a mixture not a compound.</p>

A pure compound will evaporate completely, leaving no residue whereas solution will not be evaporated completely, i.e. some residue will be left behind.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 50</span><br />
Chlorine gas, Aluminium foil, Iodine vapour, Graphite, Sulphur powder, Diamond are not compounds.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 51</span><br />
(a). Those mixtures in which the substances are completely mixed together and are indistinguishable from one another, are called homogeneous mixtures. They have a uniform composition throughout its mass. All the homogeneous mixtures are called solutions.<br />
Examples- Sugar solution, salt solution, copper sulphate solution, etc.<br />
Those mixtures in which the substances remain separate and one substance is spread throughout the other substance as small particles, droplets or bubbles, are called heterogeneous mixtures. Heterogeneous mixture does not have a uniform composition throughout its mass.<br />
Example- Starch solution, soap solution.<br />
(b). Homogeneous mixtures &#8211; Soda water, air, vinegar, alcohol and water mixture, sugar and water mixture, Copper sulphate solution.<br />
Heterogeneous mixture &#8211; Wood, petrol and water mixture, chalk and water mixture.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 52</span><br />
(a).(i).Elements &#8211; An element is a substance which cannot be split up into two or more simpler substances by the usual chemical methods of applying heat, light or electricity.<br />
Ex. Hydrogen, Oxygen<br />
(ii). Compounds &#8211; A compound is a substance made up of two or more elements chemically combined in a fixed proportion by mass.<br />
Ex. Sodium chloride, calcium carbonate<br />
(iii). Mixtures &#8211; A mixture is a substance which consists of two or more elements or compounds not chemically combined together.<br />
(b). Elements &#8211; Gold, Diamond, Graphite<br />
Compounds &#8211; Common salt, Sea water, Marble<br />
Mixtures &#8211; Brass, Sand, Petroleum, Chalk, Air<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 53</span><br />
(i). METALS &#8211; A metal is an element that is malleable, ductile and conducts electricity.<br />
Example &#8211; Iron, Copper<br />
(ii). NON-METALS &#8211; A non metal is an element that is neither malleable, nor ductile and does not conducts electricity.<br />
Example &#8211; Carbon, Sulphur<br />
(iii). METALLOIDS &#8211; The elements which show some properties of metals and some other properties of non-metals are called metalloids.<br />
Example &#8211; Boron, Silicon, Helium, Magnesium, Copper<br />
(b). Metals &#8211; Mercury, Sodium,<br />
Non-metals &#8211; Diamond, Sulphur, Iodine, Carbon, Boron<br />
Metalloids &#8211; Silicon, Germanium<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 54</span><br />
(a). Mixtures &#8211; A mixture is a substance which consists of two or more elements or compounds not chemically combined together.<br />
Examples &#8211; Air, gun powder.<br />
(b). Homogeneous mixtures- Those mixtures in which the substance are completely mixed together and are indistinguishable from one another, are called homogeneous mixtures.<br />
Examples- Sugar solution, copper sulphate solution.<br />
Those mixtures in which the substances remain separate and one substance is spread throughout the other substance as small particles, droplets or bubbles, are called heterogeneous mixtures.<br />
Example- Starch solution, soap solution.<br />
(c). Other name for homogeneous mixtures is SOLUTIONS.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 55</span><br />
(a). Three general classes of matter are elements, compounds and mixtures.<br />
Element &#8211; Hydrogen<br />
Compound &#8211; Sodium chloride<br />
Mixtures &#8211; Salt solution<br />
(b).<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 18</span><br />
Colloid<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 19</span><br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 20</span><br />
(a) Colloidal; true<br />
(b) Heterogeneous; centrifugation<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 21</span><br />
(a)Solute-The substance which is dissolved in a liquid to make a solution is called as solute.<br />
(b)Solvent-The liquid in which solute is dissolved is known as solvent.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 22</span><br />
A solution is a homogeneous mixture of two or more substances whereas a colloid is a kind of solution in which the size of solute particles is intermediate between those in true solutions and those in suspensions.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 23</span><br />
A colloid is a kind of solution in which the size of solute particles is intermediate between those in true solutions and those in suspensions whereas a suspension is a heterogeneous mixture in which the small particles of a solid are spread throughout a liquid without dissolving in it.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 24</span><br />
A true solution does not scatter a beam of light passing through it but a colloidal solution scatters a beam of light passing through it and renders its path visible. A true solution is a homogeneous mixture of two or more substances whereas a colloidal solution is a kind of solution in which the size of solute particles is intermediate between those in true solutions and those in suspensions and is a heterogeneous mixture.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 25</span><br />
True Solutions &#8211; Salt solution and sugar solution<br />
Colloidal Solution &#8211; Starch solution, Ink, Blood<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 26</span><br />
The given solution is taken in a beaker. Then, a strong beam of light is allowed to fall on the solution from one side of the beaker in a dark room. If the beam of light is visible in the solution, then it is a colloidal solution.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 27</span><br />
The path of light beam is illuminated and becomes visible.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 28</span><br />
A true solution can be distinguished from a colloidal solution by experimenting Tyndall effect. A true solution does not scatter a beam of light passing through it but a colloidal solution scatters a beam of light passing through it.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 29</span><br />
The particles of a suspension cannot pass through a filter paper whereas particles of colloids can easily pass through filter paper.<br />
Colloidal solutions are quite stable whereas suspensions are very unstable.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 30</span><br />
Both the given solutions will be kept stationary in different beakers for some time.<br />
The beaker in which the dissolved particles settle down after some time is a suspension and another one is a solution.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 31</span><br />
Starch solution and milk will show Tyndall effect.<br />
This is because in a milk solution and starch solution (colloidal solutions) the size of solute particles is big enough to scatter the light passing through it.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 32</span><br />
Types of solution-<br />
(i). Solid in solid.<br />
Example- Brass<br />
(ii). Solid in a liquid<br />
Example- Tincture of iodine<br />
(iii). Liquid in liquid<br />
Example- ethanoic acid<br />
(iv). Gas in a liquid<br />
Example- CO2 in water<br />
(v). gas in gas<br />
Example- Air<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 33</span><br />
Solutions &#8211; Brine<br />
Suspensions &#8211; Chalk water mixture, milk of magnesia, Muddy river water<br />
Colloids &#8211; Milk, blood, ink, shaving cream, smoke in air, soda water<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 34</span><br />
(a). Sol &#8211; Sol is a colloid in which tiny solid particles are dispersed in a liquid medium. Examples are ink and soap solution<br />
(b). Aerosol- Aerosol is a colloid in which a solid or liquid is dispersed in a gas. Examples are hairspray and fog.<br />
(c). Emulsion &#8211; An emulsion is a colloid in which minute droplets of one liquid are dispersed in another liquid which is not miscible with it. Examples are milk and butter.<br />
(d). Foam- A foam is a colloid in which a gas is dispersed in a liquid medium. Examples are soap bubbles and shaving cream.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 35</span><br />
The concentration of a solution is the amount of solute present in given quantity of the solution.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 36</span><br />
If a saturated solution is heated to a higher temperature, then it becomes unsaturated.<br />
If a saturated solution is cooled to a lower temperature, then some of its dissolved solute will separate out in the form of solid crystals.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 37</span><br />
According to question-<br />
21.5 g of NaCl dissolves in 60 g of water.<br />
So, amount of NaCl which gets dissolved in 100 g of water = 21.5 x 100 / 60 = 35.8 g<br />
Thus, the solubility of NaCl is 35.8 g at 25oC.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 38</span><br />
According to question-<br />
9.72 g of KCl dissolves in 30 g of water.<br />
So, amount of KCl which gets dissolved in 100 g of water = 9.72 x 100/30 = 32.4 g<br />
Thus, the solubility of KCl = 32.4 g<br />

i. Cooking of food &#8211; Chemical change<br />

iii. Cutting of trees &#8211; Physical change<br />
iv. Dissolving salt in water &#8211; Physical change<br />
v. Digestion of food &#8211; Chemical change<br />
vi. Melting of ice- Physical change<br />

(d) Breaking of a glass tumbler &#8211; Physical change</p>
