<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 42</span><br />
Physical change &#8211; Sublimation of solid, Formation of clouds, making of fruit salad from raw fruits, dissolving CO2 in water<br />
Chemical change &#8211; Decomposition of water into H2 and O2 by passing electric current<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 43</span><br />
Physical change &#8211; Melting of candle wax, mixing of iron filings and sand, breaking a piece of chalk, cutting a piece of paper<br />
Chemical change &#8211; Burning of candle wax, burning of wood, burning of piece of paper<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 44</span><br />
When sea water is a mixture of dissolved salts and water only, it is homogeneous solution.<br />
And if sea water contains suspended impurities like decayed plants or animal material, etc. then it is called heterogeneous solution.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 45</span><br />
Sugar solution, Salt solution, copper sulphate solution and ammonium chloride solution do not show Tyndall effect.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 46</span><br />
(a). The change in which no new substance is formed is called a physical change.<br />
Example- Melting of candle wax, mixing of iron filings and sand<br />
(b).The change in which new substance is formed is called a chemical change.<br />
Example- Burning of candle wax, burning of wood<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 47</span><br />
<img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-27952" src="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Lakhmir-SIngh-Class-9-Chemistry-Image-47-2.png" alt="Lakhmir SIngh Class 9 Chemistry Image 47 2" width="682" height="211" srcset="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Lakhmir-SIngh-Class-9-Chemistry-Image-47-2.png 682w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Lakhmir-SIngh-Class-9-Chemistry-Image-47-2-300x93.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 682px) 100vw, 682px" /><br />
(b). Chemical change &#8211; Coal burning in air, making of cake<br />
Physical change- A glass bottle breaking, wool being knitted into a sweater.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 48</span><br />
(a). The maximum amount of a solute which can be dissolved in 100 g of a solvent at a specified temperature is known as the solubility of that solute in that solvent .<br />
The solubility of solids in liquids is directly proportional to temperature whereas the solubility of gases in liquids is inversly proportional to temperature.<br />
(b). This statement means that 100 g of water can dissolve a maximum of 20.7 g of copper sulphate at 20oC.<br />
(c). The solubility of solids in liquids increases on increasing the temperature and decreases on decreasing the temperature.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 49</span><br />
(a). A solution is a homogeneous mixture of two or more substances.<br />
Example- Salt solution, metal alloys.<br />
(b). A suspension is a heterogeneous mixture in which the small particles of a solid are spread throughout a liquid without dissolving in it.<br />
Example- Muddy-water, Milk of magnesia.<br />
(c). A colloid is a kind of solution in which the size of solute particles is intermediate between those in true solutions and those in suspensions.<br />
Example- Soap solution, milk.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 50</span><br />
(a). A solution in which no more solute can be dissolved at that temperature is called a saturated solution while a solution in which more quantity of solute can be dissolved without raising its temperature is called an unsaturated solution.<br />
To test the saturation or unsaturation of a solution, more solute may be added to the solution. If that solute gets dissolved in the solution then the solution will be unsaturated.<br />
To test whether a given solution is saturated or not, add some more solute to the solution and try to dissolve it by stirring. If solute does not dissolve in the given solution, then it will be a saturated solution.<br />
(b). Take some water in a beaker and heat it slowly with the help of burner. Now, start adding sodium chloride salt to the hot water with a spoon and stir it with a glass rod continuously so that sodium chloride goes on dissolving in water. Take the temperature of water up to 25oC and then keeping this temperature constant, go on adding sodium chloride till no more sodium chloride dissolves in it and some undissolved crystals will be left at the bottom. The contents of the beaker are now filtered and the clear solution obtained is the saturated solution of sodium chloride at 25oC.<br />
If the temperature is lowered from 25oC to 10oC, then some of the crystals of sodium chloride will separate out from the solution in the form of solute crystals.</p>
<p><strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Text Book PAGE N0 82</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 66</span><br />
Indigestion mixtures are suspensions so there is an instruction written on the bottle of these mixtures &#8220;SHAKE IT WELL BEFORE USE&#8221;. This is because the particles of indigestion mixture i.e. suspensions are unstable and settle down at the bottom of the bottle after some time.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 67</span><br />
(a) Mixtures like A are known as suspensions.<br />
(b) Mixtures like B are known as colloids.<br />
(c) Mixtures like C are known as true solutions.<br />
(d) The phenomenon existed by A and B which occurs on passing a beam of light through them is called Tyndall effect.<br />
(e) (i) Chalk-water mixture is like A.<br />
(ii) Soap solution is a mixture like B.<br />
(iii) Salt solution is a mixture like C.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 68</span><br />
(a) When solid A is dissolved in water, chemical change takes place. This is because the properties of products B and C are entirely different from those of solid A and water and a lot of heat and energy is evolved in the reaction.<br />
(b) Physical change occurs when solid D is dissolved in water. This is because the product E shows the properties of both, solid D and water.<br />
(c) Sodium metal could behave like solid A.<br />
Product B is sodium hydroxide.<br />
Product C is hydrogen.<br />
(d) Solid D is ammonium chloride.<br />
(e) D can be recovered from E by evaporation.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 69</span><br />
(a) Solution like X are known as unsaturated solution.<br />
(b) Solution like Y are known as saturated solution.<br />
(c) If solution Y at 30oC is cool down to 10oC by keeping the beaker in crushed ice, then some of the dissolved solid will separate out from the solution and settle at the bottom of the beaker as crystals. This is because the solubility of solid decreases on cooling.<br />
(d) Solubility is the term used to denote the amount of solid dissolved in 100 grams of water in a solution.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 70</span><br />
According to question:<br />
Solubility at 40oC = 41 g<br />
But, solubility = solid dissolved in 100 grams of water in a solution<br />
So, mass of ammonium chloride needed to make a saturated solution of ammonium chloride in 50 g of water at 40oC= 41/2 g = 20.5 g</p>

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 33</span><br />
Sugar is soluble in water whereas sand is insoluble in water. The difference in their solubility is used to separate them. The mixture of sand and sugar is dissolved in water, then it is filtered with the help of filter paper. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while sugar solution is obtained as filtrate.The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of sugar.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 34</span><br />
The difference in the solubility of salt and sand in water is used to separate them from their mixture.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 35</span><br />
Salt is soluble in water whereas sand is insoluble in water. The difference in their solubility is used to separate them. The mixture of sand and salt is dissolved in water, then it is filtered with the help of filter paper. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while salt solution is obtained as filtrate .The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of salt.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 36</span><br />
Sugar is soluble in alcohol but salt is insoluble in alcohol, so a mixture of sugar and salt can be separated by using alcohol as solvent.<br />

The mixture of sand and sodium chloride is dissolved in water, then it is filtered with the help of filter paper. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while sodium chloride solution is obtained as filtrate .The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of sodium chloride.<br />

Potash alum is soluble in water whereas sand is insoluble in water. The difference in their solubility is used to separate them. The mixture of sand and potash alum is dissolved in water, then it is filtered with the help of filter paper. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while potash alum solution is obtained as filtrate .The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of potash alum.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 39</span><br />
Sulphur is soluble in carbon disulphide whereas sodium chloride is insoluble in carbon disulphide.The mixture of sulphur and sodium chloride is shaken with carbon disulphide.Sulphur dissolves in carbon disulphide whereas sodium chloride remains undissolved. The solution is then filtered,sodium chloride is obtained as residue.On evaporating the filtrate ,carbon disulphide solvent is eliminated and solid sulphur remains behind.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 40</span><br />
Mixture of iodine and common salt is heated. Iodine sublimes on heating leaving behind common salt and can be recovered in the form of sublimate by cooling its vapours.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 41</span><br />
Mixture of camphor and sand is heated. Camphor sublimes on heating leaving behind sand and can be recovered in the form of sublimate by cooling its vapours.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 42</span><br />
Mixture of iron filings and powdered carbon can be separated by using magnet.A horse-shoe magnet is moved on the surface of the mixture.The iron filings are attracted by the magnet,they cling to the poles of the magnet and get separated. This process is repeated a number of times till complete separation of iron filings is done.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 44</span><br />
In factories, scrap iron is separated from the heap of waste materials by using big electromagnets fitted to a crane.When a crane fitted with a powerful electromagnet is lowered on to the heap of waste materials, then the scrap iron objects present in the heap cling to the electromagnet. The crane is then moved up and away to drop these scrap iron objects at a separate place.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 47</span><br />
At first, the mixture of common salt, sulphur powder and sand is shaken with carbon disulphide. Sulphur dissolves in carbon disulphide whereas common salt and sand remain undissolved. The solution is then filtered, common salt and sand mixture is obtained as residue. On evaporating the filtrate, carbon disulphide solvent is eliminated and solid sulphur remains behind. Now, the common salt and sand mixture is shaken with water. Common salt gets dissolved in water .The solution is then filtered, sand is obtained as residue. The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of common salt.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 48</span><br />
The mixture of water, kerosene and sand is filtered with the help of filter paper first. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while mixture of water and kerosene is obtained as filtrate .The mixture of water and kerosene is then put in separating funnel and allowed to stand for sometime. The mixture separates into two layers according to the difference in the densities of water and kerosene. Water is heavier than kerosene. So,water forms lower layer while kerosene forms upper layer.On opening the stop clock of separating funnel,the lower layer of water comes out first and collected in beaker leaving behind kerosene in the separating funnel.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 49</span><br />
The mixture of common salt,sand and ammonium chloride will be heated first.Ammonium chloride sublimes on heating and can be recovered in the form of sublimate by cooling its vapours leaving behind mixture of common salt and sand.Salt is soluble in water whereas sand is insoluble in water.The mixture of sand and salt is dissolved in water, then it is filtered with the help of filter paper. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while salt solution is obtained as filtrate .The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of salt.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 50</span><br />

This process is repeated a number of times till complete separation of iron nails occur leaving behind mixture of camphor and common salt. Mixture of camphor and common salt is heated. Camphor sublimes on heating leaving behind common salt and can be recovered in the form of sublimate by cooling its vapours<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 51</span><br />
The mixture of water, groundnut oil and common salt is put in a separating funnel and allowed to stand for sometime. The mixture separates into two layers according to the densities of water and groundnut oil. Water is heavier than groundnut oil. So, water forms lower layer while groundnut oil forms upper layer. On opening the stop clock of separating funnel, the lower layer of water comes out first and collected in beaker leaving behind groundnut oil in the funel. Now, solution of water and common salt is heated. Water gets evaporated leaving behind solid common salt.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 52</span><br />
Mixture of chalk powder,iron filings and naphthalene can be separated by using magnet and then by sublimation. A horse-shoe magnet is moved on the surface of the mixture.The iron filings are attracted by the magnet, they cling to the poles of the magnet and get separated. This process is repeated a number of times till complete separation of iron filings occur leaving behind mixture of chalk powder and naphthalene. Then, mixture of chalk powder and naphthalene is heated.Naphthalene sublimes on heating leaving behind chalk powder and can be recovered in the form of sublimate by cooling its vapours.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 53</span><br />
Mixture of iodine, iron filings and salt can be separated by using magnet and then by sublimation. A horse-shoe magnet is moved on the surface of the mixture.The iron filings are attracted by the magnet, they cling to the poles of the magnet and get separated. This process is repeated a number of times till complete separation of iron filings occur leaving behind mixture of iodine and salt. Then, mixture of iodine and salt is heated. Iodine sublimes on heating leaving behind salt and can be recovered in the form of sublimate by cooling its vapours.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 54</span><br />
Mixture of iron filings,chalk powder and common salt can be separated by using magnet first.A horse-shoe magnet is moved on the surface of the mixture.The iron filings are attracted by the magnet,they cling to the poles of the magnet and get separated. This process is repeated a number of times till complete separation of iron filings occur leaving behind mixture of chalk powder and common salt.The mixture of chalk powder and common salt is then dissolved in water and then filtered with the help of filter paper. <span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 55</span><br />

The iron filings are attracted by the magnet, they cling to the poles of the magnet and get separated. This process is repeated a number of times till complete separation of iron filings occur leaving behind mixture of common salt and sand.The mixture of common salt and sand is then dissolved in water and then filtered with the help of filter paper. Sand remains as residue on the filter paper while common salt solution is obtained as filtrate .The filtrate is then evaporated to get crystals of common salt.<br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 57</span><br />
The mixture of mustard oil and water is put in separating funnel and allowed to stand for sometime.The mixture separates into two layers according to the densities of water and mustard oil. Water is heavier than mustard oil. So,water forms lower layer while mustard oil forms upper layer. On opening the stop clock of separating funnel, the lower layer of water comes out first and collected in beaker leaving behind mustard oil.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 58</span><br />
The mixture of cooking oil(groundnut oil) and water is put in separating funnel and allowed to stand for sometime.The mixture separates into two layers according to the densities of water and groundnut oil. Water is heavier than groundnut oil. So,water forms lower layer while groundnut oil forms upper layer. On opening the stop clock of separating funnel,the lower layer of water comes out first and collected in beaker leaving behind groundnut oil.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 59</span><br />
Mercury, oil and water are immiscible liquids and have different densities. Mixture of mercury, oil and water will be put in separating funnel and allowed to stand for sometimes. The mixture separates into three layers according to the densities of mercury, oil and water. On opening the stop clock of separating funnel, the lower layer formed by mercury comes out first and collected in beaker leaving behind other two layers. Similarly, again on opening the stop clock of separating funnel, the lower layer of water comes out first and collected in beaker leaving behind oil in the funnel.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 60</span><br />
Sulphur is soluble in carbon disulphide whereas iron filing is insoluble in carbon disulphide.The mixture of sulphur and iron filing is shaken with carbon disulphide.Sulphur dissolves in carbon disulphide whereas iron filings remain undissolved. The solution is then filtered, iron filing is obtained as residue.On evaporating the filtrate, carbon disulphide solvent is eliminated and solid sulphur remains behind.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 61</span><br />
Centrifugation is used to separate cream from milk.Milk is a suspension of tiny droplets of oil in a watery liquid.It is put in closed container in a big centrifuge machine.When machine is switched on,milk is rotated at very high speed in its container.The cream being lighter floats over the skimmed milk and then can be removed.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 62</span><br />
Impure copper sulphate is dissolved in minimum amount of water in a china dish to make copper sulphate solution. It is then filtered to remove insoluble impurities. Now, copper sulphate solution is heated gently on a water bath to evaporate water and a saturated solution is obtained. Then heating is stopped and saturated solution of copper sulphate is allowed to cool slowly. Crystals of pure copper sulphate will be formed leaving behind impurities. These crystals are then separated and dried.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 63</span><br />
Crystallisation is better method for recovering sugar from sugar solution than evaporation because-<br />
(a)Sugar decomposes or get charred on heating to dryness during evaporation.There is no such problem in crystallization.<br />
(b)The soluble impurities do not get removed in the process of evaporation. But such impurities get removed in crystallization.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 64</span><br />
Chromatography is a technique of separating two or more dissolved solids which are present in a solution in very small quantities.Its two applications are-<br />
(a)Chromatography is used to separate solutions of coloured substances(dyes and pigments).<br />
(b)Chromatography is used to separate small amounts of products of chemical reactions.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 65</span><br />
(a)Water and kerosene mixture can be separated by using a separating funnel because these are immiscible liquids and they have different densities.<br />
(b)Water and acetone mixture can not be separated by by using a separating funnel because these are miscible liquids.</p>
<p><strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Text Book PAGE NO 107</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 66</span><br />
The mixture of common salt and ammonium chloride is taken in a china dish and placed on a tripod stand. The china dish is covered with an inverted glass funnel. A loose cotton plug is put in the upper, open end of the funnel to prevent the ammonium chloride vapours from escaping into the atmosphere. The china dish is heated by using a burner. On heating the mixture, ammonium chloride changes into white vapours. These vapours rise up and get converted into solid ammonium chloride on coming in contact with the cold, inner walls of the funnel. In this way, pure ammonium chloride collects on the inner sides of the funnel in the form of a sublimate and can be removed. Common salt does not change into vapours on heating, so it remains behind in the china dish and can be separated out.<br />
<img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-27957" src="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-common-salt-and-ammonium-chloride-by-sublimation-66.png" alt="Separation of mixture of common salt and ammonium chloride by sublimation 66" width="629" height="469" srcset="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-common-salt-and-ammonium-chloride-by-sublimation-66.png 629w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-common-salt-and-ammonium-chloride-by-sublimation-66-300x224.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 629px) 100vw, 629px" /><br />
Fig. Separation of mixture of common salt and ammonium chloride by sublimation<br />
Ammonium chloride sublimes on heating whereas common salt does not sublime on heating. So, we can separate ammonium chloride from a mixture of common salt and ammonium chloride by the process of sublimation.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 67</span><br />
A mixture of common salt and water can be separated completely by the process of distillation. The distillation can be used to separate a liquid from dissolved non-volatile solids.<br />
The salt water mixture is taken in the distillation flask A and heated. Some porcelain pieces are put in the distillation flask to avoid bumping of the solution due to uneven heating. On heating, water forms vapours which rise up and come out through the side tube B of the distillation flask, and go into water condenser C. Cold water from tap is circulated through the outer tube of condenser for cooling the vapours. The hot vapours get cooled in the condenser to form pure water (i.e. distilled water) which trickles down from the condenser and collects in the beaker D. Since the salt is non-volatile, so it remains behind in the distillation flask.<br />
<img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-27958" src="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-salt-and-water-by-distillation-67.png" alt="Separation of mixture of salt and water by distillation 67" width="846" height="465" srcset="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-salt-and-water-by-distillation-67.png 846w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-salt-and-water-by-distillation-67-300x165.png 300w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-salt-and-water-by-distillation-67-768x422.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 846px) 100vw, 846px" /><br />
Fig. Separation of mixture of salt and water by distillation<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 68</span><br />
In cities, drinking water is supplied from water works where river or lake water is made free from suspended solid substances and germs. In water works, the methods like sedimentation, decantation, loading, filtration and chlorination etc. are used to remove undesirable materials from water. The source of water supply in a city is either a nearby river or lake (reservoir), from there it is pumped into &#8216;sedimentation tank&#8217;. Here it is allowed to stand for sometime so that many of insoluble substances present in water settle down at bottom of the tank. From there, it is sent to a &#8216;loading tank&#8217; where some alum is added to water. Here suspended clay particles in water get loaded with alum particles, become heavy and settle down at the bottom of the tank. Then, it is passed through &#8216;filtration tank&#8217;. It has three layers: fine sand layer at top, coarse sand layer in middle and gravel as the bottom layer. These act as filters and even the small suspended particles get removed when water passes through these layers. Then, the clear water is passed into a chlorination tank. Here, chlorine is added to water to kill the germs present in it. Now, the clean and disinfected water is pumped by pumping station into high storage tanks and from there, it is supplied to homes and factories through the network of big and small pipes.<br />
<img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-27959" src="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Water-purification-process-at-water-works-68.png" alt="Water purification process at water works 68" width="671" height="308" srcset="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Water-purification-process-at-water-works-68.png 671w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Water-purification-process-at-water-works-68-300x138.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 671px) 100vw, 671px" /><br />
Fig. Water purification process at water works<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 69</span><br />
(a) Fractional distillation is the process of separating two or more miscible liquids (liquids which mix together in all proportions and form a single layer) by distillation, the distillate being collected in fractions boiling at different temperatures. The separation of two liquids by fractional distillation depends on the difference in their boiling points. It is carried out by using a fractionating column.<br />
Fractionating column is a long vertical glass tube filled with glass beads. The glass beads provide a large surface area for hot vapours to cool and condens repeatedly. It provides different temperature zones inside it, the highest temperature being at the bottom of the column and the lowest temperature near its top. It is fitted in the neck of the distillation flask.<br />
(b)<br />
<img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-27956" src="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-alcohol-and-water-by-fractional-distillation-69.png" alt="Separation of mixture of alcohol and water by fractional distillation 69" width="526" height="380" srcset="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-alcohol-and-water-by-fractional-distillation-69.png 526w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-mixture-of-alcohol-and-water-by-fractional-distillation-69-300x217.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 526px) 100vw, 526px" /><br />
Fig. Separation of mixture of alcohol and water by fractional distillation<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 70</span><br />
(a)Air is mixture of gases like nitrogen, oxygen, argon, carbon dioxide, helium, neon, krypton, xeon etc. The various gases of air are separated from one another by fractional distillation of liquid air. This separation is based on the fact that different gases of air have different boiling points(in liquid form).<br />
The air is first filtered to remove dust, then water vapour and carbon dioxide are removed. Air is compressed to a high pressure and then cooled. The cooled air is then allowed to expand quickly into a chamber through a jet. This cools the air even more. This process of compression, cooling and rapid expansion of air is repeated again and again to make the air more and more cool so that it becomes liquid air. Now, the liquid air is fed into a tall fractionating column and warmed up slowly.<br />
Liquid nitrogen has lowest boiling point of -196oC.So, on warming, it boils off first to form nitrogen gas and is collected at the upper part of the fractional distillation column. Liquid argon has a slightly higher boiling point of -186oC. So, it boils off next and collected as argon gas in the middle part of fractional distillation column. Liquid oxygen has a still higher boiling point of -183 oC. So, liquid oxygen boils off last and collected as oxygen gas at the bottom of fractional distillation column.<br />
(b)<br />
<img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-27955" src="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-major-gases-of-air-70.png" alt="Separation of major gases of air 70" width="669" height="258" srcset="https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-major-gases-of-air-70.png 669w, https://www.learncbse.in/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Separation-of-major-gases-of-air-70-300x116.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 669px) 100vw, 669px" /><br />
Fig. Separation of major gases of air</p>
<p><strong>Lakhmir Singh Chemistry Text Book PAGE NO 108</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 86</span><br />
(a) Y will be collected from near the bottom of the fractional distillation column because it has highest boiling point of -183oC.<br />
(b) Z will be collected from the top part of the fractional distillation column because it has lowest boiling point of -196oC.<br />
(c) X will be collected from the middle part of the fractional distillation column because it has a boiling point of -186oC which is lower than that of Y but higher than that of Z.<br />
(d) X is liquid argon; Y is liquid oxygen; Z is liquid nitrogen.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 87</span><br />
(a) We will use fractional distillation to separate a mixture of A and B.<br />
(b) We will use separating funnel to separate a mixture of B and C.<br />
(c) (i) Alcohol would behave like A.<br />
(ii) Water would behave like B.<br />
(iii) Oil would behave like C.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 88</span><br />
(a) P is sand; Q is common salt; R is iron fillings; S is ammonium chloride.<br />
(b) We first separate R (iron filings) by using a magnet to attract them. Then, separate S (ammonium chloride) by sublimation. Now, we shake P(sand)and Q(common salt) with water and filter. P(sand) is obtained as residue. Now, we evaporate filtrate to dryness to obtain Q(common salt).<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 89</span><br />
(a) X is alcohol.<br />
(b) Y is iodine.<br />
(c) Process Z is called sublimation<br />
(d) Process used to recover both the components alcohol and iodine from tincture of iodine is distillation.<br />
(e) The process used to recover only component Y from tincture of iodine is evaporation.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 90</span><br />
(a) (i) Constituent A could be sulphur.<br />
(ii) Liquid D could be carbon disulphide.<br />
(b) (i) Constituent B could be copper sulphate.<br />
(ii) Liquid E could be water.<br />
(c) Liquid C could be vegetable oil.<br />
(d) Filter the mixture of A, B and C. C(oil) being liquid will be obtained as a filtrate. Residue consists of A(sulphur) and B(copper sulphate). Add water to the residue mixture, shake and filter. A(sulphur) is obtained as residue. Now, evaporate filtrate to obtain B(copper sulphate).</p></h1>

<center><h1><font color="white">let see solution of chapter 2 force and laws of motion </font></h1></center>






<h1><body bgcolor="black">
<font color="white"><p><span style="color:purple;"><strong>Question 1:<br />
</strong></span>What name is given to the product of mass and velocity of a body ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The product of mass and velocity of a body is called momentum.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 2:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity which is considepurple to be a measure of the quantity of motion of a body.<br />
<span style="color: ;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Momentum is the measure of quantity of motion of a body</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 3:</strong></span><br />
What is the SI unit of momentum ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The SI unit of momentum is kilogram meters per second(kg.m/s)</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 4:</strong></span><br />
State whether momentum is scalar or vector.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Momentum is a vector quantity and is dirceted along the direction of velocity.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 5:</strong></span><br />
What is the total momentum of the bullet and the gun before firing ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The total momentum of the bullet and the gun before firing would be zero because velocities of both of them will be zero.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 6:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity whose unit is kg.m/s.<br />
<span style="color:purple ;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Momentum has its SI unit as kilogram meters per second(kg.m/s)</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 7:</strong></span><br />
What will be the momentum of a body of mass &8216;m&8217; which is moving with a velocity V ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Momentum of a body of mass &8216;m&8217; and velocity &8216;v&8217; will be<br />
p = m x v</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 8:</strong></span><br />
What is the usual name of the forces which cannot produce motion in a body but only change its shape ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Balanced forces cannot produce motion in a body but can its shape.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 9:</strong></span><br />
Name the unbalanced force which slows down a moving bicycle when we stop pedalling it.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Frictional force slows down a moving bicycle when we stop pedaling it.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 10:</strong></span><br />
State whether the following statement is true or false :<br />
Unbalanced forces acting on a body change its shape.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The given statement is false.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 11:</strong></span><br />
When a ball is dropped from a height, its speed increases gradually. Name the force which causes this change in speed.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Force of gravity causes this change in speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 12:</strong></span><br />
Name the property of bodies (or objects) to resist a change in their state of rest or of motion.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Inertia is the property of bodies to resist a change in their state of rest or motion</p>
<p><span style="color: purple ;"><strong>Question 13:</strong></span><br />
What is the other name of Newton&8217;s first law of motion ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Newton&8217;s first law of motion is also known as Galileo&8217;s law of inertia.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 14:</strong></span><br />
The mass of object A is 6 kg whereas that of another object B is 34 kg. Which of the two objects, A or B, has more inertia ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Object B has more inertia. Since mass is a measure of inertia of a body and object B has greater mass, so it will have greater inertia.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 15:</strong></span><br />
Name the scientist who gave the laws of motion.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Isaac Newton gave the laws of motion.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 16:</strong></span><br />
State whether force is a scalar or a vector quantity.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Force is a vector quantity.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 17:</strong></span><br />
With which physical quantity should the speed of a running bull be multiplied so as to obtain its momentum ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The speed of the running bull should be multiplied with its mass to get its momentum.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 18:<br />
</strong></span>Fill in the following blanks with suitable words :<br />
(a) &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;is a measure of the inertia of a body.<br />
(b) When a running car stops suddenly, the passengers are jerked &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;..<br />
(c) When a stationary car starts suddenly, the passengers are jerked &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;..<br />
(d) Newton&8217;s first law of motion is also called Galileo&8217;s law of &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;<br />
(e) If there were no unbalanced force of&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;.. and no&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;. resistance, a moving bicycle would go on moving for ever.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) Mass<br />
b) forward<br />
c) backward<br />
d) inertia<br />
e) friction; air</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 19:</strong></span><br />
Explain why, it is easier to stop a tennis ball than a cricket ball moving with the same speed.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Since the speed of tennis ball and cricket ball is same, the momentum of cricket ball will be higher due to its mass being greater than mass of tennis ball. So, less force is requipurple to stop a tennis ball than to stop a cricket ball.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 20:</strong></span><br />
Explain the meaning of the following equation : .<br />
p = m x v<br />
where symbols have their usual meanings.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
p = m x v<br />
This equation signifies that momentum of a body is the product of its mass and its velocity.<br />
Here, p is momentum of the body<br />
m is the mass of the body<br />
v is the velocity of the body.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 21:</strong></span><br />
Explain how, a karate player can break a pile of tiles with a single blow of his hand.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
A karate player can break a pile of tiles with a single blow because he strikes the pile with his hand very fast. In doing so, the large momentum of his hand is purpleuced to zero in a very short time. This exerts a large force on the pile of tiles which is sufficient to break them apart.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 22:</strong></span><br />
Calculate the momentum of a toy car of mass 200 g moving with a speed of 5 m/s.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the toy car,<br />
m = 200 g = 0.2 kg<br />
Speed, v = 5 m/s<br />
Momentum, p = m x v<br />
= 0.2 x 5 = 1 kg.m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 23:</strong></span><br />
What is the change in momentum of a car weighing 1500 kg when its speed increases from 36 km/h to 72 km/h uniformly ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of car = 1500 kg<br />
Velocity v<sub>1</sub> = 36 km/hr = 10 m/s<br />
Momentum p<sub>1</sub> = 1500 x 10 = 15000 kg.m/s<br />
Velocity v<sub>2</sub> = 72 km/hr = 20 m/s<br />
Momentum p<sub>2</sub> = 1500 x 20 = 30000 kg.m/s<br />
Change in momentum = p<sub>2</sub>-p<sub>1</sub>= 30000 &8211; 15000 = 15000 kg.m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 24:</strong></span><br />
A body of mass 25 kg has a momentum of 125 kg.m/s. Calculate the velocity of the body.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the body, m = 25 kg<br />
Momentum p = 125 kg.m/s<br />
p = m x v<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7650/16739662517_eec391c280_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-Q24" width="193" height="111" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 25:<br />
</strong></span> Calculate the momentum of the following :<br />
(a) an elephant of mass 2000 kg moving at 5 m/s<br />
(b) a bullet of mass 0.02 kg moving at 400 m/s<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4329/36193102966_fda5d9fa72_o.jpg" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-force-and-laws-of-motion-1" width="727" height="214" /><br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) Mass of elephant = 2000kg<br />
Velocity = 5 m/s<br />
Momentum = 2000 x 5 = 10000 kg.m/s<br />
b) Mass of bullet = 0.02 kg<br />
Velocity = 400 m/s<br />
Momentum = 0.02 x 400 = 8 kg.m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:56</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 26:</strong></span><br />
Which of the two, balanced forces or unbalanced forces, can change the shape of an object ? Give an example to illustrate your solution.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Balanced forces can change the shape of the object. For example, when a balloon is pressed between hands, then balanced forces (equal and opposite forces) act on the balloon due to which the shape of the balloon changes.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 27:</strong></span><br />
Describe the term &8216;inertia&8217; with respect to motion.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Inertia of motion is the property of a body due to which it resists a change in its state of uniform motion. For eg., if there is no air resistance and no friction to oppose the motion of a moving bicycle, it will go on moving forever.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 28:</strong></span><br />
State Newton&8217;s first law of motion. Give two examples to illustrate Newton&8217;s first law of motion.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Newton&8217;s first law of motion states that a body at rest will remain at rest, and a body in motion will continue in motion in a straight line with a uniform speed unless it is compelled by an external force to change its state of rest or of uniform motion. For example, a book lying on a table remains on the table unless we lift it with the force of our hands. And, on a frictionless surface, a moving car continues to be in the state of motion until brakes are applied on it.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 29:</strong></span><br />
On what factor does the inertia of a body depend ? Which has more inertia, a cricket ball or a rubber ball of the same size ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Inertia of a body depends on its mass. A cricket ball has more inertia than a rubber ball of the same size because it has more mass than the rubber ball.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 30:</strong></span><br />
Why do the passengers in a bus tend to fall backward when it starts suddenly ?<br />
<span style="color:purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a bus starts suddenly, its passengers tend to fall backwards because due to their inertia, the passengers tend to remain in a state of rest even when the bus starts moving.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 31:</strong></span><br />
Explain why, a person travelling in a bus falls forward when the bus stops suddenly.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a bus stops suddenly, its passengers tend to fall forward because due to their inertia, the passengers tend to remain in a state of motion even though the bus has come to rest.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 32:</strong></span><br />
Give reason for the following :<br />
When a hanging carpet is beaten with a stick, the dust particles start coming out of it.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a hanging carpet is beaten with a stick, the carpet moves to and fro with the force of the stick while the dust particles remain in their state of rest on account of their inertia and thus dust particles separate out from the carpet.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 33:</strong></span><br />
When a tree is shaken, its fruits and leaves fall down: Why ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a tree is shaken, the tree moves to and fro while the fruits and leaves remain in their state of rest on account of their inertia and thus fruits and leaves separate from the tree and fall from the tree.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 34:</strong></span><br />
Explain why, it is dangerous to jump out of a moving bus.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
It is dangerous to jump out of a moving bus because the jumping man, who is moving with the high speed of the bus would tend to remain in state of motion due to inertia even on falling to the ground and get hurt due to resistance offepurple by the ground.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 35:</strong></span><br />
What is the momentum in kg.m/s of a 10 kg car travelling at (a) 5 m/s (b) 20 cm/s, and (c) 36 km/h ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of car, m = 10 kg<br />
Momentum = m x v<br />
a) Velocity, v = 5 m/s Momentum = 10 x 5 = 50 kg.m/s<br />
b) Velocity, v = 20 cm/s = 0.2 m/s Momentum = 10 x 0.2 = 2 kg.m/s<br />
c) Velocity, v = 36km/hr = 10 m/s Momentum = 10 x 10 = 100 kg.m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 36:</strong></span><br />
(a) Define momentum of a body. On what factors does the momentum of a body depend ?<br />
(b) Calculate the change in momentum of a body weighing 5 kg when its velocity decreases from 20 m/s to 0.20 m/s.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) Momentum is the physical quantity which is the measure of the quantity of motion of a moving body. It depends on mass and velocity of the body.<br />
b) Mass of body = 5 kg<br />
Velocity v<sub>1</sub> = 20 m/s<br />
Momentum p<sub>1</sub> = 20 x 5 = 100 kg.m/s<br />
Velocity v<sub>2</sub> = 0.2 m/s<br />
Momentum p<sub>2</sub> = 5 x 0.2 = 1 kg.m/s<br />
Change in momentum = p<sub>2</sub>&8211; p<sub>1</sub>= 1-100 = -99 kg.m/s (Negative sign shows that momentum decreases)</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 37:</strong></span><br />
(a) Define the term &8216;force&8217;.<br />
(b) State the various effects of force.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) Force is an influence which tends to set a stationary body in motion or stop a moving body; or which tends to change the speed and direction of a moving body; or which tends to change the shape and size of a body.<br />
b) Various effects of force are<br />
i) A force can move a stationary body.<br />
ii) A force can stop a moving body.<br />
iii) A force can change the speed of a moving body.<br />
iv) A force can change the direction of a moving body.<br />
v) A force can change the shape and size of a body.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 38:</strong></span><br />
Give one example each where :<br />
(a) a force moves a stationary body.<br />
(b) a force stops a moving body.<br />
(c) a force changes the speed of a moving body.<br />
(d) a force changes the direction of a moving body.<br />
(e) a force changes the shape (and size) of a body.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) Kicking a stationary football.<br />
b) Applying brakes to a moving bicycle.<br />
c) Pressing an accelerator to speed up a moving car.<br />
d) A moving cricket ball hit by a bat.<br />
e) Flattening of dough by a rolling pin to make chapatis.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 39:</strong></span><br />
(a) What do you understand by the terms &8220;balanced forces&8221; and &8220;unbalanced forces&8221; ? Explain with examples.<br />
(b) What type of forces &8211; balanced or unbalanced &8211; act on a rubber ball when we press it between our hands ? What effect is produced in the ball ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) If the resultant of all the forces acting on a body is zero, the forces are called balanced forces. These forces do not change the state of rest or of uniform motion of a body but can change the shape of the body. For example, when a balloon is pressed between hands, then balanced forces (equal and opposite forces) act on the balloon due to which the shape of the balloon changes.<br />
If the resultant of all the forces acting on a body is not zero, the forces are called unbalanced forces. These forces change the state of rest or of uniform motion of a body. For eg., if we push a toy car lying on the ground, it starts moving due to the unbalanced force exerted by our hands.<br />
b) When we press a rubber ball between our hands, balanced forces acts on it and hence its shape changes.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 40:</strong></span><br />
(a) What happens to the passengers travelling in a bus when the bus takes a sharp turn ? Give reasons for<br />
your solution.<br />
(b) Why are road accidents at high speeds very much worse than road accidents at low speeds ?<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4320/35400371334_0bc6db2904_o.jpg" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-force-and-laws-of-motion-2" width="844" height="304" /><br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) When a bus takes a sharp turn, the passengers tend to fall sideways because of their inertia or their tendency to continue moving in a straight line.<br />
b) Road accidents at high speeds are much worse than road accidents at low speeds because the momentum of vehicles at high speeds is very high and causes a lot of damage to the vehicles and injuries to the passengers during collision.</p>
<p><span style="color: 0000ff;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:57</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 51:<br />
</strong></span>A plastic ball and a clay ball of equal masses, travelling in the same direction with equal speeds, strike against a vertical wall. From which ball does the wall receive a greater amount of momentum ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The wall will receive equal momentum from both the balls because both balls have equal mass and velocity.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 52:<br />
</strong></span>A moving bicycle comes to rest after sometime if we stop pedalling it. But Newton&8217;s first law of motion says that a moving body should continue to move for ever, unless some external force acts on it. How do you explain the bicycle case ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
In this case, the bicycle has been compelled to change its state of motion by the external force of air resistance and friction. If there were no air resistance and no friction to oppose the motion of the bicycle, then according to the first law of motion, the bicycle would go on moving forever.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 53:<br />
</strong></span>A man throws a ball weighing 500 g vertically upwards with a speed of 10 m/s.</p>
<ol>
<li>What will be its initial momentum ?</li>
<li>What would be its momentum at the highest point of its flight ?</li>
</ol>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of ball = 500 g = 0.5 kg<br />
Initial velocity = 10 m/s</p>
<ol>
<li>Initial momentum = 0.5 x 10 = 5 kg.m/s</li>
<li>Velocity at the highest point = 0 m/s</li>
</ol>
<p>Momentum at the highest point = 0.5 x 0 = 0 kg.m/s</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 54:<br />
</strong></span>A car is moving on a level road. If the driver turns off the engine of the car, the car&8217;s speed decreases gradually and ultimately it comes to a stop. A student says that two forces act on the car which bring it to a stop. What could these forces be ? Which of these two forces contributes more to slow down and stop the car ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The two forces acting on the car are force of friction and air resistance. Force of friction contributes more to slow down and stop the car.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 55:<br />
</strong></span>There are two types of forces X and Y. The forces belonging to type X can produce motion in a stationary object but cannot change the shape of the object. On the other hand, forces belonging to type Y cannot produce motion in a stationary object but can change the shape of the object. What is the general name of the forces such as (a) X, and (b) Y ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) X are unbalanced force.<br />
b) Y are balanced forces.</p>
<p><span style="color: 0000ff;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:74</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 1:</strong></span><br />
Which physical quantity corresponds to the rate of change of momentum ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><strong><span style="color: purple;"><br />
</span></strong>Force corresponds to the rate of change of momentum.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 2:</strong></span><br />
State the relation between the momentum of a body and the force acting on it.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><strong><span style="color: purple;"><br />
</span></strong>The rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction in which the force acts.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 3:</strong></span><br />
What is tire unit of force ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The SI unit of force is newton(N)</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 4:</strong></span><br />
Define one newton force.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
A newton force is defined as that force which when acting on a body of mass of 1 kg produces an acceleration of 1m/s<sup>2</sup> in it.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 5:</strong></span><br />
What is the relationship between force and acceleration ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Force acting on a body is directly proportional to the acceleration produced in the body.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8750/16760797279_f2171a51bb_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q5" width="496" height="48" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 6:</strong></span><br />
If the mass of a body and the force acting on it are both doubled, what happens to the acceleration ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8735/16739663197_c967458b2d_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q6" width="343" height="111" /><br />
Acceleration remains same since<br />
Now if force is doubled i.e. 2F and mass is doubled i.e. 2m<br />
Then acceleration</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 7:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity whose unit is &8216;newton&8217;.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Newton is the SI unit of force.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 8:</strong></span><br />
Which physical principle is involved in the working of a jet aeroplane ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Jet airplanes work on the principle of conservation of momentum.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 9:</strong></span><br />
Name the principle on which a rocket works.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Rockets work on the principle of conservation of momentum.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 10:</strong></span><br />
Is the following statement true or false :<br />
A rocket can propel itself in a vacuum.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
True, because rocket does not require air for obtaining uplift or for burning its fuel.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 11:</strong></span><br />
What is the force which produces an acceleration of 1 m /s<sup>2 </sup> in a body of mass 1 kg ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass, m = 1 kg<br />
Acceleration, a =<br />
1m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Force F = m x a = 1<br />
x 1= 1N</p>

Find the acceleration produced by a force of 5 N acting on a mass of 10 kg.<br />

Force F =5 N<br />
Mass m = 10 kg<br />

<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 13:</strong></span><br />
A girl weighing 25 kg stands on the tloor. She exerts a downward force of 250 N on the floor. What force does the floor exert on her ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The force exerted by the floor on her = the downward force exerted by the girl =250 N<br />
This is due to Newton&8217;s third law of motion which states that to every action there is an equal and opposite reaction.<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8732/16759561640_edcfbf064c_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q14" width="123" height="49" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 14:</strong></span><br />
Name the physical quantity which makes it easier to accelerate a small car than a large car.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Less mass of the small car makes it easier to accelerate a small car than a large car because acceleration is inversely<br />
proportional to mass of the car</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 15:<br />
</strong></span>Fill in the following blanks with suitable words :<br />
(a) To every action, there is an&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;.. and&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230; reaction<br />
(b)  Momentum is a&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;.. Its emit is&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;<br />
(c)  Newton&8217;s second law of motion can be written as Force = mass x &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230; or Force = &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;.. of change of&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;.<br />
(d)  Forces in a Newton&8217;s third law pair have equal&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230; but act in opposite&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;..<br />
(e)  In collisions and explosions, the total &8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230; remains constant, provided that no external&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;&8230;..<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) Equal; opposite<br />
b) Vector; kg.m/s<br />
c) Acceleration; rate; momentum<br />
d) Magnitude; directions<br />
e) Momentum; force</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 16:<br />
</strong></span>Explain the meaning of the following equation :<br />
F = m x a<br />
where symbols have their usual meanings<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Force is directly proportional to the product of &8216;mass&8217; of the body and the &8216;acceleration&8217; produced in the body by the action of force.<br />
F = m x a<br />
where F is the force applied on the body<br />
m is the mass of the body<br />
a is the acceleration produced in the body</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 17:<br />
</strong></span>To take the boat away from the bank of a river, the boatman pushes the bank with an oar. Why ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
To take boat away from the bank of a river, the boatman pushes the bank with the oar. The bank exerts an equal and opposite force on the boat which makes the boat move forward away from the bank.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 18:<br />
</strong></span>Why does a gunman get a jerk on firing a bullet ?<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4300/35429633653_519ffb4022_o.jpg" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-force-and-laws-of-motion-3" width="333" height="213" /><br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Gunman gets a jerk on firing a bullet because when a bullet is fipurple from a gun, the force sending the bullet forward is equal to the force sending the gun backwards but due to high mass of the gun, it moves only a little distance backwards giving a jerk to the gunman.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 19:<br />
</strong></span>If action is always equal to reaction, explain why a cart pulled by a horse can be moved.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
To make the cart move, the horse bends forward and pushes the ground with its feet. When the forward reaction to the backward push of the horse on the ground is greater than the opposing frictional forces of the wheels, the cart moves.</p>
<p><span style="color: 0000ff;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:75</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 20:<br />
</strong></span>Explain how a rocket works<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
A rockets works on the principle of action and reaction. In a rocket, the hot gases produced by the rapid burning of fuel rush out of a jet at the bottom of the rocket at a very high speed. The equal and opposite reaction force of the downward going gases pushes the rocket upward with a great speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 21<br />
</strong></span>Do action and reaction act on the same body or different bodies <span style="font-size: 13.3333px;">?</span> How are they related in magnitude and direction ? Are they simultaneous or not ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Action and reaction act on two different bodies. Action and reaction are equal in magnitude but they act in opposite directions and there is simultaneous action and reaction.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 22<br />
</strong></span>If a man jumps out from a boat, the boat moves backwards. Why ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
When a man jumps out from a boat, the boat moves backwards due to the fact that to step out of the boat, the man presses the boat with his foot in the backward direction. The push of the man on the boat is action. The boat exerts an equal force on the man in the forward direction and since the boat is not fixed and is floating, it moves backwards due to the action force exerted by the man.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 23<br />
</strong></span>Why is it difficult to walk on a slippery road ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
It becomes very difficult to walk on a slippery road because of the fact that on a slippery road, the friction is much less, and we cannot exert a backward action force on slippery ground which would produce a forward reaction force on us.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 24:<br />
</strong></span>Explain why, a runner presses the ground with his feet before he starts his run.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
To start his run, a runner bends forward and pushes the ground with his feet in the backward direction. In turn ground exerts a reaction force on the runner in the forward direction which makes him run.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 25:<br />
</strong></span>A 60 g bullet fipurple from a 5 kg gun leaves with a speed of 500 m/s. Find the speed (velocity) with which the gun recoils (jerks backwards).<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of bullet, m<sub>1</sub> = 60g = 0.06 kg<br />
Velocity of bullet v<sub>1</sub> = 500 m/s<br />
Mass of gun m<sub>2</sub> = 5 kg<br />
Recoil velocity v<sub>2</sub><br />
According to the law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub> x v<sub>1</sub> = m<sub>2</sub> x v<sub>2</sub><br />
0.06 x 500 = 5 x v<sub>2</sub><br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7612/16947018635_78a7df2db0_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q25" width="319" height="168" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 26:<br />
</strong></span>A 10 g bullet travelling at 200 m/s strikes and remains embedded in a 2 kg target which is originally at rest but free to move. At what speed does the target move off ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of bullet, m<sub>1</sub> = 10g = 0.01 kg<br />
Velocity of bullet v<sub>1</sub> = 200 m/s<br />
Mass of block with the bullet as bullet gets embedded in it, m<sub>2</sub> = 2+0.01 = 2.01 kg<br />
Recoil velocity v<sub>2</sub><br />
According to the law of conservation of momentum m<sub>1</sub> x v<sub>1</sub> = m<sub>2</sub> x v<sub>2</sub><br />
0.01 x 200 = 2.01 x v<sub>2</sub><br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7602/16759561630_551bfcab6f_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q26" width="464" height="171" /></p>

<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 32:</strong></span><br />
The velocity of a body of mass 10 kg increases from 4 m/s to 8 m/s when a force acts on it for 2 s.<br />
(a) What is the momentum before the force acts ?<br />
(b) What is the momentum after the force acts ?<br />
(c) What is the gain in momentum per second ?<br />
(d) What is the value of the force ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the body = 10 kg<br />
Initial velocity u = 4 m/s<br />
Final velocity v = 8 m/s<br />
Time t = 2 s<br />
a) Momentum before force acts p<sub>1</sub>= m x u = 10 x 4 = 40 kg.m/s<br />
b) Momentum after force acts p<sub>2</sub> = m x v = 10 x 8 = 80 kg.m/s<br />
c) Gain in momentum for 2 s = p<sub>2</sub>-p<sub>1</sub> =40 kg.m/s<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7606/16921066026_cda788c36d_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q32" width="378" height="207" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 33:</strong></span><br />
A gun of mass 3 kg fires a bullet of mass 30 g. The bullet takes 0.003 s to move through the barrel of the gun and acquires a velocity of 100 m/s. Calculate :<br />
(i) the velocity with which the gun recoils.<br />
(ii) the force exerted on gunman due to recoil of the gun<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the gun m<sub>1</sub> = 3 kg<br />
Mass of bullet m<sub>2</sub> = 30 g = 0.03 kg<br />
Velocity of bullet v<sub>2</sub> =100 m/s<br />
i) According to the law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub> x v<sub>1</sub> = m<sub>2</sub> x v<sub>2</sub><br />
3 x v<sub>1</sub>= 0.03 x 100<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8750/16947018385_e51ce93922_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q33" width="332" height="258" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 34:</strong></span><br />
Draw a diagram to show how a rocket engine provides a force to move the rocket upwards. Label the diagram appropriately.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
