<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 35:</strong></span><br />
Name the laws involved in the following situations :<br />
(a) the sum of products of masses and velocities of two moving bodies before and after their collision remains the same.<br />
(b) a body of mass 5 kg can be accelerated more easily by a force than another body of mass 50 kg under similar conditions<br />
(c) when person A standing on roller skates pushes another person B (also standing on roller skates) and makes him move to the right side, then the person A himself gets moved to the left side by an equal distance.<br />
(d) if there were no friction and no air resistance, then a moving bicycle would go on moving for ever.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a)Law of conservation of momentum<br />
b)Newton&8217;s second law of motion<br />
c) Newton&8217;s third law of motion<br />
d)Newton&8217;s first law of motion</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 36:</strong></span><br />
(a) State and explain Newton&8217;s second law of motion.<br />
(b) A 1000 kg vehicle moving with a speed of 20 m/s is brought to rest in a distance of 50 metres :<br />
(i) Find the acceleration.<br />
(ii) Calculate the unbalanced force acting on the vehicle.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
(a) According to Newton&8217;s second law of motion: The rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force, and takes place in the direction in which the force acts.<br />
Consider a body of mass m having initial velocity u. the initial momentum of this body will be mu. Suppose a force F acts on this body for time t causing the final velocity to be v. The final momentum of the body will be mv. Now the change in momentum is mv � mu and the time taken for this change is t. So according to Newton&8217;s second law of motion,<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7603/16759316288_2e793b8d81_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q36" width="813" height="439" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 37:</strong></span><br />
(a) Explain why, a cricket player moves his hands backwards while catching a fast cricket ball.<br />
(b) A 150 g ball, travelling at 30 m/s, strikes the palm of a player&8217;s hand and is stopped in 0.05 second. Find the force exerted by the ball on the hand.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) A player moves his hands backwards while catching a fast ball because a fast moving ball has a large momentum and in stopping this ball, its momentum has<br />
to be purpleuced to zero. Now, when a cricket player moves back his hands on catching the fast ball, then the time taken to purpleuce the momentum of the ball is increased. So, the rate of change of momentum of ball is decreased and hence a small force is exerted on the hands of the player and the hands of the player do not get hurt.<br />
b)Mass of ball = 150 g = 0.15 kg<br />
Initial velocity u = 30 m/s<br />
Final velocity v = 0 m/s<br />
Time t = 0.05 s<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8718/16945695322_24ba6e7e42_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q37" width="812" height="183" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 38:</strong></span><br />
(a) State Newton&8217;s third law of motion and give two examples to illustrate the law.<br />
(b) Explain why, when a fireman directs a powerful stream of water on a fire from a hose pipe, the hose pipe tends to go backward.<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4325/36194082596_e1065383ba_o.jpg" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-force-and-laws-of-motion-4" width="360" height="285" /><br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) According to Newton&8217;s third law of motion: Whenever one body exerts a force on another body, the second body exerts an equal and opposite force on the first body. In other words, to every action, there is an equal and opposite reaction. Two examples to illustrate this law-<br />
When a man jumps out from a boat, the boat moves backwards. This is due to the fact that to step out of the boat, the man presses the boat with his foot in the backward direction. The push of the man on the boat is action. The boat exerts an equal force in the forward direction and since the boat is not fixed and is floating, it moves backwards due to the action force exerted by the man.<br />
Gunman gets a jerk on firing a bullet from his gun. This is because when a bullet is fipurple from a gun, the force sending the bullet forward is equal to the force sending the gun backwards but due to high mass of the gun, it moves only a little distance backwards giving a jerk to the gunman.<br />
b) When a fireman directs a powerful stream of water on a fire, the hose pipe tends to go backward due to the reaction force of the water rushing through it in the forward direction at a great speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: 0000ff;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:76</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 39:</strong></span><br />
(a) State the law of conservation of momentum.<br />
(b) Discuss the conservation of momentum in each of the following cases :<br />
(i) a rocket taking off from ground.<br />
(ii) flying of a jet aeroplane.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) According to the law of conservation of momentum: When two (or more) bodies act upon one another, their total momentum remains constant (or conserved) provided no external forces are acting. It means that when one body gains momentum, then some other body loses an equal amount of momentum i.e. momentum is neither created nor destroyed.<br />
b)<br />
a. Rocket taking off from the ground The chemicals inside the rocket burn and produce very high velocity blast of hot gases. These gases pass out through the tail nozzle of the rocket in the downward direction with tremendous speed and the rocket moves up to balance the momentum of the gases. The gases have a very high velocity ang hence a very large momentum. An equal momentum is imparted to the rocket in the opposite direction, so that it goes up with a high velocity.<br />
b. Flying of jet aeroplane<br />
In jet aeroplanes, a large volume of gases produced by the combustion of fuel is allowed to escape through a jet in backward direction. Due to high velocity, the backward rushing gases have a large momentum. They impart an equal and opposite momentum to the jet aeroplane due to which it moves forward with a great speed.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 40:</strong></span><br />
(a) If a balloon filled with air and its mouth untied/ is released with its mouth in the downward direction, it<br />
moves upwards. Why ?<br />
(b) An unloaded truck weighing 2000 kg has a maximum acceleration of 0.5 m/s<sup>2</sup>. What is the maximum acceleration when it is carrying a load of 2000 kg ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
a) If of a balloon filled with compressed air and its mouth untied is released with its mouth in the downward direction, the balloon moves in the upward direction because the air present in the balloon rushes out in the downward direction. The equal and opposite reaction of downward going air pushes the balloon upwards.<br />
b) Mass of the unloaded truck, m<sub>1</sub>= 2000 kg<br />
Acceleration a<sub>1</sub> = 0.5 m/s<sup>2</sup><br />
Mass of loaded truck, m<sub>2</sub> = 2000+ 2000 = 4000 kg<br />
Acceleration a<sub>2</sub><br />
m<sub>1</sub> x a<sub>1</sub> = m<sub>2</sub> x a<sub>2</sub><br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8688/16921065836_d0c693c121_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q40" width="302" height="134" /></p>
<p><span style="color: 0000ff;"><strong>Lakhmir Singh Physics Class 9 solutions </strong><strong>Page No:77</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 51:</strong></span><br />
Why are car seat-belts designed to stretch some what in a collision ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Car seat-belts are somewhat stretchable so as to increase the time taken by the passengers to fall forward. Due to this, the rate of change of momentum of passengers is purpleuced and hence less stopping force acts on them. So the passengers do not get hurt.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 52:</strong></span><br />
The troops (soldiers) equipped to be dropped by parachutes from an aircraft are called paratroopers. Why do paratroopers roll on landing ?<br />
<img src="https://farm5.staticflickr.com/4298/35430038623_68445f0dae_o.jpg" alt="lakhmir-singh-physics-class-9-solutions-force-and-laws-of-motion-5" width="401" height="278" /><br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
The paratroopers roll on landing to increase the time taken to purpleuce the momentum of their body. Thus, the rate of change of momentum is purpleuced and hence less force is exerted on their legs and they do not get hurt.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 53:</strong></span><br />
Why would an aircraft be unable to fly on the moon ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
An aircraft needs air because air moving under the wings of aircraft is strong enough to hold it up and air is also requipurple to burn the fuel in aircraft engines. Since there is no air on moon, an aircraft cannot fly on moon.</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 54:</strong></span><br />
Explain why it is possible for a small animal to fall from a considerable height without any injury being caused when it reaches the ground.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
It is possible for a small animal to fall from a considerable height without being injupurple because a small animal has small mass, so the momentum produced is less. When the small animal falls to the ground with less momentum, less opposing force of ground acts on it and hence no injury is caused to it</p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 55:</strong></span><br />
A boy of mass 50 kg running at 5 m/s jumps on to a 20 kg trolley travelling in the same direction at 1.5 m/s. What is their common velocity ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the boy, m<sub>1</sub>= 50 kg<br />
Speed of boy, u<sub>1</sub> = 5 m/s<br />
Mass of trolley m<sub>2</sub> = 20 kg<br />
Speed of trolley u<sub>2</sub> =1.5 m/s<br />
Combined mass of boy and trolley, m = 20+ 50 = 70 kg<br />
Combined velocity v<br />
Acc. to the law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub>u<sub>1</sub> + m<sub>2</sub>u<sub>2</sub> = mv<br />
50 x 5 + 20 x 1.5 = 70 x v<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7624/16945695202_0f80ecd139_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q55" width="319" height="189" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 56:</strong></span><br />
A girl of mass 50 kg jumps out of a rowing boat of mass 300 kg on to the bank, with a horizontal velocity of 3 m/s. With what velocity does the boat begin to move backwards ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the boat m<sub>b</sub> = 300 kg<br />
Velocity of boat v<sub>b</sub><br />
Mass of girl m<sub>g</sub> = 50 kg<br />
Velocity of girl v<sub>g</sub> = 3 m/s<br />
Acc. to the law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>b</sub>v<sub>b</sub>=m<sub>g</sub>v<sub>g</sub><br />
300 x v<sub>b</sub> = 50 x 3<br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8693/16760796709_673e70a19f_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q56" width="281" height="165" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 57:</strong></span><br />
A truck of mass 500 kg moving at 4 m/s collides with another truck of mass 1500 kg moving in the same direction at 2 m/s. What is their common velocity just after the collision if they move off together ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of first truck, m<sub>1</sub>= 500 kg<br />
Speed of first truck, u<sub>1</sub> = 4 m/s<br />
Mass of second truck, m<sub>2</sub> = 1500 kg<br />
Speed of second truck, u<sub>2</sub> =2 m/s<br />
Combined mass of both trucks, m = 1500 + 500 = 2000 kg<br />
Combined velocity v<br />
Acc. to the law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub>u<sub>1</sub> + m<sub>2</sub>u<sub>2</sub> = mv<br />
500 x 4 + 1500 x 2 = 2000 x v<br />
<img src="https://farm8.staticflickr.com/7605/16921065796_a9e3ab401c_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q57" width="350" height="191" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 58:</strong></span><br />
A ball X of mass 1 kg travelling at 2 m/s has a head-on collision with an identical ball Y at rest. X stops and Y moves off. Calculate the velocity of Y after the collision.<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the ball x, m<sub>1</sub>= 1 kg<br />
Speed of ball x, u<sub>1</sub> = 2 m/s<br />
Mass of ball y, m<sub>2</sub> = 1 kg<br />
Speed of ball y, u<sub>2</sub> =0 m/s (at rest)<br />
Velocity of ball x after collision, v<sub>1</sub> = 0 m/s<br />
Velocity of ball y after collision, v<sub>2</sub><br />
Acc. to the law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub>u<sub>1</sub> + m<sub>2</sub>u<sub>2</sub> = m<sub>1</sub>v<sub>1</sub> + m<sub>2</sub>v<sub>2</sub><br />
1 x 2 + 1 x 0 = 1 x 0 + 1 x v<sub>2</sub><br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8719/16739662627_0bc360633b_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q58" width="286" height="200" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 59:</strong></span><br />
A heavy car A of mass 2000 kg travelling at 10 m/s has a head-on collision with a sports car B of mass 500 kg. If both cars stop dead on colliding, what was the velocity of car B ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of car A, m<sub>1</sub>= 2000 kg<br />
Speed of car A, v<sub>1</sub> = 10 m/s<br />
Mass of car B, m<sub>2</sub> = 500 kg<br />
Speed of car B, v<sub>2</sub><br />
Acc to law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub>v<sub>1</sub> = m<sub>2</sub>v<sub>2</sub><br />
2000 x 10 = 500 x v<sub>2</sub><br />
<img src="https://farm9.staticflickr.com/8723/16759315958_b0321c6e7d_o.png" alt="lakhmir-singh-and-manjit-kaur-physics-class-9-solution-Chapter-2-Force-and-Laws-of-motion-A-Q59" width="291" height="166" /></p>
<p><span style="color: purple;"><strong>Question 60:</strong></span><br />
A man wearing a bullet-proof vest stands still on roller skates. The total mass is 80 kg. A bullet of mass 20 grams is fipurple at 400 m/s. It is stopped by the vest and falls to the ground. What is then the velocity of the man ?<br />
<span style="color: purple;"><strong>solution :</strong></span><br />
Mass of the man, m<sub>1</sub>= 80 kg<br />
Speed of man, v<sub>1</sub><br />
Mass of bullet m<sub>2</sub> = 20 g = 0.02 kg<br />
Speed of bullet v<sub>2 </sub>= 400 m/s<br />
Acc to law of conservation of momentum<br />
m<sub>1</sub>v<sub>1</sub> = m<sub>2</sub>v<sub>2</sub><br />
80 x v<sub>1</sub> = 0.02 x 400<br /></font>

<h2><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3 Tissues</span></strong></h2>
<p><strong><span style="color: #eb4924;">Text Book Solutions &#8211; P.S.Verma and V.K.Agarwal &#8211; Biology</span></strong></p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #00bdeb;">CBSE Class 9 Chapter 3 Tissues</span></strong></p>
<p><a class="button-blue" title="LearnCBSE Forum - Post and Discuss your Queries" href="http://ask.learncbse.in/"> Share Queries and Discuss your Views and Ideas &#8211; <strong>LearnCBSE Forum</strong></a></p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page No &#8211; 165.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 1:</span><br />
Importance of tissues-<br />
(i) Formations of tissues have brought about a division of labour in multicellular organisms.<br />
(ii) Tissues become organised to form organs and organs organise into organ system.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 2:</span><br />
Plants are autotrophic organisms, so prepare their own food by photosynthesis. Moreover plants are stationary or fixed organisms; they do not have to move from place to place in the search of their food. Since they do not consume or need much energy, so most of the plant tissues are supportive, which provide them with structural strength. Animals are heterotrophic organisms. They have to move in search of food, mate and find shelter, so they need more energy as compared to plants. Most of the tissues they contain are living.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 3:</span><br />
Plant Tissues<br />
1. They require less maintenance energy.<br />
2. There is a differentiation of meristematic and permanent tissues.<br />
Animal Tissues:<br />
1. They require more maintenance energy.<br />
2. Such a differentiation is absent in them.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 4:</span><br />
They are located at the base of leaves or internodes, e.g., stems of grasses and other monocots. Such tissues also occur below the nodes. It produces an increase in the length of an organ such as leaves and internodes.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 5:</span><br />
(i) Apical meristem &#8211; It brings about the elongation of the root and stem.<br />
(ii) Lateral meristem &#8211; It causes the organ (stem or root) to increase in diameter and girth.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 6:</span><br />
Simple permanent tissues &#8211; These tissues are composed of cells which are structurally and functionally similar.<br />
There are three types of simple permanent tissues:<br />
(i) Parenchyma &#8211; Parenchyma cells are living and posses the power of division. The cell wall is thin and encloses a dense cytoplasm which contains a small nucleus and surrounds a large central vacuole.<br />
(ii) Collenchyma &#8211; Its tissues consists of living cells. It is characterized by the deposition of extra cellulose at the corners of the cells. In collenchymas, intercellular spaces are generally absent. Collenchyma cells are elongated in shape. They often contain a few chloroplasts.<br />
(iii)Sclerenchyma &#8211; Sclerenchyma cells are dead cells and they are devoid of protoplasm. The cells walls of Sclerenchyma are greatly thickened of lignin. The cells of Sclerenchyma are closely packed without intercellular spaces.</p>
<p><strong>PS Verma and V.K. Agarwal Biology Class 9 Page No &#8211; 165.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 7:</span><br />
(a) Parenchyma<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-07-a.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
(b) Collenchyma<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-07-b.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 8:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-08.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 9:</span><br />
Xylem Tissue<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-09.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 10:</span><br />
Functions of Collenchyma:<br />
(i) It provides mechanical support and elasticity.<br />
(ii) It provides tensile strength to the plants.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 11:</span><br />
Sclerenchyma cells are dead cells and they are devoid of protoplasm. The cells walls of sclerenchyma are greatly thickened by lignin. The cells of sclerenchyma are closely packed without intercellular spaces.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 12:</span><br />
Xylem:<br />
1. It conducts water and minerals.<br />
2. Conducting channels or tracheary elements are tracheids and vessels.<br />
Phloem:<br />
1. It conducts organic solutes and food materials.<br />
2. Conducting channels are sieve tubes.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution 13:</span><br />
Tracheids:<br />
1. Single celled.<br />
2. The end walls remain intact.<br />
Vessels:<br />
1. Made up of a row of cells.<br />
2. End walls get dissolved and become perforated.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
The different types of elements present in the phloem are:<br />
(i) Sieve tubes &#8211; Sieve tubes are slender, tube-like structures composed of elongated thin-walled cells, placed end to end. Their end walls are perforated by numerous pores and are called sieve plates.<br />
(ii) Companion Cells &#8211; It is a small thin-walled cell containing dense and very active cytoplasm and large elongated nucleus.<br />
(iii) Phloem parenchyma &#8211; These are thin-walled, living cells of parenchyma of phloem. They have two functions, storage and slow lateral conduction of food.<br />
(iv) Phloem Fibre &#8211; These are thick-walled, elongated spindled shaped dead cells which posses narrow lumen. They provide mechanical strength to the tissue.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 2</span><br />
Tracheary elements are the elements of xylem. Their function is to carry water and mineral salts in upward direction from the roots to different part of shoots.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 3</span><br />
(i) Parenchyma Functions:<br />
(a) The main function of parenchyma is to store and assimilate food.<br />
(b) Transport of materials occurs through cells or cell walls of parenchyma cells.<br />
(ii) Collenchyma Functions:<br />
(a) It provides mechanical support and elasticity.<br />
(b) It provides tensile strength to the plants.<br />
(iii) Sclerenchyma Functions:<br />
(a) It is mainly mechanical and protective in function.<br />
(b) It gives strength, rigidity, flexibility and elasticity to the plant body.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 4</span><br />
Parenchyma:<br />
1. The tissue consists of thin-walled living cells.<br />
2. It is distributed in almost all the parts of the plant body.<br />
3. The living cells of parenchyma assimilate and store food. They also store waste products.<br />
Collenchyma:<br />
1. The tissue consists of cells having localised thickening in their cell walls.<br />
2. It occurs mostly in the aerial parts of the plants and is restricted to the other layers.<br />
3. Collenchyma is the chief mechanical tissue in parts of a young plant particularly in the young dicotyledonous stems.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 5:</span><br />
Collenchyma:<br />
1. It consists of living cells.<br />
2. Its cells contain cytoplasm.<br />
3. Its cell walls are cellulosic.<br />
Sclerenchyma:<br />
1. It consists of dead cells.<br />
2. Its cells are empty.<br />
3. Its cell walls are lignified.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 6</span><br />
Xylem is composed of cells of four different types: 1. Tracheids; 2. Vessels or tracheae; 3. Xylem parenchyma and 4. Xylem Sclerenchyma. Except xylem parenchyma, all other xylem elements are dead and bounded by thick lignified walls. Vessels are shorter and wider than tracheids. Vessels are very long tube-like structures formed by a row of cells placed end to end. Tracheids are elongated cells with tapering ends. They also conduct water.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 7</span><br />
Functions of Xylem:<br />
(i) The main function of xylem is to carry water and mineral salts upward from the root to different parts of shoots.<br />
(ii) Since walls of tracheids, vessels and sclerenchyma of xylem are lignified, they give mechanical strength to the plant body.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 8</span><br />
Functions of Phloem:<br />
Phloem transports photosynthetically prepared food materials from the leaves to the storage organs and later from storage organs to the growing regions of the plant body.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 9</span><br />
The different types of plant tissues are:<br />
1. Meristematic tissues &#8211; It is of three types: Apical, Lateral and Intercalary.<br />
2. Permanent Tissue &#8211; It of two types: Simple and Complex tissues. Simple tissues are of three types &#8211; Parenchyma, Collenchyma and Sclerenchyma.<br />
Complex tissues are of two types &#8211; Xylem and Phloem.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 10</span><br />
Sieve tube elements do not have nuclei but have cytoplasm. They are dependent on adjacent companion cells which contains dense and very active cytoplasm and a large elongated nucleus.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 11</span><br />
Functions of Epithelial tissues are:<br />
(i) The cells of the body surface form the outer layer of skin. These cells protect the underlying cells from drying, injury, and chemical effects.<br />
(ii) Inside the body, epithelial cells form lining of mouth and alimentary canal and protect these organs.<br />
(iii) Epithelial tissues help in absorption of water and nutrients in small intestine.<br />
(iv) Some epithelial tissues perform secretory function such as sweat, saliva in skin and mouth cavity.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 12</span><br />
(i) Striated Muscles &#8211; It occur in the muscles of limbs, body wall, face, neck, etc. Striated muscles present in tongue, pharynx, diaphragm and upper part of oesophagus are called visceral straited muscles.<br />
(ii) Smooth Muscles &#8211; Smooth muscles are found in the walls of the hollow (tubular) visceral organs except that of the heart. They occur in the wall of alimentary canal and internal organs, ducts of glands, urogenital ducts and blood vessels.<br />
(iii) Cardiac Muscles &#8211; The cardiac muscles occur in the heart.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 13:</span><br />
(a) Neuron &#8211; Nervous Tissue<br />
(b) Dendrite &#8211; Nervous Tissue<br />
(c) Cilia &#8211; Ciliated Epithelium<br />
(d) Collagen fibres &#8211; Connective Tissue<br />
(e) Elastin fibre &#8211; Connective Tissue<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 14</span><br />
(a) Osteoblast &#8211; It provides shape to the body.<br />
(b) Chondroblast &#8211; It provided support and flexibility to the body parts.<br />
(c) Goblet Cells &#8211; It is a mucus secreting epithelial cell which secrets mucus.<br />
(d) Neuron &#8211; The dendrites receive impulses and the axon takes impulses away from the cell body.<br />
(e) Muscle Cell &#8211; They undergo rapid contraction for locomotion.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 15</span><br />
Two characteristics of nerve cells are:<br />
(i) They are highly specialised unit cells.<br />
(ii) Neurons have the ability to receive stimuli from within or outside the body and to conduct (send) impulses (signals) to different parts of the body.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 16</span><br />
Bone &#8211; It provides skeletal support to the body.<br />
Cartilage &#8211; It provides support and flexibility to the body parts.<br />
Ligament &#8211; It connects bones to bones.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 17:</span><br />
(a) Adipose tissues.<br />
(b) Ciliated epithelium.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 18</span><br />
Functions:<br />
(i) It transports nutrients, hormones and vitamins to the tissues and transports excretory products from the tissues to the liver and kidney.<br />
(ii) The RBCs carry oxygen to the tissues for the oxidation of food stuff.<br />
(iii) WBCs fight disease by engulfing and destroying foreign bodies.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 19</span><br />
The different tissues in animals are:<br />
(i) Epithelial Tissues &#8211; These are the protective tissues of the animal body. Depending upon the shape and function of the cells, the epithelial tissues are classified as follows:<br />
a. Squamous epithelium.<br />
b. Cuboidal epithelium.<br />
c. Columnar epithelium.<br />
d. Glandular epithelium.<br />
e. Ciliated epithelium.<br />
(ii) Muscular Tissues &#8211; The muscular tissues form the contractile tissues and are made up of muscle cells. On the basis of their location, structure and function, there are three types of muscular tissues:<br />
a. Striated muscles.<br />
b. Smooth muscles.<br />
c. Cardiac muscles.<br />
(iii) Connective Tissues &#8211; The connective tissues are specialised to connect and anchor various body organs. They are of five types:<br />
a. Aerolar connective tissue.<br />
b. Dense regular connective tissue.<br />
c. Adipose tissues.<br />
d. Skeletal tissues.<br />
e. Fluid connective tissues.<br />
(iv) Nervous Tissues &#8211; These tissues are specialised to transmit messages within our body. Brain, spinal cord and nerves are all composed of nervous tissues.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 20:</span><br />

<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution SAQ &#8211; 21:</span><br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-21.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 1:</span><br />
Simple tissues &#8211; These tissues are composed of cells which are structurally and functionally similar.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-laq-01.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
There are three types of simple tissues:<br />
(i) Parenchyma &#8211; Parenchyma cells are living and posses the power of division. The cell wall is thin and encloses a dense cytoplasm which contains a small nucleus and surrounds a large central vacuole.<br />
(ii) Collenchyma &#8211; It tissues also consists of living cells. It is characterized by the deposition of extra cellulose at the corners of the cells. In collenchymas, intercellular spaces are generally absent. Collenchyma cells are elongated in shape. They often contain a few chloroplasts.<br />
(iii) Sclerenchyma &#8211; Sclerenchyma cells are dead cells and they are devoid of protoplasm. The cells walls of Sclerenchyma are greatly thickened by the deposition of lignin. The cells of sclerenchyma are closely packed without intercellular spaces.<br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 2:</span><br />
Meristematic tissues are the tissues in which the cells divide continuously and help in increasing the length and girth of the plant.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-laq-02-a.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
According to their position in the plant, meristems are of three types:<br />
a) Apical Meristems &#8211; These are situated at the growing tip of the stems and roots and increase the height of the plant.<br />
b) Lateral Meristems &#8211; These are found beneath the bark and in vascular bundles of dicot roots and stems. These are responsible for the growth of cambium and hence increases the girth of the plant.<br />
c) Intercalary Meristems &#8211; They are located at the base of leaves or internodes or below the nodes. It increases the length of the plant.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-laq-02-b.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
<span style="color: #eb4924;">Solution LAQ &#8211; 3:</span><br />
Simple tissues &#8211; These tissues are composed of cells which are structurally and functionally similar.<br />
There are three types of simple tissues:<br />
(i) Parenchyma &#8211; Parenchyma cells are living and posses the power of division. The cell wall is thin and encloses a dense cytoplasm which contains a small nucleus and surrounds a large central vacuole.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-laq-03-a.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
(ii) Collenchyma &#8211; It tissues also consists of living cells. It is characterized by the deposition of extra cellulose at the corners of the cells. In collenchymas, intercellular spaces are generally absent. Collenchyma cells are elongated in shape. They often contain a few chloroplasts.<br />
<img src="https://hcvermasolutions.files.wordpress.com/2016/08/p-s-verma-and-v-k-agarwal-solutions-for-biology-class-9-chapter-3-tissues-laq-03-b.png" alt="PS Verma Biology Class 9 Chapter 3" width="750" height="450" /><br />
(iii) Sclerenchyma &#8211; Sclerenchyma cells are dead cells and they are devoid of protoplasm. The cells walls of sclerenchyma are greatly thickened by the deposition of lignin. The cells of sclerenchyma are closely packed without intercellular spaces.<br />
